Conditional Wages Based on Time in Ijarah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional wages based on time of work in ijarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, and Zufar on conditional wages in ijarah and apply the distinction between ta'liq and taqit to determine the valid wage.

Core Idea
A single contract with two conditional wages on time is valid only for the first condition according to Abu Hanifa, requiring ujrat al-mithl for later work.

This passage presents a dispute among the Hanafi imams regarding a hire contract where the wage varies depending on whether the work is done today or tomorrow. The core issue is whether such a conditional wage is valid in ijarah, given the prohibition of uncertainty (gharar) and the principles of suspension (ta'liq) and specification (taqit). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyze how linguistic interpretations affect legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the conditions
The hirer says to the tailor: 'If you sew today, you get one dirham; if you sew tomorrow, you get half a dirham.' Recognize that this is an ijarah contract with two alternative wages based on time.
The work (tailoring) is the same; only the time differs.
2
State the positions of the Hanafi imams
Abu Hanifa: first condition (today) is valid, second (tomorrow) is invalid → if work tomorrow, ujrat al-mithl capped. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): both conditions valid → named wage due for each day. Zufar: both conditions invalid → full ujrat al-mithl.
The difference hinges on how 'today' and 'tomorrow' are interpreted.
3
Analyze the reasoning: ta'liq vs. taqit
Abu Hanifa argues that 'tomorrow' is for suspension (ta'liq), which corrupts the contract if combined with time. 'Today' cannot be for specification because that would combine time and work, also corrupting. Therefore only the first condition stands. Sahibayn argue that 'today' is for specification (taqit) and 'tomorrow' for suspension, so no conflict; both conditions are valid.
The linguistic analysis determines whether two namings coincide on any day.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, if work tomorrow, tailor gets ujrat al-mithl (capped at half dirham). Under Sahibayn, he gets the named half dirham. Under Zufar, he gets uncapped ujrat al-mithl.
The cap is based on the named wage in the invalid condition.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon position)
The text states that the narration from Abu Hanifa that ujrat al-mithl does not exceed half dirham is more correct, as chosen by Imam al-Karkhi. This is the operative position for fatwa.
Al-Jami' al-Saghir narrates a range (between half and one dirham), but the first narration is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
درزی سے کہا اگر آج سیئے تو ایک درہم اور کل سیئے تو نصف درہم آج سیما تو ایک درہم ملے گا اور اگر کل سیا تو اجرت مثل ملے گی۔ ولوقال ان خطته اليوم فبدرهم وان خطته غدا فبنصف درهم فان خاطه اليوم فله درهم وان خاطه غدا فله اجر مثله عند ابي حنيفة لايجاوز به نصف درهم وفى الجامع الصغير لا ينقص من نصف درهم ولا يزاد على درهم وقال ابويوسف ومحمد الشرطان جائزان وقال زفر الشرطان فاسدان لان الخياطة شيء واحد وقد ذكرنا بمقابلته بدلان على البدل فيكون مجهولا وهذا لان ذكر اليوم للتعجيل وذكر الغد للترفيه فيجتمع في كل يوم تسميتان . ولهما ان ذكر اليوم للتاقيت وذكر الغد للتعليق فلا يجتمع في كل يوم تسميتان ولان التعجيل والتاخير مقصودان فنزل منزلة اختلاف النوعين ولابي حنيفة ان ذكر الغد للتعليق حقيقة ولا يمكن حمل اليوم على التاقيت لان فيه فساد العقد لاجتماع الوقت والعمل واذا كان كذالك يجتمع في الغد تسميتان دون اليوم فيصح الاول ويجب المسمى ويفسد الثانى ويجب اجر المثل لا يجاوز به نصف درهم لانه هو المسمى فى الثانى وفى الجامع الصغير لا يزاد على درهم ولا ينقص من نصف درهم لان التسمية الأولى لا تنعدم فى اليوم الثانى فيعتبر لمنع الزيادة وتعتبر التسمية الثانية لمنع النقصان فان خاطه في اليوم الثالث لا يجاوز به نصف درهم عند ابي حنيفة هو الصحيح لانه اذا لم يرض بالتاخير الى الغد فبالزيادة عليه الى ما بعد الغد اولى۔ تشريح: مذکورہ بیان تو تر دید عمل کے ساتھ اجرت کا تھا۔ اگر اجرت کی تردید تر دید وقت کے ساتھ ہو تو یہ بھی صحیح ہے۔ جیسے مستاجر یوں کہے کہ اگر تو آج ہی دے تو ایک درہم ملے گا اور اگر کل پیئے گا تو نصف درہم ملے گا۔ اب اگر وہ آج ہی سی دے تو ایک ہی درہم ملے اور کل سیئے تو امام ابو ضیفہ کے نزدیک اجرت مثل ملے گی نہ کہ اجر سمی لیکن اجرت مثل نصف درہم سے زیادہ نہیں دی جائے گی یہ امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت ہے جو امام قدوری نے ذکر کی ہے۔ اور امام کرخی نے اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ نصف درہم سے کم اور ایک درہم سے زائد نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن پہلی روایت اصح ہے۔
If he said to the tailor: 'If you sew today, then for one dirham; if you sew tomorrow, then for half a dirham.' If he sewed it today, he gets one dirham; if he sewed it tomorrow, he gets the like wage (ujrat al-mithl) according to Abu Hanifa, not exceeding half a dirham. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is not less than half a dirham and not more than one dirham. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: both conditions are valid. Zufar said: both conditions are invalid, because tailoring is one thing, and we have mentioned two compensations for it on an alternative basis, so it is unknown. This is because mentioning 'today' is for acceleration and mentioning 'tomorrow' is for ease, so two namings come together on each day. For them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): mentioning 'today' is for specification (taqit) and mentioning 'tomorrow' is for suspension (ta'liq), so two namings do not come together on each day. Also, acceleration and delay are intended purposes, so it is treated like a difference of types. For Abu Hanifa: mentioning 'tomorrow' is truly for suspension, and it is not possible to interpret 'today' as specification because that would corrupt the contract due to the combination of time and work. If that is the case, then on tomorrow two namings come together, not on today. So the first condition is valid and the named wage is obligatory, and the second condition is invalid and the like wage is obligatory, not exceeding half a dirham, because that is the named wage in the second. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, it does not exceed one dirham and is not less than half a dirham, because the first naming is not absent on the second day; so it is considered to prevent increase, and the second naming is considered to prevent decrease. If he sewed on the third day, according to Abu Hanifa he does not exceed half a dirham—this is correct, because if he was not satisfied with delay until tomorrow, then all the more so with more delay. Explanation: The above statement was regarding the variation of wages with variation of work. If the variation of wages is with variation of time, this is also valid. For example, if the hirer says: 'If you give today, you get one dirham; if you give tomorrow, you get half a dirham.' If he gives today, he gets one dirham; if he sews tomorrow, according to Abu Hanifa he gets the like wage, not the named wage, but the like wage is not increased beyond half a dirham. This is a narration from Abu Hanifa mentioned by Imam al-Quduri. Imam al-Karkhi adopted it. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is not less than half a dirham and not more than one dirham. But the first narration is more correct.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on a conditional hire contract where the wage depends on when the work is done. The text presents the views of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Zufar. The core issue is whether the contract is valid given the alternative wages. Abu Hanifa considers the condition for tomorrow as a suspension (ta'liq), which is not accepted in ijarah, so only the first condition (today) is valid; if work is done tomorrow, ujrat al-mithl (like wage) applies, capped at half a dirham or limited between half and one dirham according to different narrations. The Sahibayn consider both conditions valid because 'today' specifies time and 'tomorrow' suspends, so no conflict. Zufar invalidates both because the work is one and two wages create uncertainty. The explanation clarifies that the same ruling applies if the wage variation is based on time rather than work. The commentary follows the author's order: first the ruling, then the proofs and responses. All examples are from Hanafi fiqh, specifically tailoring contracts.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of hire for services or usufruct, where the wage is known and the work is specified.
اجرت مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The market wage for similar work, determined by custom and prevailing rates, used when the named wage is invalid.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The naming of a wage in the contract; here it refers to the two different wage amounts mentioned for different days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 1 dirham
B) 0.5 dirham
C) Ujrat al-mithl not exceeding 0.5 dirham
D) The contract is void; no wage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes partial validity of conditional wages in ijarah, with the mufta bihi being Abu Hanifa's view that only the first condition binds and subsequent work requires capped ujrat al-mithl.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Alternative Wages in Ijarah: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Explains Hanafi dispute on conditional hire contracts with varying wages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on conditional ijarah contracts and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A conditional wage does not automatically void ijarah; Abu Hanifa views it as a valid choice between two contracts.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding ijarah (hire) contracts where the wage depends on a future condition. While the Sahibayn argue that such uncertainty invalidates the contract, Imam Abu Hanifa upholds its validity by treating it as a choice between two sound agreements. Understanding their reasoning sharpens your ability to distinguish between void and constructive contractual terms.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the scenario and the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa: the contract is valid and the named wage applies upon fulfillment of the condition; otherwise ujrat al-mithl is due.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa alone, not the school consensus.
2
Identify the opponent's view
State the Sahibayn's (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) position: the contract is void due to jahalah in both the subject matter and the wage.
They are joined by Zufar, Sufyan al-Thawri, and the three Imams.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Sahibayn's dalil: the manfa'ah is unknown at contract time, and the alternative wages create uncertainty. Unlike the Roman-Persian stitching case, here the wage is due upon takhliyah (handover), before work removes uncertainty.
They distinguish based on when the wage becomes obligatory.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa argues that mentioning 'tomorrow' is for ta'liq (suspension) and 'today' for tawqit (time-binding), so the two named wages do not combine on the same day. The contract gives a choice between two valid contracts, analogous to the stitching case.
He also caps the ujrat al-mithl at the lower named wage when the condition is unfulfilled.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa's ruling, such contracts are enforceable and the named wage applies when the condition is met. Under the Sahibayn, the contract is void and only ujrat al-mithl is due.
The commentary sides with Abu Hanifa as the stronger view.

Source Text

كتاب الاجارات
۹۲
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذکر غد در حقیقت برائے تعلیق ہے اور ذکر یوم کو تاقیت پر محمول کرنا ممکن ہیں کیونکہ اس میں وقت و عمل کے اجتماع کی وجہ سے عقد کا فساد ہے اور جب یہ بات ہے تو کل کے دن میں دو تسمیئے جمع ہوں گے نہ کہ آج کے دن میں پس پہلی شرط صحیح ہوگی اور اجر سمی واجب ہوگا۔ اور شرط ثانی فاسد ہوگی اور اجر مثل واجب ہوگا ۔ جو نصف درہم سے نہیں بڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ دوسرے دن کی مقررہ اجرت یہی ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ ایک درہم سے زائد اور نصف درہم سے کم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ پہلا تسمیہ دوسرے روز معدوم نہ ہوگا۔ پس پہلا تسمیہ زیادتی کو روکنے کے لئے اور دوسرا تسمیہ کی کو روکنے کے لئے معتبر ہوگا۔ پھر اگر درزی نے تیسرے دن سیاآ تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نصف درہم سے زیادہ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ یہی صحیح ہے اس لئے کہ مستاجر جب کل تک کی تاخیر پر راضی نہیں تھا تو اس سے زیادہ پرسوں تک کی تاخیر پر بدرجہ اولی راضی نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح قوله ان خطته اليوم ... الخ مذکورہ بیان تو تر دید عمل کے ساتھ اجرت کا تھا۔ اگر اجرت کی تردید تر دید وقت کے ساتھ ہو تو یہ بھی صحیح ہے۔ جیسے مستاجر یوں کہے کہ اگر تو آج ہی دے تو ایک درہم ملے گا اور اگر کل پیئے گا تو نصف درہم ملے گا۔
اب اگر وہ آج ہی سی دے تو ایک ہی درہم ملے اور کل سیئے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اجرت مثل ملے گی نہ کہ اجر سمی لیکن اجرت مثل نصف درہم سے زیادہ نہیں دی جائے گی یہ امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت ہے جو امام قدوری نے ذکر کی ہے۔ اور امام کرخی نے اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ نصف درہم سے کم اور ایک درہم سے زائد نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن پہلی روایت اصح ہے۔
قوله وقال ابو يوسف ... الخ - صاحبین کے نزدیک دونوں شرطیں جائز ہیں تو جس روز سیئے گا اس کی مسٹمی اجرت ملے گی۔ یعنی آج سیئے تو ایک درہم اور کل سیئے تو نصف درہم ، امام زفر ، ائمہ ثلاثہ سفیان ثوری احق کے نزدیک دونوں شرطیں فاسد ہیں ۔ کیونکہ خیاطت شی واحد ہے جس کے مقابلہ میں دو عوض بطریق بدلیت ذکر کئے گئے ہیں تو بدل مجہول ہوا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ ذکر یوم برائے تجھیل ہے اور ذکر غد برائے توسع تو ہر دن میں دو قسمیئے جمع ہو گئے ۔ یعنی جب کہ آج اور کل کا ذکر عجلت اور آسانی کے لئے ہوا تو گویا جو عقد کل کے لئے ہے وہ بھی آج ہی سے ثابت ہے۔ تو آج کے روز ایک تو آج کے عقد کا تسمیہ ایک درہم ہوا اور دوسرا کل کا تسمیہ نصف درہم ہوا اور یہی کل کا حال ہے۔ پس ہر روز دو قسمیئے جمع ہو گئے ۔ لہذا عقد فاسد ہے۔
قوله ولهما ان ذكر اليوم ... الخ - صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذکر یوم بغرض تعجیل برائے توقیت ہے (لا نہ حقیقت ) اور ذکر خد برائے تعلیق (یعنی برائے اضافت ہے۔ کیونکہ اجارہ تعلیق کو قبول نہیں کرتا ) پس ہر دن میں دور تسمیئے جمع نہ ہوئے ۔ نیز اس لئے بھی کہ تجھیل و تاخیر میں سے ہر ایک ایسا امر ہے جو بلحاظ اغراض مقصود ہوتا ہے تو یہ اختلاف غرض نوعی اختلاف کے درجہ میں ہو گیا یعنی گویا فارسی ورومی دو مختلف کی سلائی کے مانند ہے۔ لہذا عقد صحیح ہوگا۔
قوله ولابي حنيفة .... الخ - امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذکر غد حقیقی تعلیق کے لئے ہے اور ذکر یوم کوتو قیت پر محمول نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ ورنہ وقت اور عمل کے اجتماع کیوجہ سے عقد فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اگر وقت کا لحاظ کریں تو وہ اجیر خاص ہو جاتا ہے اور اگر کام کا لحاظ کریں تو وہ اجیر مشترک قرار پاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ ان دونوں میں منافات ہے ان کے لوازم میں تنافی ہونے کی وجہ سے اس لئے کہ ذکر عمل موجب عدم وجوب اجرت ہے۔ جب تک کہ وہ عمل نہ کرے اور ذکر وقت موجب وجوب اجرت ہے جب کہ وہ مدت میں خود کو پیش کر دے اور تنافی لوازم تنافی ملزومات پر دال ہوتی ہے۔ بہر کیف ذکر وقت سے معیاد مقصود نہیں ہے۔ اور جب یہ بات ہے تو دو سمیئے آج کے دن میں جمع نہ ہوئے بلکہ کل کے دن میں جمع ہوئے ۔ لہذا شرط اول صحیح ہوگی اور اجر سمی واجب ہوگا اور شرط ثانی فاسد ہوگی اور اجرت مثلی واجب ہوگی جو نصف درہم سے زیادہ دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ دوسرے دن کی مقررہ اجرت یہی نصف درہم ہے۔ قوله فان خاطه في اليوم الثالث .... الخ - پھر اگر درزی نے کپڑا تیسرے روز سیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نصف درہم سے زیادہ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ جب مستاجر کل تک کی تاخیر پر راضی نہیں تھا تو پرسوں تک کی تاخیر پر بدرجہ اولی راضی نہ ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک صحیح یہ ہے کہ نصف درہم سے کم کر دیا جائے۔
اگر اس دکان میں عطار کو ٹھہرائے تو ایک درہم ایک مہینے میں اگر لوہار کو ٹھہرائے تو دو در ہم اجارہ جائز ہے
ولو قال ان اسكنتَ فى هذا الدكان عطارا فبدرهم فى الشهر وان اسكنته حدادا فبدرهمین جاز وای الأمرين فعل استحق المسمى فيه عند ابي حنيفة وقالا الاجارة فاسدة وكذا اذا استاجر بيتا على انه ان سكن فيه فبدرهم وان اسكن فيه حدادا فبدرهمين فهو جائز عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لا يجوز ومن استاجر دابة الى الحيرة بدرهم وان جاوز بها الى القادسية فبدرهمين فهو جائز ويحتمل الخلاف وان استاجرها الى الحيرة على انه ان حمل عليها كر شعير فينصف درهم وان حمل عليها كر حنطة فبدرهم فهو جائز في قول ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا لا يجوز وجه قولهما ان المعقود عليه مجهول وكذا الاجر احد الشيائين وهو مجهول والجهالة توجب الفساد بخلاف الخياطة الرومية والفارسية لان الاجر يجب بالعمل وعنده ترتفع الجهالة اما في هذه المسائل يجب الاجر بالتخلية والتسليم فيبقى الجهالة وهذا الحرف هو الاصل عندهما ولابي حنيفة انه خيّره بين عقدين صحيحين مختلفين فيصح كما في مسألة الرومية والفارسية وهذا لان سكناه بنفسه يخالف اسكانه الحداد الاترى انه لايدخل ذالك فى مطلق العقد وكذا فى اخواتها والاجارة تعقد للانتفاع وعنده ترتفع الجهالة ولو احتيج الى الايجاب بمجرد التسليم يجب اقل الاجرين للتيقن به ترجمہ اگر کہا کہ اگر تو نے اس دکان میں عطار بٹھایا تو ایک درہم ماہواری ہے اور لوہار بٹھایا تو دو درہم ماہواری ہے تو یہ جائز ہے۔ ان میں سے جو کرے گا اس کی اجرت مسمی کا مستحق ہوگا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اجارہ فاسد ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کمرو بایں شرط کرایہ پر لیا کہ اگر خود رہا تو ایک درہم میں ہے اور لوہار کو رکھا تو دو درہم میں ہے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جائز نہیں۔ اگر جانور کرایہ پر لیا حیرہ تک ایک درہم میں اور اگر اس سے قادسیہ تک بڑھا تو دو درہم میں تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اور اختلاف کا احتمال ہے اگر جانور حیرہ تک بایں شرط کرایہ پر لیا کہ اگر اس پر ایک کر جو لا دے تو نصف درہم میں ہے۔ اور اگر ایک گر گیہوں لا دے تو ایک درہم میں ہے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول میں ۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جائز نہیں ۔ ان کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے۔ کہ معقود علیہ مجہول ہے۔ ایسے ہی اجرت دو چیزوں میں سے ایک ہے اور وہ مجہول ہے اور جہالت موجب فساد ہوتی ہے بخلاف، رومی و فارسی سلائی کے کیونکہ اجرت واجب ہو گی عمل سے اور عمل کے وقت جہالت اٹھ جائے گی۔ رہے یہ مسائل سوان میں اجرت تخلیہ اور تسلیم
Book of Ijarah... Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the mention of 'tomorrow' is for suspension and the mention of 'today' can be construed as time-bound... When the tailor sews on the third day, according to Abu Hanifa he will not be given more than half a dirham. This is correct because when the lessor was not satisfied with delay until tomorrow, he would be even less satisfied with delay until the day after tomorrow... The explanation of his statement 'if he sews it today...' The above discussion was about wage being dependent on act. If wage is dependent on time, it is also valid. For example, the lessee says: 'If you give today, you will get one dirham; if you give tomorrow, you will get half a dirham.'... Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say both conditions are valid, so whatever day he sews, he gets the named wage for that day. Imam Zufar, the three Imams, Sufyan al-Thawri, and others say both conditions are invalid because tailoring is one thing against which two compensations are mentioned alternatively, so the compensation is unknown... The proof of the two (Sahibayn) is that mentioning 'today' is for expediting and is time-bound, and mentioning 'tomorrow' is for suspension (since ijarah does not accept suspension), so two named wages do not combine in each day... And for Abu Hanifa, his proof is that mentioning 'tomorrow' is for real suspension and 'today' cannot be construed as time-bound, otherwise the contract would be void due to combination of time and work... If a person says: 'If you seat an attar in this shop, then one dirham per month; if you seat a blacksmith, then two dirhams,' it is valid, and whichever he does, he deserves the named wage according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Sahibayn) say the ijarah is void. Similarly, if he rents a house on condition that if he lives in it himself, then one dirham; if he seats a blacksmith, then two dirhams, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, and they say it is not valid. If he rents an animal to al-Hira for one dirham, and if he goes beyond to al-Qadisiyya, then two dirhams, it is valid and may admit difference. If he rents it to al-Hira on condition that if he loads barley on it, then half a dirham; if he loads wheat, then one dirham, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, and they say it is not valid. Their reasoning is that the subject matter is unknown, and the wage is one of two things which is unknown, and uncertainty necessitates invalidity, unlike the Roman and Persian stitching because there the wage becomes due by the work and uncertainty is removed at the time of work. But in these cases, the wage becomes due by vacation and delivery, so uncertainty remains. This is their principle. For Abu Hanifa, he gave him a choice between two valid different contracts, so it is valid as in the case of Roman and Persian stitching.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the validity of ijarah (hire) contracts that specify alternative wages contingent on different outcomes. The discussion covers several scenarios: a tailor hired to sew a garment with different wages if sewn today (one dirham) versus tomorrow (half dirham); a shop rented to either an attar or a blacksmith at different rates; a house rented to the tenant himself or to a blacksmith; and an animal hired for different destinations or loads. The core issue is whether such conditional wages (جعالة) are valid or lead to uncertainty (جهالة) rendering the contract void. Abu Hanifa considers these contracts valid: the specified wage applies when the condition is fulfilled, and if not, a fair wage (اجرة مثل) is due, capped by the lower named amount. The Sahibayn argue that both the subject matter (منفعة) and the wage are unknown at the time of contract, and uncertainty invalidates the contract. They distinguish the tailoring case (Roman vs. Persian stitching) because there the wage becomes known at the time of work, whereas in these cases the wage is due upon handing over the property (تخلیہ) before the work is done. The commentary sides with Abu Hanifa's view as the stronger (اصح). This text is from the Urdu commentary 'Ashraf al-Hidaya' on the Hanafi classic 'Al-Hidaya', expanding on its concise rulings.

Key Terms
اجرة مسمى (ujrat al-musamma): The wage explicitly named and agreed upon in the contract.
اجرة مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work, used when the named wage is invalid or not applicable.
جهالة (jahalah): Legal uncertainty or ignorance that can invalidate a contract if excessive.
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspension of a contract's effect on a future condition; generally not accepted in ijarah.
توقیت (tawqit): Binding the contract to a specific time period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a tailor is hired with the condition: 'If you sew today, 1 dirham; if tomorrow, 0.5 dirham', and he sews on the third day, what wage does he receive?
A) 1 dirham
B) 0.5 dirham at most, as ujrat al-mithl
C) Nothing, because the contract is void
D) The fair wage less than 0.5 dirham

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, alternative wages can be valid if they represent a choice between known options; uncertainty is resolved upon condition fulfillment.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Tailor's Wage for Third-Day Sewing
Ruling on tailor's wage when sewing occurs on the third day – intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of awlawiyya (a fortiori) to determine the wage when a hired tailor delays work beyond the agreed time, and distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Delay reduces benefit, but the wage cannot exceed the named amount; a fortiori reasoning limits the wage.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi dispute in contracts of hire (ijara). The case: a tailor is hired to sew a cloth on the first day but sews on the third. Should he receive the full wage, half, or less? Both Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, use the same starting point—the named wage of half a dirham—but reach different conclusions because of their differing assessment of the lessee's consent.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa rules regarding the tailor's wage for sewing on the third day.
He holds that no more than half a dirham is due.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Name the Sahibayn and state their ruling on this case.
They hold that the wage should be less than half a dirham.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Sahibayn's reasoning: the greater delay diminishes the benefit to the lessee, so the wage should be reduced accordingly.
Their dalil seems to be based on a stricter view of implied consent.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Show how Abu Hanifa uses awlawiyya (a fortiori): if the lessee was not satisfied with a one-day delay, he is even less satisfied with a two-day delay, so the wage cannot increase beyond the named amount.
This is a qiyas-based argument.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the tailor gets exactly half a dirham; under the Sahibayn, he gets less than half.
The text declares Abu Hanifa's view as the correct (sahih) and relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فان خاطه في اليوم الثالث .... الخ - پھر اگر درزی نے کپڑا تیسرے روز سیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نصف درہم سے زیادہ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ جب مستاجر کل تک کی تاخیر پر راضی نہیں تھا تو پرسوں تک کی تاخیر پر بدرجہ اولی راضی نہ ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک صحیح یہ ہے کہ نصف درہم سے کم کر دیا جائے۔
He said: If he sewed it on the third day... then if the tailor sewed the cloth on the third day, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no more than half a dirham will be given. This is correct. Because when the lessee was not satisfied with the delay until the next day, then a fortiori he will not be satisfied with the delay until the day after. According to the Sahibayn, the correct view is that it should be reduced to less than half a dirham.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a tailor who delayed sewing until the third day when the contract specified the first day. The original ruling (assumed from earlier text) is that if the tailor sews on the first day, he gets the named wage; if on the second day, he still gets it because the lessee implicitly consents. The issue here is the third day. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that no more than half a dirham (the agreed wage for the first day) is due, because the lessee's consent to delay does not extend beyond one day; the third day is a further breach. The Sahibayn, however, hold that the wage should be reduced to less than half a dirham, as the delay is more severe. The text prefers Abu Hanifa's view as correct. This follows the Hanafi principle of 'the stronger reason' (adilla al-awlawiyya): if the lessee is not content with a one-day delay, he is even less content with a two-day delay.

Key Terms
اجرت مثل (ujrat mithl): The equivalent wage determined by market rate when named wage is invalid or unjust.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
بدرجہ اولی (bi-darajah awla): A fortiori; with even greater reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what wage is due to the tailor if he sews the cloth on the third day?
A) The named wage (half dirham) in full.
B) More than half a dirham.
C) No more than half a dirham.
D) Less than half a dirham.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijara, the wage for delayed performance is limited to the named wage; a fortiori reasoning prevents increase, but a one-day delay is excused by implied consent.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Validity of Conditional Ijara Contracts with Variable Wages
Rulings on ijara contracts with conditional wage based on lessee's choice of use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Abu Hanifa's position on conditional ijara contracts and contrast it with the Sahibayn's view, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A rental contract is valid if the wage is tied to the lessee's future permissible choice, as uncertainty resolves at use.

In Hanafi fiqh, a lease contract requires that both the benefit (manfa'ah) and the wage (ujrah) be known at the time of contract. But what if the wage is not fixed, but instead depends on which of two permissible uses the lessee chooses? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples – Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) – famously disagreed. This lesson unpacks their arguments and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify the examples given (shop, house, animal) and the ruling that the contract is valid and the named wage is due for whichever use is chosen.
Abu Hanifa upholds validity as long as both uses are permissible and the wage is specified for each.
2
Identify the opponent's view
The Sahibayn (and the three other imams) rule the contract void (fasid) due to ignorance (jahala) in the object and wage.
They require certainty at contract formation, not at performance.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning: the wage becomes due upon delivery (takhliya wa taslim) in property ijara, before the exact use is known, so uncertainty remains and invalidates the contract.
Contrast with service ijara (tailoring) where wage is due upon work, resolving uncertainty.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa argues that the lessee is given a choice between two distinct valid contracts, analogous to Roman vs Persian tailoring. The uncertainty is removed at the time of benefit (intifa').
He distinguishes the lessee's self-occupancy from hiring out to a blacksmith as fundamentally different acts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the named wage for the chosen use is due; under the Sahibayn, the contract is void and the lessee must pay ujrat al-mithl (equivalent rent).
Later Hanafi fatwa relies on Abu Hanifa's view due to necessity.

اگر اس دکان میں عطار کو ٹھہرائے تو ایک درہم ایک مہینے میں اگر لوہار کو ٹھہرائے تو دو در ہم اجارہ جائز ہے
ولو قال ان اسكنتَ فى هذا الدكان عطارا فبدرهم فى الشهر وان اسكنته حدادا فبدرهمین جاز وای الأمرين فعل استحق المسمى فيه عند ابي حنيفة وقالا الاجارة فاسدة وكذا اذا استاجر بيتا على انه ان سكن فيه فبدرهم وان اسكن فيه حدادا فبدرهمين فهو جائز عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لا يجوز ومن استاجر دابة الى الحيرة بدرهم وان جاوز بها الى القادسية فبدرهمين فهو جائز ويحتمل الخلاف وان استاجرها الى الحيرة على انه ان حمل عليها كر شعير فينصف درهم وان حمل عليها كر حنطة فبدرهم فهو جائز في قول ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا لا يجوز وجه قولهما ان المعقود عليه مجهول وكذا الاجر احد الشيائين وهو مجهول والجهالة توجب الفساد بخلاف الخياطة الرومية والفارسية لان الاجر يجب بالعمل وعنده ترتفع الجهالة اما في هذه المسائل يجب الاجر بالتخلية والتسليم فيبقى الجهالة وهذا الحرف هو الاصل عندهما ولابي حنيفة انه خيّره بين عقدين صحيحين مختلفين فيصح كما في مسألة الرومية والفارسية وهذا لان سكناه بنفسه يخالف اسكانه الحداد الاترى انه لايدخل ذالك فى مطلق العقد وكذا فى اخواتها والاجارة تعقد للانتفاع وعنده ترتفع الجهالة ولو احتيج الى الايجاب بمجرد التسليم يجب اقل الاجرين للتيقن به
ترجمہ اگر کہا کہ اگر تو نے اس دکان میں عطار بٹھایا تو ایک درہم ماہواری ہے اور لوہار بٹھایا تو دو درہم ماہواری ہے تو یہ جائز ہے۔ ان میں سے جو کرے گا اس کی اجرت مسمی کا مستحق ہوگا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اجارہ فاسد ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کمرو بایں شرط کرایہ پر لیا کہ اگر خود رہا تو ایک درہم میں ہے اور لوہار کو رکھا تو دو درہم میں ہے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جائز نہیں۔ اگر جانور کرایہ پر لیا حیرہ تک ایک درہم میں اور اگر اس سے قادسیہ تک بڑھا تو دو درہم میں تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اور اختلاف کا احتمال ہے اگر جانور حیرہ تک بائیں شرط کرایہ پر لیا کہ اگر اس پر ایک کر جو لا دے تو نصف درہم میں ہے۔ اور اگر ایک گر گیہوں لا دے تو ایک درہم میں ہے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول میں ۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جائز نہیں ۔ ان کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے۔ کہ معقود علیہ مجہول ہے۔ ایسے ہی اجرت دو چیزوں میں سے ایک ہے اور وہ مجہول ہے اور جہالت موجب فساد ہوتی ہے بخلاف، رومی و فارسی سلائی کے کیونکہ اجرت واجب ہو گی عمل سے اور عمل کے وقت جہالت اٹھ جائے گی۔ رہے یہ مسائل سوان میں اجرت تخلیہ اور تسلیم
سے واجب ہو جاتی ہے تو جہالت باقی رہے گی۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک یہی کلیہ ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے دو مختلف اور صحیح عقدوں میں اختیار دیا ہے تو صحیح ہوگا۔ جیسے رومی و فارسی سلائی کے مسئلہ میں ہے۔ اور یہ اس لئے کہ اس کا خود بنا لو ہار کو بسانے کے خلاف ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ یہ مطلق عقد میں داخل نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح دیگر اجارات میں ہے۔ اور اجارہ منعقد کیا جاتا ہے انتفاع کے لئے اور انتفاع کے وقت جہالت جاتی رہے گی اور اگر خالی سپرد کرنے سے
ایجاب اجرت کی ضرورت پڑی تو اقل الا جرین واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہ متیقن ہے۔
تشریح قوله ولو قال ان اسكنت ... الخ - مکان و عامل، مسافت اور بوجھ میں تردید کرنے سے بھی اجرت کی تردید صحیح ہے۔ مثلاً یوں کہے کہ اگر اس دکان میں لوہار کو رکھے گا۔ تو یہ کرایہ ہو گا اور خطار کو رکھے گا تو یہ ہوگا یا اصل جانور کو کوفہ تک لے جائے گا تو یہ کرایہ ہو گا۔ اور واسط تک لے جائے گا تو یہ ہو گا یا اس پر گیہوں لا دے گا تو اجرت یہ ہوگی اور جولا دے گا تو یہ ہوگی ۔ ان تر دیدات میں سے جو چیز پائی جائے گی۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کی اجرت واجب ہوگی ۔ صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزد یک عقد ہی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ قـولــه ويحتمل الاختلاف .. الخ ۔ یعنی دابۂ مستاجرہ مذکورہ کے حکم میں دونوں احتمال ہیں یہ بھی ممکن ہے۔ کہ اجارہ کا جواز سب کے نزدیک ہو اور یہ بھی ممکن ہے کہ جواز کا قول امام ابو حنیفہ کا ہو اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز نہ ہو۔ جیسے اس مسئلہ کے دیگر نظائر میں ان کے یہاں عدم جواز ہے۔ احتمال اختلاف کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں سے اس مسئلہ کی بابت کوئی اختلاف ذکر نہیں کیا۔ غایہ البیان میں ہے کہ فقیہ ابواللیث کا میلان اس طرف ہے کہ حکم مذکور اتفاقی ہے۔ اور فخر الاسلام کا میلان اس طرف ہے کہ حکم جواز امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک عدم جواز ہے۔ عقابی وغیرہ بھی اسی طرف گئے ہیں۔
قوله وجه قولهما ... الخ - صاحبین کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ صورتوں میں معقود علیہ مجہول ہے۔ نیز اجرت دو چیزوں میں سے ایک چیز ہے اور وہ بھی مجہول ہے اور جہالت موجب فساد ہوتی ہے بخلاف رومی یا فارسی سلائی کے کہ اس میں اجارہ کا فساد اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ اجرت تو کام کرنے کے بعد واجب ہوگی اور اس وقت جہالت مرتفع ہو جائے گی۔ بخلاف ان مسائل کے جو یہاں مذکور ہیں کہ ان میں تخلیہ تسلیم ہی سے اجرت واجب ہوتی ہے تو جہالت باقی رہے گی ۔ صاحبین کے یہاں قاعدہ کلیہ یہی ہے
ان الاجر متي وجب بالتسليم من غير عمل ولا يدرى عند التسليم ايهما يجب يفسد العقد قوله ولابي حنيفة .... الخ - امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے مستاجر کو دو مختلف اور صحیح عقدوں میں اختیار دیا ہے تو جیسے بحالت انفراد عقد صحیح ہے ایسے ہی بحالت اجتماع صحیح ہو گا۔ اور ہم نے مختلف عقد اس لئے قرار دیئے کہ مستاجر کا خود ہنا اور لوہار کو بسانا دونوں مختلف ہیں اسی لئے مطلق عقد میں لو ہار کو ٹہر انا داخل نہیں ہوتا۔ قوله ولوا حتیج ال - اگر خالی تسلیم سے ایجاب اجبرت کی ضرورت پڑے بایں طور کہ عین مستاجرہ سپرد کردی لیکن اس سے ابھی نفع نہیں اٹھایا یہاں تک کہ منفعت معلوم ہو ۔ تو اقل الاجرین واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ متیقن ہے۔ ہو۔
If he said: If you seat an 'attar (perfumer) in this shop, then one dirham per month; if you seat a blacksmith, then two dirhams - the contract is valid. Whichever of the two actions he does, he is entitled to the named wage according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Sahibayn) said: The contract is void. Similarly, if he rented a house on condition that if he lives in it himself, it is for one dirham, and if he seats a blacksmith in it, it is for two dirhams - it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, and they said it is not valid. Whoever rents an animal to al-Hira for one dirham, and if he goes beyond it to al-Qadisiyya, then for two dirhams - it is valid and may bear difference of opinion. And if he rents it to al-Hira on condition that if he loads on it a kurr of barley, then half a dirham, and if he loads a kurr of wheat, then one dirham - it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, and they said it is not valid. The reason for their statement: The object of contract is unknown, likewise the wage is one of two things and it is unknown, and ignorance necessitates invalidity, unlike Roman and Persian tailoring, because the wage becomes due with work, and at that time ignorance is removed. As for these issues, the wage becomes due with vacating and delivery, so ignorance remains. This is their general principle. For Abu Hanifa: He gave him a choice between two different valid contracts, so it is valid, like the case of Roman and Persian tailoring. This is because his living in it himself is different from seating a blacksmith; do you not see that this does not enter into the absolute contract? Similarly in its counterparts. The contract of hire is made for benefit, and at the time of benefit, ignorance is removed. And if there is need for obligation merely by delivery, the lesser of the two wages is due for certainty.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the validity of ijara contracts where the wage is determined by the lessee's future choice among different uses. The examples include renting a shop or house with different wages depending on who occupies it (attar vs blacksmith), or renting an animal with different wages for different destinations or loads.

Imam Abu Hanifa considers these contracts valid. His reasoning: the lessee is given a choice between two different, individually valid contracts. This is analogous to the case of Roman vs Persian tailoring (khiyata rumiyya wa farisiyya) where the worker's wage depends on which style he does, and that is valid. Here, the choice is between two distinct permissible uses, each with its own identified wage. Uncertainty about which wage will be due is resolved at the time the lessee exercises his choice, because the wage becomes due at the moment of use (intifa'), and then the benefit is known. If the contract is terminated before use (e.g., mere delivery), the lesser of the two wages is paid because it is the amount certain.

The Sahibayn (and the three other imams according to the commentary) deem these contracts void. Their reason: Both the object (the exact use) and the wage are unknown at the time of contract. This ignorance (jahala) leads to invalidity. Unlike the tailoring case where wage becomes due with work (so ignorance is removed), here in ijara of property, the wage becomes due with vacating and delivery (takhliya wa taslim) before the benefit is taken, so ignorance persists. Their general principle: if the wage is made obligatory by delivery alone, without work, and it is not known at delivery which wage is due, the contract is invalid.

The text also notes a possible difference of opinion regarding the animal hired to al-Hira: Imam Muhammad did not mention a dispute in al-Jami' al-Saghir, leading some scholars (like Faqih Abu al-Layth) to consider it agreed upon (ittifaqi), while others (like Fakhr al-Islam and al-Uqabi) hold that the dispute exists as in the other cases. The relied-upon position appears to be Abu Hanifa's view of validity.

The commentary further explains that the choice can be in place (makan), worker (amil), distance (masafa), or load (bujh). In all such cases, Abu Hanifa validates the contract, while the Sahibayn and the three other imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) declare it void.

Key Hanafi nuance: The wage is not fixed until the lessee's choice is exercised. If the contract ends before that, only the minimum guaranteed wage is due.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijara): A contract of hire or lease for a specific benefit in exchange for a wage.
تخلیہ و تسلیم (takhliya wa taslim): Vacating and delivery of the hired property to the lessee; this triggers the obligation of wage in property rental.
اقل الاجرین (aqall al-ajrayn): The lesser of the two wages; it is due when the contract does not specify which wage applies and the lessee has not yet made a choice.
معقود علیہ (ma'qud 'alayh): The object of contract; in ijara, it is the usufruct (manfa'ah).
جہالت (jahala): Ignorance or uncertainty about a material element of the contract, such as the wage or subject matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is a rental contract valid where the tenant may either live in the house himself for one dirham or seat a blacksmith for two dirhams?
A) Because the wage is known from the start.
B) Because the contract gives a choice between two different valid contracts, and uncertainty is removed at use.
C) Because the house is the subject of rent regardless of occupant.
D) Because the tenant's choice does not affect the wage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a lease contract with a wage contingent on the lessee's choice among permissible uses is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and this is the relied-upon position; the wage becomes certain upon the lessee's exercise of choice.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Hiring with Options for Work, Place, or Load – The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijarah with options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa validates an ijarah contract with options while the Sahibayn deem it invalid, and apply the ruling to determine the mufta bihi and the rent payable.

Core Idea
Giving a choice between individually valid contracts does not make the whole contract invalid.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of an ijarah contract when the employer gives the worker an option between different types of work, places, or loads. While all agree that each option, if taken alone, forms a valid contract, the Sahibayn hold that the uncertainty (jahalah) at the time of contract invalidates it. Abu Hanifa, however, argues that since each option is a valid contract, giving a choice does not introduce harmful ignorance. This lesson will walk you through the arguments, the proof structures, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize the three types of options: place/worker (shop/blacksmith vs tailor), distance (Kufa vs Wasit), load (wheat vs barley). The rent is specified for each option.
The options are alternative obligations; the actual work is determined later by the worker's choice.
2
State the Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Hanifa holds the contract sahih (valid); the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it fasid (invalid). The three other Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) agree with the Sahibayn.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute with cross-madhhab consensus on the opposing view.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's Proof
The ma'qud 'alayh (subject matter) is unknown because the exact work is not specified; the rent is also uncertain because it depends on which option is chosen. Ignorance (jahalah) of either leads to fasād. They distinguish this from the Roman/Persian stitching case, where the rent becomes due after work, removing ignorance.
Their universal principle: if rent becomes obligatory upon delivery (takhliah) without work and the rent is unknown at delivery, the contract is invalid.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's Proof
Abu Hanifa sees the contract as giving an option between two different valid contracts. Since each contract is valid individually, the combined contract is also valid. The rent becomes certain upon the choice being made.
He analogizes to the stitching case, where options among styles do not invalidate the contract.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
Later authorities like Fakhr al-Islam and 'Aqabi prefer Abu Hanifa's view, making it the mufta bihi. However, the practical outcome – the lesser rent being due – is agreed upon by all.
Imam Muhammad's silence in al-Jami' al-Saghir initially suggested consensus, but later scholarship confirmed the ikhtilaf.

امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے مستاجر کو دو مختلف اور صحیح عقدوں میں اختیار دیا ہے تو جیسے بحالت انفراد عقد صحیح ہے ایسے ہی بحالت اجتماع صحیح ہو گا۔ اور ہم نے مختلف عقد اس لئے قرار دیئے کہ مستاجر کا خود ہنا اور لوہار کو بسانا دونوں مختلف ہیں اسی لئے مطلق عقد میں لو ہار کو ٹہر انا داخل نہیں ہوتا۔ قوله ولوا حتیج ال - اگر خالی تسلیم سے ایجاب اجبرت کی ضرورت پڑے بایں طور کہ عین مستاجرہ سپرد کردی لیکن اس سے ابھی نفع نہیں اٹھایا یہاں تک کہ منفعت معلوم ہو ۔ تو اقل الاجرین واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ متیقن ہے۔
Commentary on the phrase 'And if he said: If you occupy...' - The rent is also validly specified by specifying the place, worker, distance, and load. For example, he says: 'If you put a blacksmith in this shop, the rent will be such; if you put a tailor, it will be such,' or 'If you take the animal to Kufa, the rent will be such; if to Wasit, it will be such,' or 'If you load wheat on it, the rent will be such; if barley, it will be such.' Whichever of these specifications occurs, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the rent is obligatory. According to the Sahibayn and the three Imams, the contract itself is not valid. His statement: 'And it may involve a difference of opinion...' means that regarding the ruling of the aforementioned hired animal, there are two possibilities: it is possible that the contract is valid according to all, and it is possible that the ruling of validity is from Imam Abu Hanifa, and the Sahibayn hold it invalid, as in other similar cases. The reason for the possibility of difference is that Imam Muhammad did not mention any difference concerning this issue in al-Jami' al-Saghir. In Ghayat al-Bayan it is said that Faqih Abu al-Layth inclined to the view that the ruling is unanimous, while Fakhr al-Islam inclined to the view that it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and invalid according to the Sahibayn; 'Aqabi and others also inclined to this. His statement: 'The proof of their statement...' - The proof of the Sahibayn's statement is that in the mentioned cases, the subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) is unknown, and also the rent is one of two things, which is also unknown, and ignorance leads to invalidity. This is unlike the case of Roman or Persian stitching, in which the ijarah is not invalid because the rent becomes obligatory after the work, and at that time the ignorance is removed. Unlike the issues mentioned here, where the rent becomes obligatory upon vacant delivery (takhliah) alone, so the ignorance remains. This is the universal principle according to the Sahibayn: whenever the rent becomes obligatory upon delivery without work and it is not known at the time of delivery which one is obligatory, the contract is invalid. His statement: 'And for Abu Hanifa...' - Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that he has given the hirer an option between two different and valid contracts, so just as each contract is valid individually, so is it valid collectively. And we consider them different contracts because the hirer's own sewing and placing the blacksmith are different; therefore, in an absolute contract, placing the blacksmith is not included. His statement: 'And if there is need...' - If there is need for determining the rent by mere delivery, i.e., the hired object is handed over but no benefit is taken from it until the benefit is known, then the lesser of the two rents is obligatory because it is certain.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of an ijarah contract when the hirer gives the employee an option to perform one of several different types of work (e.g., blacksmithing vs. tailoring) or when the employer gives an option regarding the distance or load. Abu Hanifa holds the contract valid because each option constitutes a valid contract on its own, and giving an option between valid contracts does not invalidate the whole. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the three other Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) hold that such ignorance of the exact subject matter (the specific work or rent) at the time of contract makes the contract invalid (fasid). Abu Hanifa analogizes to the case of Roman and Persian stitching, where the worker is given a choice of stitching style; there the contract is valid because rent becomes due after work, removing ignorance. Here, however, the rent becomes due upon mere delivery (takhliah), so ignorance persists. The commentator also notes a possible consensus (ittifaq) view from Imam Muhammad's silence in al-Jami' al-Saghir and then reports a later preference for the difference of opinion. The final ruling: if the contract is invalid due to such ignorance, the lesser of the two rents is payable as mutayyaqin (certain).

Key Terms
معقود علیہ (ma'qud 'alayh): The subject matter of the contract, here the specific benefit (service or use) being hired.
تخلیہ تسلیم (takhliah taslim): Vacant delivery — handing over the hired object without actual use, which in some ijarah contracts makes the rent obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is the ijarah contract invalid when options for work or location are given?
A) Because the rent is not specified at all.
B) Because both the subject matter and the rent are unknown at the time of contract, and ignorance persists.
C) Because the hirer did not specify the duration.
D) Because the worker must be free.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an ijarah contract with options for work/place/load is valid according to Abu Hanifa because each option is a valid contract, and the lesser rent is paid if the contract is deemed invalid.

Taking a Hired Slave on a Journey
Ruling on taking a hired slave on a journey with proof by analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking a hired slave on a journey and explain the proof by analogy emphasizing the role of mashaqqah.

Core Idea
A hired slave cannot be taken on a journey without stipulation because travel imposes extra hardship not covered by an absolute contract.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in ijarah: what happens when a person hires a slave for service in the town and later wishes to take him on a journey? The Hanafi school holds that this is not permissible without an explicit stipulation. The reasoning draws on the concept of mashaqqah (hardship) and analogies to other contracts. By the end, you will understand both the ruling and its underlying proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is taking a hired slave on a journey when the contract of hire was for service in the town (hadar). The ruling is that it is not permitted (ghayr ja'iz) unless travel was stipulated at the time of contract.
The contract itself remains valid; the prohibition is on the hirer's action.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author provides two analogies (qiyas): (1) hiring a house for a blacksmith or washerman – you must specify the trade because it affects the use; (2) hiring an animal for riding in the city – you cannot ride it out on a journey without stipulation.
Both analogies illustrate that a change in the nature of service requires express agreement.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
The common factor ('illah) is the significant increase in hardship (mashaqqah) between town service and travel service. An absolute contract ('itlaq) does not encompass such added burden.
Hanafi usul holds that an absolute contract covers only the customary scope; additional hardship must be explicitly included.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage presents the ruling as established, but some later scholars note that if local custom ('urf) treats travel as part of service, some exceptions may be considered. However, the Hanafi relied-upon position requires stipulation.
This nuance is important for real-world fatwa application.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi. No intra-Hanafi disagreement is recorded in this specific issue.
The strength of the proof (qiyas with clear 'illah) leaves little room for alternate views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من استاجر عبدا ليخدمه فليس له ان يسافر به الا ان يشترط ذالك لان خدمة السفر اشتملت على زيادة مشقة فلا ينتظمها الاطلاق ولهذا جعل السفر عذرا فلابد من اشتراطه كاسكان الحداد والقصار في الدار ولان التفاوت بين الخدمتين ظاهر فاذا تعينت الخدمة فى الحضر لا يبقى غيره داخلا كما في الركوب.
And whoever hires a slave to serve him, he is not permitted to travel with him unless he stipulates that, because the service of travel includes additional hardship, so the absolute contract does not encompass it. For this reason, travel is made an excuse (for rescission), so stipulation is necessary, like placing a blacksmith or a washerman in a house. And because the difference between the two services is apparent, so when the service is specified as in the town (hadar), the other service is not included, just as in riding.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: if a person hires a slave for service (presumably in the town/city), he cannot take that slave on a journey unless he explicitly stipulated that at the time of the contract. The reason is that travel imposes greater hardship on the slave, and an absolute contract ('itlaq) does not cover such hardship. Travel itself is considered a valid excuse to cancel the contract (since the purpose cannot be fulfilled under the same terms). The commentator draws an analogy (qiyas) to hiring a house for a blacksmith or washerman — you must specify the type of work because it affects the use. Similarly, if the service is specified as urban (hadari), the travel service is not included. Another analogy is riding: if you hire an animal for riding in the city, you cannot ride it out on a long journey without stipulation.

Key Terms
مشقة (mashaqqah): Hardship; here specifically the extra hardship of journeying as compared to staying in town.
عذر ('udhr): Excuse; travel is considered a valid excuse for the hirer to rescind the ijarah contract because the service cannot be performed as originally intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can't a person who hires a slave for service in the town take him on a journey without stipulating it?
A) Because the slave's master might object.
B) Because travel involves increased hardship and is not covered by the absolute contract.
C) Because the contract is automatically void if travel occurs.
D) Because the slave must consent to travel.

Key Takeaway
A hired slave cannot be taken on a journey unless travel is stipulated in the contract because the service of travel involves extra hardship not encompassed by absolute terms.

Hiring a Restricted Slave and Taking the Wage
Ruling on validity of ijarah with a mahjoor slave and whether the hirer can reclaim the wage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ijarah with a restricted slave and explain the istihsan basis that validates the contract after work completion.

Core Idea
A restricted slave's beneficial work validates a wage by istihsan, preventing the hirer from reclaiming it.

This lesson explores a specific ruling on hiring a restricted slave (mahjoor). In the Hanafi school, while strict analogy (qiyas) would void the contract due to lack of permission, istihsan (juristic preference) validates it if the work is completed. The hirer cannot then reclaim the wage because the transaction is deemed beneficial. Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being ruled upon? Hiring a mahjoor slave for a month and paying the wage upfront. The ruling: the hirer cannot take back the wage.
2
Recognize the qiyas position
By strict analogy (qiyas), the contract is void because the slave lacks the master's permission and is legally restricted. This is compared to the case if the slave died, where the contract would be invalid.
3
Understand the istihsan basis
Istihsan looks at the outcome: if the work is completed safely, the transaction is beneficial (nafi'). Beneficial acts are implicitly permissible for a restricted slave, like accepting a gift. Thus, the contract is valid by istihsan.
The illa (effective cause) is benefit.
4
Apply to the consequence
Since the contract is valid by istihsan, the hirer has no right to reclaim the wage; the slave keeps it as earned compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من استاجر عبدا محجورا عليه شهرا واعطاه الاجر فليس للمستاجر ان يأخذ منه الاجر واصله ان الاجارة صحيحة استحسانا اذا فرع من العمل والقياس ان لا يجوز لانعدام اذن المولى وقيام الحجر فصار كما اذا هلك العبد وجه الاستحسان ان التصرف نافع على اعتبار الفراغ سالما ضار على اعتبار هلاك العبد والنافع ماذون فيه كقبول الهبة واذا جاز ذالك لم يكن للمستاجر ان ياخذ منه الاجر
And whoever hires a restricted slave for a month and gives him the wage, the hirer is not allowed to take the wage from him. The basis is that the ijarah is valid by istihsan if he completes the work, while by qiyas it is not valid due to the absence of the master's permission and the existence of restraint (hajr), so it becomes like if the slave died. The face of istihsan is that the transaction is beneficial (nafi') on the consideration of completing the work safely, and harmful on the consideration of the slave's perishing, and the beneficial transaction is permitted (ma'dhun fih) like accepting a gift. When that is valid, the hirer cannot take the wage from him.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage deals with a mahjoor slave — a slave who is legally restricted from conducting transactions (e.g., a minor or insane slave, or one whose master has not given permission to work). If such a slave is hired for a month and the hirer pays the wage in advance, and the slave completes the work, the hirer cannot demand the wage back. The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference). By strict analogy (qiyas), the contract would be invalid because the slave lacks the master's permission and is restricted; thus any transaction would be void, similar to if the slave died (so the wage would be lost). However, istihsan considers that the act of working is beneficial (nafi') if the slave completes it safely, and harmful only if the slave perishes or the work is not done. Since beneficial actions are implicitly permitted for the slave (like accepting a gift), the ijarah is deemed valid. Once the contract is valid and the wage paid, the hirer cannot reclaim it.

Key Terms
محجور عليه (mahjoor 'alayh): A slave who is legally restricted (hajr) from conducting transactions due to lack of permission from the master or legal incapacity.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that abandons strict analogy (qiyas) for a more suitable ruling based on benefit or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis (istihsan) for considering the ijarah with a restricted slave valid after work is completed?
A) The slave's master gave implicit permission.
B) The transaction is beneficial and analogous to accepting a gift.
C) The hirer is in urgent need.
D) The slave is treated as a free person.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a restricted slave's completed beneficial work makes the ijarah valid by istihsan, and the hirer cannot reclaim the wage.

Stipulating Travel in a Hire Contract
Ruling with talil and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking a hired slave on a journey without stipulation and explain the qiyas used to derive it.

Core Idea
An absolute hire contract does not cover the increased hardship of travel without explicit stipulation.

This passage addresses a common scenario: hiring a slave for service and then wishing to travel with him. The Hanafi school holds that without a specific stipulation, the contract does not permit travel because traveling imposes additional hardship. The author supports this ruling with a clear analogy to housing a tradesman in a rented dwelling, demonstrating how the absolute contract is interpreted by customary usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
State the ruling: the hirer may not travel with the slave unless he stipulates it. Identify the condition (shart) required.
2
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
Explain why the absolute contract does not cover travel: journey service involves increased hardship (mashaqqa), which the default contract does not include.
3
Examine the first analogy (qiyas)
Compare with lodging a blacksmith or fuller in a rented house: extra burden requires a specific agreement.
The blacksmith's work causes extra wear like travel causes extra fatigue.
4
Examine the second analogy (qiyas)
Compare with hiring a riding animal for a specific route: exceeding the route is not allowed without a new agreement.
This illustrates that specifying a service scope precludes additional services.
5
Derive the 'illah (effective cause)
Identify the 'illah: significant difference in the nature of service (town vs. travel) that amounts to extra hardship.
The 'illah is the increased difficulty that is not included in the standard service.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من استاجر عبدا ليخدمه فليس له ان يسافر به الا ان يشترط ذالك لان خدمة السفر اشتملت على زيادة مشقة فلا ينتظمها الاطلاق ولهذا جعل السفر عذرا فلابد من اشتراطه كاسكان الحداد والقصار في الدار ولان التفاوت بين الخدمتين ظاهر فاذا تعينت الخدمة فى الحضر لا يبقى غيره داخلا كما في الركوب .
ترجمہ جس نے اجارہ پر لیا غلام تا کہ اس کی خدمت کرے تو اس کو سفر میں نہیں لے جاسکتا ۔ مگر یہ کہ اس کی شرط کرے کیونکہ سفری خدمت زائد مشقت پر مشتمل ہے تو مطلق اجارہ اس کو شامل نہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے سفر کو عذر قرار دیا گیا ہے تو اس کی شرط کرنا ضروری ہے گھر میں نو ہار یا دھوبی کو ٹھہرانے کی طرح ۔ اور اس لئے کہ دونوں خدمتوں میں تفاوت ظاہر ہے۔ پس جب حضری خدمت متعین ہو گئی تو دوسری خدمت داخل نہ رہی جیسے سواری میں ہے۔
And whoever hires a slave to serve him, he may not travel with him unless he stipulates that, because journey service includes increased hardship, so the absolute contract does not encompass it. For this reason, travel is made an excuse, so stipulation is necessary, like lodging a blacksmith or fuller in the house. And because the difference between the two services is apparent; when service in the town is specified, other than it does not remain included, as in riding.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: if someone hires a slave for service, he cannot take the slave on a journey unless he explicitly stipulates that condition in the contract. The reason is that journey service involves additional hardship (mashaqqa) compared to service in the town. The absolute contract (itlaq) only covers the usual service, not the extra hardship. By analogy, if you rent a house, you cannot house a blacksmith or fuller who would cause extra wear and tear unless you stipulate it. Similarly, if you hire a riding animal for a specific route, you cannot exceed that route without a new agreement. The text follows the Hanafi position that the default contract is limited to the specified conditions.

Key Terms
اجارة (ijarah): A contract for hire or lease, transferring usufruct (manfa'ah) for a known wage.
اطلاق (itlaq): The absolute, unrestricted scope of the contract without conditions.
مشقة (mashaqqa): Hardship or difficulty that goes beyond the norm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is stipulation required to take a hired slave on a journey?
A) Because travel is inherently dangerous.
B) Because travel involves increased hardship not covered by the absolute contract.
C) Because the slave's master must approve any change of location.
D) Because the contract automatically ends upon travel.

Key Takeaway
Without an explicit stipulation, a hire contract does not permit the hirer to impose additional hardship such as travel.

Hiring an Interdicted Slave and the Role of Istihsan
Ruling on the validity of hiring an interdicted slave and the status of wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring an interdicted slave and explain why the contract is valid by istihsan despite the lack of master's permission.

Core Idea
A contract with an interdicted slave is valid if beneficial — istihsan overrides qiyas.

This passage examines a specific scenario in leasing (ijara): hiring a slave who has been forbidden by his master from trading. The Hanafi school rules that if the slave completes the work safely, the lease is valid and the hirer cannot reclaim the wage, even though the slave lacked permission. The reasoning involves a conflict between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference), and the passage explains why istihsan prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring an interdicted slave. The ruling: the lease is valid (sahih) by istihsan, and the hirer cannot reclaim the wage.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
By qiyas, the contract would be invalid due to lack of master's permission and interdiction, similar to the case of the slave dying.
Qiyas is the default method here.
3
Identify the istihsan argument
The istihsan argument focuses on the beneficial nature of the transaction when the slave returns safely, comparing it to accepting a gift, which is permitted.
Benefit (nafi') vs. harm (darar).
4
Determine the operative principle
The master implicitly permits beneficial acts by the slave, so the contract is valid; the wage becomes the master's property.
5
Note the practical consequence
The hirer cannot reclaim the wage; it belongs to the master because the lease is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من استاجر عبدا محجورا عليه شهرا واعطاه الاجر فليس للمستاجر ان يأخذ منه الاجر واصله ان الاجارة صحيحة استحسانا اذا فرع من العمل والقياس ان لا يجوز لانعدام اذن المولى وقيام الحجر فصار كما اذا هلك العبد وجه الاستحسان ان التصرف نافع على اعتبار الفراغ سالما ضار على اعتبار هلاك العبد والنافع ماذون فيه كقبول الهبة واذا جاز ذالك لم يكن للمستاجر ان ياخذ منه الاجر
ترجمہ کسی نے عبد مجور کو ایک ماہ کے لئے اجارہ پر لیا اور اس کو اجرت دے دی تو مستاجر کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ اس سے اجرت واپس لے لے۔ اس کی اصل یہ ہے کہ اجارہ استحسانا صحیح ہے جب کہ وہ کام سے فارغ ہو گیا اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ جائز نہ ہو۔ آقا کی اجازت نہ ہونے اور حجر قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے غلام مر گیا۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ غلام کا تصرف نافع ہے سلامتی کے ساتھ فارغ ہونے کے اعتبار سے اور مضر ہے غلام کے تلف ہو جانے کے اعتبار سے اور نافع تصرف میں وہ ماذون ہے جیسے ہبہ قبول کرنا پس جب یہ عقد جائز ہوا تو مستاجر کو اس سے اجرت واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ رہا۔
And whoever hires an interdicted slave for a month and gives him the wage, the hirer may not take the wage from him. The basis is that the lease is valid by istihsan if he finishes the work, and by qiyas it is not valid because of the lack of the master's permission and the existence of interdiction, so it becomes as if the slave died. The face of istihsan is that the transaction is beneficial with regard to completion safely, harmful with regard to destruction of the slave, and the beneficial is permitted, like accepting a gift. When that is permitted, the hirer may not take the wage from him.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage discusses hiring a slave who is under interdiction (mahjur) – i.e., a slave not permitted by his master to engage in trade. The ruling is that if such a slave performs the work and receives the wage, the hirer cannot reclaim the wage. By qiyas (analogy), the contract would be invalid because the slave has no capacity to contract without permission, similar to if the slave died. But by istihsan (juristic preference), the contract is valid because the slave's action is beneficial to the master if the slave returns safely, and the master implicitly allows beneficial acts. Therefore, the wage is considered the master's property, and the hirer cannot take it back.

Key Terms
محرور (mahjur): A slave who is interdicted (prevented) by his master from engaging in commercial transactions.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas for a stronger reason (here, benefit to the master).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A hirer pays an interdicted slave for completed work; later the master demands the wage. What happens?
A) The hirer can take the wage back.
B) The hirer must pay the master again.
C) The hirer cannot take the wage back; it belongs to the master.
D) The contract is void and the slave must return the wage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, beneficial acts by an interdicted slave are permitted by istihsan, making the lease valid and the wage non-reclaimable.

Liability of a Usurper Consuming a Slave's Wage: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability of a usurper who consumes a slave's wage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on the usurper's liability for a slave's wage and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Liability for consuming property depends on whether it is protected (muhraz) against the taker.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute. A usurper seizes a slave; the slave then works for a wage, which the usurper consumes. The key question: is the usurper liable to the master? Abu Hanifa says no, because the wage is not 'protected' against someone who already holds the slave. The Sahibayn say yes, because the wage is the master's property consumed without permission. Understanding their reasoning reveals the Hanafi school's method of deriving liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the action
Who are the parties (usurper, slave, master)? What did the usurper do (consume the slave's wage)? What is the legal question (liability)?
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa: no liability. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): liable. Note the authority: both are within the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the reasoning of each side
Abu Hanifa: liability requires destroying protected property (mal muhraz). The wage is not protected against the usurper because the slave cannot protect himself from the usurper. Sahibayn: the lease is valid, so the wage is the master's property. Consuming it without permission triggers liability.
Key term: muhraz (protected).
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical effect
Later Hanafi jurists prefer the Sahibayn's view (liability) for greater protection of the owner's property. The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, the master cannot claim compensation if the wage is consumed; under the Sahibayn, he can.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من غصب عبدًا فآجر العبد نفسه فاخذ الغاصب الاحر فاكله فلاضمان عليه عند ابي حنيفة وقالا هو ضامن لانه اكل مال المالك بغیر اذنه اذ الاجارة قد صحت على مامر وله ان الضمان انما يجب باتلاف مال محرز لان التقوم به وهذا غير محرز فى حق الغاصب لان العبد لا يحرز نفسه عنه فكيف يحرز ما في يده وان وجد المولى الاجر قائما بعينه اخذه لانه وجد عين ماله ويجوز قبض العبد الاجر في قولهم جميعا نـــــــه مــــــادون له في التصرف على اعتبار الفراغ عــلــى مـــــامــــر
And whoever usurps a slave, and the slave hires himself out, and the usurper takes the wage and consumes it, then there is no liability upon him according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is liable, because he consumed the property of the owner without his permission, since the lease is valid as previously mentioned. And for him (Abu Hanifa): liability is only incurred by destroying protected (muhraz) property, because valuation (taqawwum) is based on it, and this (wage) is not protected with respect to the usurper, because the slave cannot protect himself from him, so how can he protect what is in his hand? And if the master finds the wage existing in kind, he takes it, because he finds his property in kind. And the slave's receipt of the wage is valid in the saying of all three (the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa) ... [ unclear ] ... he is authorized in his disposal based on completion as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. A usurper (ghasib) seizes a slave; the slave then hires himself out to a third party and earns a wage. The usurper takes and consumes that wage. Abu Hanifa rules that the usurper is not liable (daman) for the wage to the master. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is liable. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the wage is not considered 'protected property' (mal muhraz) vis-à-vis the usurper because the slave himself cannot be protected from the usurper (since the usurper already wrongfully possesses the slave). Therefore, destroying the wage does not trigger liability. However, if the master finds the actual wage (ayn) in the usurper's possession, he can take it. All three agree that the slave's receipt of the wage is valid, as the slave is authorized to conduct beneficial transactions (like accepting gifts) when the work is completed. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the later Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn (liability), because the master's property is consumed without permission.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Wrongful taking of another's property without consent, a sin and a tort.
محرز (muhraz): Property that is protected or secured; property that is in a safe place or under control.
ضمان (daman): Liability; obligation to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is a usurper not liable for consuming a slave's wage?
A) Because the slave is not the master's property.
B) Because the wage is not considered protected property (muhraz) vis-à-vis the usurper.
C) Because the slave consented.
D) Because the usurper had permission.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, liability for consuming property depends on whether the property is muhraz (protected) against the taker, leading to a valid intra-school dispute in this case.

Hiring Slave for Two Months with Different Wages per Month
Ruling on validity of hire contract with unspecified month order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a hire contract with unspecified month order and explain the reasoning that resolves the ambiguity.

Core Idea
Ambiguity in contract terms is resolved by interpreting the first mentioned period as the immediate one to preserve validity.

In hire contracts (ijara), clarity of time and wage is crucial. However, if a person hires a worker for two months with different monthly wages but does not specify which month gets which wage, the contract appears ambiguous. The Hanafi school rules it valid by applying a principle of interpretation that avoids jahalah (ignorance) and fulfills immediate need. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its justification, and contrasts the view of other schools.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the apparent problem
Identify the contract: hiring a slave for two months, one month at 4 dirhams and the other at 5 dirhams, without specifying which month. Recognize the ambiguity (jahalah) in the timing of each wage.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its immediate implication
The contract is valid (ja'iz). The first mentioned month (4 dirhams) is assigned to the month immediately following the contract, and the second month (5 dirhams) follows.
The ruling salvages the contract from invalidity.
3
Explain the reasoning (ta'lil)
The reasoning is twofold: (1) to avoid jahalah that would render the contract fasid, and (2) to fulfill the immediate need of the hirer, which is presumed to arise at contract time. The principle that speech should not be wasted (la yuhmilu kalam al-'aqil 'ala al-ilgha') drives this interpretation.
This is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve the contract.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i and some Hanbalis require explicit naming of the month for validity. For them, the ambiguity is fatal. The Hanafi response is that the ambiguity is resolvable by interpreting the first month as the immediate one.
Maliki and many Hanbali scholars agree with the Hanafi position.
5
Address the textual objection regarding the definite form 'hādhayni al-shahrayn'
Al-Hidayah uses the definite form 'these two months' whereas earlier sources used the indefinite 'two months'. The objection is that the reasoning about tankīr (indefiniteness) may not apply. The answer (by Shaykh Hamid al-Din al-Darir) is that the demonstrative 'hādhayni' still does not specify which month is which, so the same reasoning holds.
The wording does not affect the underlying ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی نے دو مہینوں کے لئے غلام کرایہ پر لیا ایک ماہ بعوض چار درہم اور ایک ماہ بعوض پانچ در ہم تو اجارہ جائز ہے

ومن استجار عبدا هذين الشهرين شهرا باربعة وشهرا بخمسة فهو جائز والاول منهما باربعة لان الشهر المذكور اولا ينصرف الى ما يلى العقد تحريا للجواز ونظرا الى تنجز الحاجة فينصرف الثاني الى ما يلى الاول ضرورة

ترجمہ کسی نے غلام اجارہ پر لیا ان دو مہینوں کے لئے۔ ایک ماہ بعوض چار درہم اور ایک ماہ بعوض پانچ درہم تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اور پہلا مہینہ ان میں سے بعوض چار درہم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جو ما ہ پہلے مذکور ہے وہ اس کی طرف منصرف ہو جا جو عقد سے متصل ہے عقد کو جائز کرنے یا حاجت کو بالفعل پوری کرنے کی غرض سے پس دوسرا مہینہ ضرور اس کی طرف منصرف ہوگا جو اول سے متصل ہے۔

وجہ سے فاسد ہو جاتا ہے۔ نیز اس لئے بھی کہ انسان اپنی ضرورت ہی کے لئے کوئی شی اجارہ پر لیتا ہے اور ظاہر یہی ہے کہ ضرورت کا وقوع بوقت عقد ہی ہوگا اس لئے جو مہینہ فی الحال شروع ہو وہی پہلا مہینہ قرار دیا جائے گا۔ اور جب وہ پہلا مہینہ قرار پا گیا تو اب دوسرا مہینہ لا محالہ وہ ہوگا جو اس کے بعد ہے۔ امام مالک اور امام احمد کے یہاں بھی مسئلہ کا یہی حکم ہے۔ البتہ امام احمد کے بعض اصحاب اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک عقد مذکور صحیح نہیں حتى يسمى الشهر

And whoever hires a slave for these two months: one month for four dirhams and one month for five dirhams, it is valid. And the first of them is for four dirhams, because the month mentioned first is turned to what follows the contract, seeking validity and considering the realization of need. Then the second turns to what follows the first by necessity.

Commentary
This passage explains a ruling from al-Hidayah about hiring a slave for two months with different wages per month, without specifying which month gets which wage. The contract is valid (ja'iz) by interpreting the first mentioned month as the month immediately following the contract, assigned the first mentioned wage (four dirhams). The reasoning is to avoid ignorance (jahalah) that would invalidate the contract, and to respect the intention of fulfilling immediate need. The commentary notes that other schools (Maliki, Hanbali) agree, but Shafi'i and some Hanbalis require specification of the month. The answer by Shaykh Hamid al-Din al-Darir is quoted but cut off.

Key Terms
تنکیر (tankīr): Indefinite form: here it means the months are mentioned without specifying which months they are.
معرفہ (ma'rifah): Definite form: here it means the months are specified by the demonstrative 'hādhayni'.
جہالت (jahālah): Ignorance or ambiguity in a contract that can render it invalid.
