Hiring for Two Months with Different Wages: Validity via Istihsan
Ruling and justification for valid hire contract with unspecified months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a person for two months with different wages and explain the justification using the principles of taharrī al-jawāz and tanjjuz al-hājah.

Core Idea
A hire contract with unspecified months is saved by interpreting the first month as immediate.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common contract dilemma: a person hires a slave for two months, with different wages for each month, but without specifying which month is first. Apparent uncertainty could invalidate the contract, but the Hanafi school uses interpretive principles to uphold its validity. You will learn how the school 'strives for validity' (taharrī al-jawāz) and considers the immediate need (tanjjuz al-hājah) to resolve the ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its apparent problem
The contract is for hiring a person for two months with different wages per month. The months are not specified as to which one comes first, creating ambiguity (jahālah) that could void the contract.
In Hanafi fiqh, gharar (uncertainty) in the object of hire generally invalidates the contract.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The contract is valid (jā'iz). The first month is the one immediately following the contract, and it carries the lower wage (four dirhams). The second month follows the first and takes the higher wage.
The ruling applies whether the hired person is a slave or free.
3
Explain the two principles of justification
First, taharrī al-jawāz: the law strives to make the contract valid by interpreting ambiguous speech in a way that avoids invalidity. Second, tanjjuz al-hājah: the need for the hire arises at the moment of the contract, so the first month is the immediate one.
This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas.
4
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad agree with the Hanafi ruling. Imam al-Shafi'i and some followers of Ahmad require the months to be explicitly named, otherwise the contract is invalid due to jahālah.
The practical difference: Hanafis permit such contracts; Shafi'is require specification.
5
Apply the ruling to a similar scenario
If a free man is hired instead of a slave, the same ruling applies. The principles are not dependent on the status of the hired person.
This shows that the ruling is general for all hire contracts with unspecified time periods.

Source Text

کسی نے دو مہینوں کے لئے غلام کرایہ پر لیا ایک ماہ بعوض چار درہم اور ایک ماہ بعوض پانچ در ہم تو اجارہ جائز ہے
كتاب الاجارات
ومن استجار عبدا هذين الشهرين شهرا باربعة وشهرا بخمسة فهو جائز والاول منهما باربعة لان الشهر المذكور اولا ينصرف الى ما يلى العقد تحريا للجواز ونظرا الى تنجز الحاجة فينصرف الثاني الى ما يلى الاول ضرورة
ترجمہ کسی نے غلام اجارہ پر لیا ان دو مہینوں کے لئے۔ ایک ماہ بعوض چار درہم اور ایک ماہ بعوض پانچ درہم تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اور پہلا مہینہ ان میں سے بعوض چار درہم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جو ما ہ پہلے مذکور ہے وہ اس کی طرف منصرف ہو جا جو عقد سے متصل ہے عقد کو جائز کرنے یا حاجت کو بالفعل پوری کرنے کی غرض سے پس دوسرا مہینہ ضرور اس کی طرف منصرف ہوگا جو اول سے متصل ہے۔ تشریح... قوله ومن استاجر عبداً .... الخ ۔ کسی نے ایک غلام دو ماہ کے لئے بایں طور اجارہ پر لیا کہ ایک ماہ چار درہم کے عوض ہے اور ایک ماہ پانچ درہم کے عوض ہے۔ تو اس نے عقد میں دو ماہ بصورت تنکیر ایسے ذکر کئے ہیں ۔ جن کا وقت معلوم نہیں۔ پس بظاہر یہ عقد جائز نہیں ہونا چاہئیے ۔ لیکن عاقل بالغ کا کلام چونکہ رائیگاں ہونے سے بچانا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے عقد کو حتی الامکان جائز کرنے کی خاطر جو مہینہ پہلے مذکور ہے۔ وہ عقد سے متصل مہینہ قرار دیا جائے گا۔ یھی جو مہینہ عقد کے بعد شروع ہوگا وہی پہلا مہینہ مانا جائے گا اور چار درہم عوض والا ہوگا ۔ اگر ایسا نہ کیا جائے تو داخل عقد مہینہ مجہول ہو گا۔ حالانکہ عقد اجارہ جہالت کی وجہ سے فاسد ہو جاتا ہے۔ نیز اس لئے بھی کہ انسان اپنی ضرورت ہی کے لئے کوئی شی اجارہ پر لیتا ہے اور ظاہر یہی ہے کہ ضرورت کا وقوع بوقت عقد ہی ہوگا اس لئے جو مہینہ فی الحال شروع ہو وہی پہلا مہینہ قرار دیا جائے گا۔ اور جب وہ پہلا مہینہ قرار پا گیا تو اب دوسرا مہینہ لا محالہ وہ ہوگا جو اس کے بعد ہے۔ امام مالک اور امام احمد کے یہاں بھی مسئلہ کا یہی حکم ہے۔ البتہ امام احمد کے بعض اصحاب اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک عقد مذکور صحیح نہیں حتى يسمى الشهر
قوله هذين الشهرين ... الخ - تاج الشریعہ وغیرہ نے اس پر یہ اشکال ذکر کیا ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے جو مسئلہ کی تعلیل تحری جواز تبخیز حاجت ذکر کی ہے اس کا مدار اس بات پر ہے کہ مستاجر نے لفظ شہرین کو بصورت نکرہ ذکر کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ مبسوط ، شیخ عتابی و ایجابی کی جامع صغیر اور دیگر کتب فقہیہ میں یونہی مرقوم ہے اذا استاجر عبد الشهرين شهرًا بار بعة وشهرًا بخمسة “ حالانکہ صاحب ہدایہ نے مسئلہ کی وضع معرفہ کی صورت میں رکھی ہے۔ حیث قال "هذين الشهرين “ اور اس صورت میں تعلیل مذکور مستقیم نہیں رہتی ۔
اس کا جواب جو شیخ حمیدالدین الضریر نے اپنے حواشی ہدایہ میں دیا ہے اور صاحب عنا یہ وصاحب کفایہ وغیرہ نے اپنی شرح ہدایہ میں نقل کیا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ کتاب میں جو ہذین الشہر مین ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی طرف سے وضع مسئلہ کے طور پر نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ مستاجر کا قول ہے اور لام برائے عہد ہے گو یا مؤجر نے مستاجر سے یوں کہا۔ اجرت عبدى هذا شهرين باربعة و شهرا بخمسة اس کے جواب میں متاجر نے کہا استاجر ته هذين الشهرين شهراً بار بعة و شهرا بخمسة پس هذين الشهرین ۔ اسی شہرین نکرہ کی طرف منصرف ہے جو موجر کے ایجاب میں داخل ہے تو تنگیر اپنی جگہ پر باقی رہی اور تعلیل مذکور مستقیم ہوگئی۔
لیکن صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ اشکال مذکور بھی بے وجہ ہے اور مذکورہ جواب بھی بیکار ہے۔ اشکال تو اس لئے بے وجہ ہے کہ تعلیل مذکور شہرین کی تنکیر پر موقوف نہیں بلکہ یہ تو شهر باربعة وشهراً بخسمة میں جو شہر انکرہ ہے اس سے بھی نام ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور مذکورہ جواب اس لئے برکا رہے کہ کتاب میں جو ہذین الشہرین ہے یہ اگر مستاجر کا قول ہو تو صاحب ہدایہ کا " و من استاجر عبدا م میں عبد کو نکرہ لانا برمحل نہ ہو گا بلکہ شہرین کو معرفہ لانے کے بجائے عبد کو معرفہ لانا احق ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس سے یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی کہ مستاجر میں لام کا برائے عہد ہونا اس وقت متصور ہو سکتا ہے جب عقد میں موجر کا کلام مستاجر کے کلام سے مقدم ہو ۔ حالانکہ یہ کوئی ضروری نہیں بلکہ متعاقدین میں سے جو بھی پہلے کلام کرے اس کا کلام ایجاب قرار پائے گا۔ اور جب دوسرا قبول کر لے تو عقد لازم ہو جائے گا۔ پھر بہت ممکن ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ عام کتب کے خلاف هذين الشهرين “ معرفہ اس لئے لائے ہوں۔ تا کہ یہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ لفظ شہرین کے معرفہ ہونے سے مسئلہ کے حکم میں کوئی فرق نہیں آتا بلکہ اس حکم میں شہرین کی تعرف و تنکیر دونوں برابر ہیں جب کہ شھراً باربعة و شهرًا بخمسة میں لفظ شهر انکرہ موجود ہے۔
متنبیہ مسئلہ مذکورہ کا جو حکم بیان کیا گیا ہے وہ صرف اسی صورت کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے کہ اجیر غلام ہی ہو بلکہ اجیر اگر کوئی آزاد شخص ہو تب بھی یہی حکم ہے اور دلیل بھی بعینہ وہی ہے جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔ پس اس مسئلہ کو باب اجارۃ العبد میں لانے کی کوئی خاص وجہ ظاہر نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ اس باب میں تو انہیں احکام کا ذکر مناسب ہے جن کا غلام کے ساتھ کوئی اختصاص ہے۔ ورنہ ظاہر ہے کہ ابواب سابقہ میں جو احکام گزرے ہیں ان میں سے بہت سے احکام ایسے ہیں جو حر وعبد میں مشترک ہیں۔
ممکن ہے کوئی یہ کہے کہ چونکہ آزاد کی بہ نسبت غلام کا اجیر ہونا زیادہ تر ہوتا ہے اس لئے اکثری وقوع کا لحاظ کر کے اس باب میں ذکر کر دیا۔ لیکن یہ کہنا اس لئے صحیح نہیں کہ اکثریت ناقابل تسلیم ہے کیونکہ غلام کی بہ نسبت آزاد کا اجیر ہونا ظاہر تر ہے اس لئے کہ ایک تو آزاد شخص کو تصرفات میں استقلال حاصل ہے۔ دوسرے یہ کہ اپنی ذات پر اور اپنے اہل و عیال پر خرچ کرنے کی احتیاج بھی غلام کی بہ نسبت آزاد کو زیادہ ہوتی ہے۔
Someone hired a slave for two months: one month for four dirhams and one month for five dirhams – the hire is valid. And the first of them is for four dirhams because the month mentioned first is directed to that which is adjacent to the contract, seeking validity and looking to the immediate fulfillment of need; so the second is necessarily directed to that which is adjacent to the first.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Hidayah on a hire contract where the months are unspecified but the wages differ. The ruling states that the contract is valid, and the first month is the one immediately following the contract, with the lower wage (four dirhams). The reasoning is based on two principles: (1) taharrī al-jawāz – striving to make the contract valid by interpreting the speech in a way that avoids invalidity, and (2) nazaran ilā tanjjuz al-hājah – considering that need arises at the time of the contract, so the first month must be the current one. The commentary then addresses an objection: the matn in Al-Hidayah uses the definite phrase 'hādhayn al-shahrayn' (these two months) while other works use the indefinite 'shahrayn'. The objection is that the reasoning about tanjīz al-hājah depends on the months being indefinite. Several answers are given, including one that the definite phrase is part of the musta'jir's speech referring back to the mujīr's offer, and another that the indefinite 'shahran' in the wage specification suffices to create the ambiguity. The passage ends with a note that the same ruling applies whether the hired person is a slave or a free person, though the chapter is on hiring slaves.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijārah): A contract of hiring or leasing whereby one party pays for the benefit of a service or property for a specified period.
تنکیر (tankīr): Indefiniteness; the word 'shahran' (a month) is indefinite because it is not specified which month.
تحری الجواز (taharrī al-jawāz): Striving to make the contract valid by interpreting ambiguous words in a way that avoids invalidity.
تنجز الحاجة (tanjjuz al-hājah): The immediate occurrence of need; the assumption that the need for the hire arises at the time of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when a person hires a slave for two months with four dirhams for one month and five dirhams for the other, which month is assigned the lower wage?
A) The second month
B) The month specified by the lessor
C) The first month immediately following the contract
D) Either month, depending on the parties' intent

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to uphold contract validity when ambiguity can be resolved by reasonable interpretation.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Critique of Chapter Placement in Ijara al-Abd
Critique of Hidayah's chapter placement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the appropriateness of a fiqh ruling's placement within a specific chapter based on the generality of its application.

Core Idea
A ruling's chapter does not restrict its scope; the same rule applies to free and slave.

This passage is a sharp critique of Al-Hidayah's decision to place a case about hiring with varying wage statements in the chapter on hiring a slave. The commentator argues that the ruling is not exclusive to slaves and that the chapter placement lacks logical necessity. This discussion sharpens your ability to distinguish between a ruling's content and its location in classical fiqh works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Locate the commentator's primary criticism: that the case of hiring with two different wage amounts is placed in 'Kitab al-Ijara, Bab Ijara al-Abd' (Chapter of Hiring a Slave).
The case involves a lessor and lessee disputing over the definite/indefinite wording of months.
2
Analyze the Refutation
Read the response from the author of Nata'ij and the commentator: the objection is baseless because the ruling does not depend on the indefiniteness of the months and the same proof applies whether the hired person is free or slave.
The commentator also critiques the author of Hidayah's hypothetical answer regarding the 'lam of covenant'.
3
Evaluate the Excuse of Common Occurrence
Consider the possible justification that slaves are more commonly hired, hence the placement. The commentator rejects this, noting that free persons are actually more frequently hired due to their independence and financial needs.
This step teaches you to assess when a 'majority' argument is valid in fiqh.
4
Extract the Maxim
Conclude that chapter placement in a fiqh text does not limit the ruling's applicability. The ruling's proof applies to all relevant cases, regardless of the chapter heading.
This principle is essential for proper istinbat and understanding the scope of Hanafi rulings.

صاحب ہدایہ کی طرف سے وضع مسئلہ کے طور پر نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ مستاجر کا قول ہے اور لام برائے عہد ہے گو یا مؤجر نے مستاجر سے یوں کہا۔ اجرت عبدى هذا شهرين باربعة و شهرا بخمسة اس کے جواب میں متاجر نے کہا استاجر ته هذين الشهرين شهراً بار بعة و شهرا بخمسة پس هذين الشهرین ۔ اسی شہرین نکرہ کی طرف منصرف ہے جو موجر کے ایجاب میں داخل ہے تو تنگیر اپنی جگہ پر باقی رہی اور تعلیل مذکور مستقیم ہوگئی۔
لیکن صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ اشکال مذکور بھی بے وجہ ہے اور مذکورہ جواب بھی بیکار ہے۔ اشکال تو اس لئے بے وجہ ہے کہ تعلیل مذکور شہرین کی تنکیر پر موقوف نہیں بلکہ یہ تو شهر باربعة وشهراً بخسمة میں جو شہر انکرہ ہے اس سے بھی نام ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور مذکورہ جواب اس لئے برکا رہے کہ کتاب میں جو هذين الشہرین ہے یہ اگر مستاجر کا قول ہو تو صاحب ہدایہ کا " و من استاجر عبدا م میں عبد کونکرہ لا نا برمحل نہ ہو گا بلکہ شہرین کو معرفہ لانے کے بجائے عبد کو معرفہ لانا احق ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس سے یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی کہ مستاجر میں لام کا برائے عہد ہونا اس وقت متصور ہو سکتا ہے جب عقد میں موجر کا کلام مستاجر کے کلام سے مقدم ہو ۔ حالانکہ یہ کوئی ضروری نہیں بلکہ متعاقدین میں سے جو بھی پہلے کلام کرے اس کا کلام ایجاب قرار پائے گا۔ اور جب دوسرا قبول کر لے تو عقد لازم ہو جائے گا۔ پھر بہت ممکن ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ عام کتب کے خلاف هذين الشهرين " معرفہ اس لئے لائے ہوں۔ تا کہ یہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ لفظ شہرین کے معرفہ ہونے سے مسئلہ کے حکم میں کوئی فرق نہیں آتا بلکہ اس حکم میں شہرین کی تعرف و تنکیر دونوں برابر ہیں جب کہ شھراً باربعة و شهرًا بخمسة میں لفظ شهر انکرہ موجود ہے۔
متنبیہ مسئلہ مذکورہ کا جو حکم بیان کیا گیا ہے وہ صرف اسی صورت کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے کہ اجیر غلام ہی ہو بلکہ اجیر اگر کوئی آزاد شخص ہو تب بھی یہی حکم ہے اور دلیل بھی بعینہ وہی ہے جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔ پس اس مسئلہ کو باب اجارۃ العبد میں لانے کی کوئی خاص وجہ ظاہر نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ اس باب میں تو انہیں احکام کا ذکر مناسب ہے جن کا غلام کے ساتھ کوئی اختصاص ہے۔ ورنہ ظاہر ہے کہ ابواب سابقہ میں جو احکام گزرے ہیں ان میں سے بہت سے احکام ایسے ہیں جو حر وعبد میں مشترک ہیں۔
ممکن ہے کوئی یہ کہے کہ چونکہ آزاد کی بہ نسبت غلام کا اجیر ہونا زیادہ تر ہوتا ہے اس لئے اکثری وقوع کا لحاظ کر کے اس باب میں ذکر کر دیا۔ لیکن یہ کہنا اس لئے صحیح نہیں کہ اکثریت ناقابل تسلیم ہے کیونکہ غلام کی بہ نسبت آزاد کا اجیر ہونا ظاہر تر ہے اس لئے کہ ایک تو آزاد شخص کو تصرفات میں استقلال حاصل ہے۔ دوسرے یہ کہ اپنی ذات پر اور اپنے اہل و عیال پر خرچ کرنے کی احتیاج بھی غلام کی بہ نسبت آزاد کو زیادہ ہوتی ہے۔
From the author of Hidayah, it is not a hypothetical case; rather it is the statement of the lessee and the lam is for covenant, as if the lessor said to the lessee: 'I hired my servant for these two months for four (dirhams) and one month for five.' In response, the lessee said: 'I hired for these two months, one month for four and one month for five.' So 'these two months' refers to the indefinite months included in the lessor's offer, so the indefiniteness remains and the mentioned explanation becomes direct. But the author of Nata'ij says that the mentioned objection is also baseless and the mentioned answer is also useless. The objection is baseless because the mentioned explanation does not depend on the indefiniteness of the two months; rather, it is achieved by the indefinite month in 'a month for four and a month for five.' And the mentioned answer is useless because in the book 'these two months' if it is the lessee's statement, then the author of Hidayah's phrase 'and whoever hires a slave' would not be appropriate; rather, it would be more appropriate to make 'slave' definite instead of making 'two months' definite. Because from this it becomes known that the lam being for covenant in the lessee's statement can only be conceived when the lessor's speech precedes the lessee's speech in the contract, whereas this is not necessary; rather, whichever of the two contracting parties speaks first, his speech becomes the offer, and when the other accepts, the contract becomes binding. Moreover, it is very possible that the author of Hidayah, contrary to common books, brought 'these two months' as definite so that it becomes known that making 'two months' definite does not change the ruling of the case; rather, in this ruling, both definiteness and indefiniteness of 'two months' are equal, since in 'a month for four and a month for five' the word 'month' is indefinite. Warning: The ruling mentioned for this case is not specific to the case where the hired person is a slave; rather, if the hired person is a free person, the same ruling applies, and the proof is exactly the same as mentioned in the book. Therefore, there is no specific reason for bringing this case in the chapter of hiring a slave, because in this chapter it is appropriate to mention only those rulings that are specific to a slave. Otherwise, it is obvious that among the rulings passed in previous chapters, many rulings are common between free and slave. Someone might say that because a slave is hired more often than a free person, considering the frequency of occurrence, it was mentioned in this chapter. But this statement is not correct because the frequency is not acceptable; hiring a free person is more apparent than hiring a slave, because firstly, a free person has independence in transactions, and secondly, his need to spend on himself and his family is greater than that of a slave.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary (hashiya) on Al-Hidayah. The commentator questions the author of Al-Hidayah's placement of a specific case in the chapter on hiring a slave ('Ijara al-Abd'). The case involves a dispute over the wording of an offer and acceptance. The objection from the author of Nata'ij is analyzed. The commentator ultimately concludes that the ruling applies equally to free persons, so the chapter placement is not logically necessary; the author of Hidayah may have included it here due to common occurrence, but this reasoning is weak. The passage demonstrates the thoroughness of Hanafi textual criticism.

Key Terms
تنکیر (tankīr): The state of being indefinite (nakira); here applied to 'shahr' (month).
تعریف و تنکیر (taʿrīf wa tankīr): Definiteness and indefiniteness; the commentator argues both yield the same legal effect in this ruling.
لام برائے عہد (lām barā-ye ʿahd): The letter 'lam' used to indicate a previously mentioned specific entity (covenantal lam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject the 'common occurrence' justification for placing the case in the chapter on hiring a slave?
A) Because common occurrence is not a valid basis for chapter placement in fiqh works.
B) Because hiring free persons is actually more common than hiring slaves.
C) Because the ruling only applies to free persons.
D) Because the author of Nata'ij disproved the justification.

Key Takeaway
Chapter placement in a fiqh text does not restrict a ruling's applicability; the ruling's proof determines its scope, and it may apply beyond the chapter's specific subject.

Ruling on Dispute over Slave's Condition at Hire
Ruling on acceptance of statements based on slave's condition at return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of accepting statements based on the slave's condition at return and explain why the current state (hal) serves only as a weight (murajjih), not as definitive proof.

Core Idea
The slave's condition at return determines whose word is taken, using the current state as a tiebreaker.

When a hired slave is returned at the end of the term, a dispute often arises: did the condition (sickness or running away) exist from the start or arise later? The Hanafi school provides a practical ruling based on the observable condition at the moment of return. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its proof through qiyas on the water mill case, and the subtle role of the current state (hal) as a mere weight (murajjih) rather than a definitive proof.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Identify the two possible states of the slave at return: sick/runaway vs healthy. Note the different rulings for each.
The ruling flips depending on the observed condition.
2
Locate the core legal principle
The passage states the ruling is based on the current condition giving weight to one party's statement. Understand the concept of hal as murajjih.
Hal is not a proof (hujja) but a weight in a probable dispute.
3
Examine the qiyas (analogy)
The origin of this ruling is the dispute over the water mill: the flow or stoppage of water indicates the state before the dispute. See how the same logic applies here.
Qiyas is on the case of 'jaryan ma' al-tahuna'.
4
Address the potential objection
The commentary raises an objection: hal is normally a repeller (dafi') of entitlement, but here it seems to create entitlement. Understand the resolution: hal only weighs the conflicting statements; entitlement comes from the contract.
The objection is resolved by clarifying hal is a murajjih, not a cause.
5
Confirm the unanimous Hanafi position
The three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on this ruling. Note that other schools may differ.
Intra-Hanafi unanimity strengthens the position.

زید نے ایک ماہ کے لئے غلام اجرت پر لیا۔ اور شروع ماہ میں اس پر قبضہ کر لیا اس کے بعد اختتام ماہ پر کہا کہ یہ غلام شروع میں بھاگ گیا یا بیمار ہوگیا تھا۔ موجد (آقا) نے اس کا انکار کیا اور کہا کہ ایسا نہیں ہوا بلکہ وہ تو ابھی تیرے آنے سے کچھ پہلے بھا گا یا بیمار ہوا ہے تو اس صورت میں حال کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ یعنی اگر بوقت منازعت و خصومت غلام بھا گا ہوا ہو۔ یا بیمار ہو تو مستاجر کا قول اس کی قسم کے ساتھ معتبر ہوگا اور اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر وہ غلام کو اس حالت میں تندرست لایا ہو تو موجر کا قول مقبول ہو گا۔ آئمہ ثلاثہ کے یہاں بھی یہی حکم ۔ قوله لا نهما اختلفا ... الخ حکم مذکور کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ موجر ومستاجر دونوں نے ایک امر حتمل میں اختلاف کیا ہے تو موجودہ حالت سے ترجیح دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ ایسی حالت پہلے سے قائم تھی ۔ اس پر یہ اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ حال ہمارے یہاں دافع استحقاق ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موجب استحقاق جیسا کہ اصول سے معلوم ہے اور جب مستاجر غلام کو اس حالت میں لایا کہ وہ تندرست ہے اور اس صورت میں موجر کا قول معتبر ہوا یہاں تک کہ موجر مستحق اجرت ہوا۔ تو حال دافع نہ ہوا بلکہ موجب استحقاق ہو گیا وھو تصلح سے اس کا جواب ہے کہ حال گوفی نفسہ صالح حجت نہیں۔ یعنی وہ کسی امر کو ثابت کرنے کے لائق نہیں تاہم وہ مرجج ہونے کے لائق ہے اور یہاں موجب استحقاق اجرت تو عقد اجارہ ہے مدت کے اندر غلام کی سپردگی کے ساتھ۔ لیکن اس کے سقوط کا موجب امر کوئی پیش آیا ہے یا نہیں؟ اس کے بارے میں مستاجر و موجر کے کلام میں تعارض ہے تو حال کو کلام موجر کے لئے مرج بنایا گیا۔ موجب استحقاق نہیں بنایا گیا
Whoever hires a slave for a month for one dirham, and takes possession of him at the beginning of the month, then comes at the end of the month while he is a runaway or sick, and the lessee says: 'He ran away or fell sick when I took him,' and the master says: 'That did not happen except an hour before you came,' then the lessee's statement is accepted. But if he brings him while he is healthy, then the lessor's statement is accepted. Because they have disputed in a probable matter, so it is given weight by the current state (hal), as it is evidence that such state existed before, and the current state is suitable as a weight (murajjih), even if it is not sufficient as proof in itself. Its origin is the dispute regarding the flow of water of the mill and its stoppage. Translation: Someone took a slave on hire for one dirham monthly and took possession of him at the beginning of the month. Then at the end of the month, he came while the slave was a runaway or sick. The lessee said: 'Since I took him, he ran away or fell sick at that time.' The master said: 'That did not happen except shortly before you came.' Then the lessee's statement will be accepted. But if he brought the slave healthy, then the lessor's statement will be accepted. Because both have disputed in a probable matter, so preference is given based on the current state (hal). Because it is evidence that such state existed before, and the present state can be a weight (murajjih), although it cannot be a proof in itself. Its origin is the dispute regarding the flow of water of the mill and its stoppage. Commentary: His saying 'Whoever hires a slave...' etc. Zaid hired a slave for one month. He took possession at the beginning of the month. Then at the end of the month, he said that this slave ran away or fell sick at the beginning. The master (owner) denied this and said that it happened only a little before you came. In this case, the current state is made the basis. That is, if at the time of dispute the slave is found to be a runaway or sick, then the lessee's statement along with his oath will be accepted, and the rent will not be obligatory. And if he brings the slave healthy, then the lessor's statement will be accepted. The three Imams also hold the same ruling. His saying 'Because they have disputed...' etc. The reason for the mentioned ruling is that both the lessor and lessee have disputed in a probable matter, so preference is given by the existing state. Because it is evidence that such a state existed before. An objection arises: In our school, the current state (hal) is a repeller of entitlement (dafi' al-istihqaq), not a provoker of entitlement (mujib al-istihqaq), as known from principles. And when the lessee brings the slave healthy, and in that case the lessor's statement is accepted, so much so that the lessor becomes entitled to the rent, then the current state did not repel but rather provoked entitlement. The answer to this is that the current state, although in itself is not suitable as proof (hujja), i.e., it is not fit to establish something, nevertheless it is fit to be a weight (murajjih). And here the cause of entitlement to rent is the contract of hire along with the delivery of the slave within the term. But whether something happened that causes its lapse – in this matter the statements of the lessee and lessor conflict. So the current state is made a weight for the lessor's statement; it is not made a cause of entitlement.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on a dispute between a hirer (musta'jir) and owner (mu'ajjir) of a slave regarding the slave's condition at the time of hire. The ruling is based on the observable condition of the slave at the end of the term. If the slave is brought back in a problematic state (runaway or sick), the hirer's claim that the condition existed from the start is accepted (with his oath), and no rent is due. If the slave is brought back healthy, the owner's claim that the condition arose later is accepted, and rent is due. The reasoning is that the current condition (hal) serves as a weight (murajjih) to prefer one party's statement, even though it is not a definitive proof. The commentary addresses a potential objection that the current state here seems to create entitlement (instead of repelling it), but explains that it only acts as a weight, not as the source of entitlement.

Key Terms
مستاجر (musta'jir): The person who hires (the lessee).
موجر (mu'jir): The person who gives on hire (the lessor/owner).
حال (ḥāl): The current observable state of the slave at the time of dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The lessor's statement, because he is the owner.
B) The lessee's statement, based on the current condition.
C) No statement is accepted; an expert witness is needed.
D) The slave's statement.

Key Takeaway
The observable condition of a hired item at the end of the term serves as a weight (murajjih) to accept the statement of the party whose claim aligns with that condition.

Dispute between Tailor/Dyer and Customer on Work Specs
Ruling on whose word is accepted when artisan and customer differ on ordered specifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disputes between artisan and customer regarding work specifications, explain the qiyas jali proof, and apply the customer's options (daman or ajr al-mithl).

Core Idea
In disputes over work instructions, the customer's word is accepted because permission originates from him.

This passage from Kitab al-Ijarat addresses a common conflict: the artisan claims one set of instructions, the customer claims another. The Hanafi school establishes a clear procedural rule: the customer's version is believed, supported by an oath, and the artisan becomes liable. The legal reasoning is a qiyas jali from the case of total denial of permission. Understanding this ruling helps in resolving everyday contractual disputes in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenarios
Note the two examples: tailor (cloak vs shirt) and dyer (red vs yellow). Both involve disagreement on the specific instructions given.
The dispute is always about the description of the order, not about the existence of the order itself.
2
State the ruling
The text says 'al-qawlu li-sahib al-thawb' – the customer's statement is accepted. The customer must take an oath because he is denying something that would be binding if admitted.
The oath is required even though his word is accepted.
3
Understand the proof (qiyas jali)
The argument: if the customer denied giving any permission at all, his word would be accepted. By a stronger reason, his word should be accepted when he denies a specific description of the permission. Common illa: permission originates from the customer.
This is a qiyas jali (obvious analogy) because the underlying reason is clear.
4
Determine the consequences after oath
The customer has two options: (1) make the artisan liable (daman) – either take the garment with compensation for damages or take the value of the cloth, or (2) accept the work and pay the fair wage (ajr al-mithl) not exceeding the named wage. For the dyer, some copies add liability for the increase in value due to dyeing.
The dyer is treated like a usurper (ghasib) because he acted without valid authorization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف
ترجمہ یہ باب موجر و مستاجر کے اختلاف کے بیان میں ہے
جب خیاط اور رب الثوب کا اختلاف ہو جائے تو قول کس کا معتبر ہوگا
قال واذا اختلف الخياط ورب الثوب فقال رب الثوب امرتک ان تعمله قباء وقال الخياط قميصا أو قال صاحب الثوب للصباغ امرتک ان تصبغه احمر قصبغته اصفر وقال الصباغ لا بل امرتني اصفر فالقول لصاحب الثوب لان الاذن يستفاد من جهته الا ترى انه لو انكر اصل الاذن كان القول قوله فكذا اذا انكر صفته لكن يحلف لانه اذكر شيئا لو اقر به لزمه قال واذا حلف فالخياط ضامن ومعناه مامر من قبل انه بالخيار ان شاء ضمنه وان شاء اخذه واعطاه اجر مثله وكذا يخير في مسئلة الصبغ اذا خلف ان شاء ضمنه قيمة الثوب ابيض قيمة الثوب الابيض و ان شاء اخذ الثوب واعطاه اجر مثله لا يجاوز به المسمى وذكر فى بعض النسخ يضمنه ما زاد الصبغ فيه لانه بمنزلة الغاصب
Chapter of Dispute. Translation: This chapter is about the dispute between lessor and lessee. When the tailor and the cloth owner differ, whose statement is accepted? He said: If the tailor and the cloth owner differ, and the cloth owner said: 'I ordered you to make it a cloak (qaba'),' and the tailor said: 'A shirt (qamis),' or the cloth owner said to the dyer: 'I ordered you to dye it red, and you dyed it yellow,' and the dyer said: 'No, but you ordered me yellow,' then the statement is that of the cloth owner, because permission is obtained from him. Do you not see that if he denied the permission entirely, his statement would be accepted? So likewise if he denies its description. But he takes an oath, because he is denying something which, if he admitted it, would be binding on him. He said: And if he takes an oath, then the tailor is liable. And its meaning has passed previously: that he has the option: if he wishes, he can make him liable (for compensation), or if he wishes, he can take the garment and give him its fair wage. Similarly, in the dyeing case, when he takes an oath, he has the choice: if he wishes, he can make him liable for the value of the white cloth, or if he wishes, he can take the cloth and give him its fair wage, not exceeding the named wage. And it is mentioned in some copies: he is liable for the increase (in value) caused by the dye, because he is like a usurper (ghasib).
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Bab al-Ikhtilaf (Chapter of Dispute) from Kitab al-Ijarat. It addresses cases where the artisan (tailor or dyer) and the customer disagree on the specific instructions given. The ruling is consistent: the customer's (cloth owner's) word is accepted in both scenarios. The proof is a qiyas jali (obvious analogy): just as the customer's word is accepted if he denies giving any permission (اذن) at all, his word is also accepted if he denies the specific description of the permission he claims to have given. This is because the permission originates from the customer, and he is the one who knows best what he instructed. The customer must take an oath. The consequences: if the customer swears, the artisan becomes liable. The customer has a choice: either to take compensation (full value of the cloth in the case of tailoring or the value of undyed cloth in dyeing) or to take the work as delivered and pay the fair wage (ajr al-mithl), which cannot exceed the named wage. Some copies add that the dyer is liable for any increase in value caused by the dye because he acted without authorization, making him akin to a usurper (ghasib).

Key Terms
اذن (idhn): Permission or authorization given by the customer to the artisan to perform work.
ضامن (dhamin): Liable for compensation; here the artisan is liable if he performs work contrary to the customer's instructions.
اجر مثل (ajr al-mithl): Fair wage for similar work without prior agreement, cannot exceed the named wage (musamma).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The tailor's statement.
B) The cloth owner's statement.
C) Both must agree on a new order.
D) The judge decides based on local custom.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over work specifications, the customer's sworn word prevails because permission originates from him, and the artisan becomes liable.

Dispute on Free vs Paid Work: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Whose Word is Accepted
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dispute resolution regarding wages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the dispute between customer and artisan, and explain the tarjih (preference) for Abu Hanifa's view.

Core Idea
In a wage dispute, the customer's word is accepted unless custom or public indication suggests a wage.

When a customer and an artisan disagree over whether work was done for free or for a wage, whose statement is accepted? This passage from al-Hidayah presents the internal Hanafi disagreement on this procedural question. Abu Hanifa's general principle faces two exceptions proposed by his disciples based on custom and apparent circumstances. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how evidence and presumption work in Hanafi fiqh. We will examine each position, its basis, and why the text ultimately prefers the strict qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the procedural principle
Recognize that the core issue is a disagreement over whether work was for free or for wage. The general principle in Hanafi law is 'al-qawlu li al-munkir' (the denier's word is accepted). The customer denies any obligation; the artisan claims a wage. So the default is the customer's word.
This principle is foundational in all disputes over debts and obligations.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and its dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that the customer's word is always accepted because he is the denier. The dalil is the principle itself, which is based on the maxim that the burden of proof is on the claimant, and the denier's oath suffices.
This is considered qiyas (strict analogy) in the text.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's exception based on custom
Abu Yusuf says: if the customer is a habitual customer (harif) of the artisan, then the artisan's claim for wage is accepted. His reasoning is that their established custom of dealing indicates that work is done for wage. This is an istihsan based on 'urf (custom).
The term 'harif' implies a regular dealing relationship.
4
Analyze Muhammad's exception based on public indication
Muhammad says: if the artisan is known for doing such work for wage (e.g., has a shop open for that purpose), then his statement is accepted. The public nature of his trade creates a presumption that the work is paid. This is also istihsan, but based on apparent circumstances (zahir).
This exception does not require a prior relationship.
5
Understand the tarjih and the response to istihsan
The text states that the qiyas is with Abu Hanifa. It then answers the istihsan of the Sahibayn by saying that the apparent circumstance (zahir) is used for repelling (daf') claims, not for establishing entitlement (istihqaq). Therefore, the default rule prevails. The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's.
This illustrates the hierarchy: qiyas over istihsan unless the istihsan is stronger, but here it is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قال صاحب الثوب عملته لي بغير اجر وقال الصانع باجر فالقول قول صاحب الثوب لانه ينكر تقوم عمله اذهو يتقوم بالعقد وينكر الضمان والصانع يدعيه والقول قول المنكر وقال ابويوسف ان كان الرجل حريفا له اى خليطا له فله الاجر والا فلا لان سبق ما بينهما يعين جهة الطلب باجر جريا على معتادهما وقال محمد ان كان الصانع معروفا بهذه الصنعة بالاجر فالقول قوله لانه لما فتح الحانوت لاجله جرى ذالك مجرى التنصيص على الاجر اعتبارا للظاهر والقياس ما قاله ابو حنيفة لانه منكر والجواب عن استحسانهما ان الظاهر للدفع والحاجة ههنا الى الاستحقاق والله اعلم
And if the cloth owner says: 'You did the work for me without wage,' and the artisan says: 'With wage,' then the statement is that of the cloth owner, because he denies that his work is compensable, for work is compensated by contract, and he denies liability, while the artisan claims it, and the statement of the denier (al-munkir) is accepted. Abu Yusuf said: If the man is a habitual customer (harif) of his, i.e., a regular associate, then he gets wage; otherwise not, because their past dealing indicates the basis of claim for wage, in accordance with their custom. Muhammad said: If the artisan is known for this work for wage, then his statement is accepted, because when he opened the shop for that purpose, this is like specifying wage, considering the apparent circumstance. And the qiyas (analogy) is what Abu Hanifa said, because he is the denier. The answer to their istihsan is that the apparent circumstance (zahir) is for repelling (daf'), and here the need is for entitlement (istihqaq). And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the dispute between a customer and an artisan about whether the work was to be free or for a wage. The general principle from Abu Hanifa is that the customer's word is accepted as the denier (al-munkir), because the artisan claims a liability (wage) and the customer denies it. Abu Yusuf introduces an exception based on custom: if the artisan is a regular customer (harif) of the artisan, then the artisan's claim for wage is accepted, because their established dealing implies a wage. Muhammad al-Shaybani goes further: if the artisan is generally known for doing such work for a wage (e.g., a tailor who opens shop for that purpose), then his word is accepted, because the visible circumstances (zahir) suggest a wage. The text then states that the qiyas (strict analogy) supports Abu Hanifa's view: the principle that the denier's word is accepted. The response to the istihsan of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is that the apparent circumstance (zahir) serves to repel (daf') a claim, but here the artisan is trying to establish entitlement (istihqaq). The correct position in the Hidayah is that the mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa, though the other views are mentioned for completeness. The passage concludes with 'Allah knows best.'

Key Terms
منكر (munkir): The party who denies a claim; in Hanafi procedural law, the denier's statement is generally accepted with oath.
حريف (harif): A regular or habitual customer (khalt/associate) to whom the artisan provides services customarily.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable result based on custom, necessity, or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, under what condition does the artisan's claim for wage prevail?
A) If the artisan is known for working for wage.
B) If the customer is a regular (harif) of the artisan.
C) If the artisan has a shop sign.
D) If the customer admits part of the work.

Key Takeaway
In a dispute over wages, the Hanafi default favors the denier (customer), but custom and public indication create exceptions; Abu Hanifa's view remains the relied-upon position.

Dispute Over Free or Paid Work: Whose Word is Taken?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on burden of proof in work-for-hire claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whose statement is accepted in a dispute over free vs. paid work, and explain the tarjih (preferred view) among them.

Core Idea
The denier's word is taken — unless custom or apparent state shifts the burden.

When an artisan claims he worked for wages and the owner insists it was volunteer, who is believed? Imam Abu Hanifa applies the general principle that the denier (owner) is credited. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, introduce exceptions based on custom and apparent state. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the school's final ruling.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify the default Hanafi position: the owner's word is taken because he is the denier (munkir) of the work's monetary value and liability.
This is based on the principle 'al-qawl li al-munkir'.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's exceptions
Abu Yusuf: if the owner is a regular customer (hiraf), the artisan gets the wage. Muhammad: if the artisan is known to work for hire, his word is taken.
These are istihsan (equity-based) departures from the qiyas.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proofs
Each uses a different basis: Abu Yusuf relies on custom (urf) between the parties; Muhammad relies on the apparent state (zahir al-hal) of the artisan's profession.
Their evidence is derived from practical reasoning, not explicit texts.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The response to both istihsan claims is that the apparent state is sufficient for defense (daf‘) but not for establishing entitlement (istihqaq). The burden of proof remains on the claimant.
This rebuttal preserves the default rule.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's view. The artisan must prove the existence of a contract for hire.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قال صاحب الثوب عملته لي بغير اجر وقال الصانع باجر فالقول قول صاحب الثوب لانه ينكر تقوم عمله اذهو يتقوم بالعقد وينكر الضمان والصانع يدعيه والقول قول المنكر وقال ابويوسف ان كان الرجل حريفا له اى خليطا له فله الاجر والا فلا لان سبق ما بينهما يعين جهة الطلب باجر جريا على معتادهما وقال محمد ان كان الصانع معروفا بهذه الصنعة بالاجر فالقول قوله لانه لما فتح الحانوت لاجله جرى ذالك مجرى التنصيص على الاجر اعتبارا للظاهر والقياس ما قاله ابو حنيفة لانه منكر والجواب عن استحسانهما ان الظاهر للدفع والحاجة ههنا الى الاستحقاق والله اعلم
And if the owner of the cloth says 'You did it for me without wage' and the artisan says 'With wage' — then the statement is that of the owner of the cloth, because he denies the valuation of his work? Indeed it is valued by contract, and he denies liability, while the artisan claims it. And the statement is that of the denier. And Abu Yusuf said: If the man is a regular customer (hiraf) i.e., an associate of his, then he has the wage; otherwise not, because the prior dealings between them determine the direction of the claim for wage, according to their custom. And Muhammad said: If the artisan is known for this craft with wage, then his statement is accepted, because when he opened the shop for that purpose, that takes the place of explicit stipulation for wage, considering the apparent. And the analogy is what Abu Hanifa said, because he is the denier. And the response to their istihsan is that the apparent is for repelling, and here the need is for entitlement. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents a second type of dispute: whether work was done for free or for hire. The Hanafi school has varying views. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the owner's word is taken because he is the denier: he denies that the work has any monetary value (since valuation occurs through contract) and denies any liability to pay. The artisan is the claimant, so the burden of proof is on him. This is the qiyas (analogical) position. Imam Abu Yusuf introduces an istihsan: if the owner is a regular customer (hiraf) of the artisan, then the artisan is entitled to the wage, because their established course of dealing indicates that transactions are for hire. Imam Muhammad also applies istihsan: if the artisan is well-known for working for hire in that trade (e.g., opening a shop), then the apparent state indicates that he works for wage, so his word is taken. The response to both istihsan arguments is that the apparent state (zahir) is sufficient for defense (daf‘) but not for establishing entitlement (istihqaq). The artisan needs to prove his right, so the analogy of Abu Hanifa remains the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
تقوم (taqawwum): being of monetary value; the work's property of being compensable by money.
منكر (munkir): denier; the party who denies the claim of the other.
حريف (hiraf): regular customer; one who frequently does business with the artisan.
صنعة (san‘ah): craft, trade, profession (of the artisan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, whose statement is taken when the owner claims work was free and the artisan claims it was for hire?
A) The artisan's statement
B) The owner's statement
C) Both must take oaths
D) The one with witnesses

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the owner's word is taken in a dispute over free vs. paid work, with the artisan bearing the burden of proof; the exceptions of the Sahibayn are not the operative ruling.

Whose Word Prevails? The Owner-Craftsman Wage Dispute in Hanafi Fiqh
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wage disputes in ijara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on wage disputes, apply the qiyas and istihsan reasoning, and identify the mufta bihi in later fatwa practice.

Core Idea
The denier's word prevails, but custom or public practice can shift the burden.

When an owner and a craftsman disagree on whether the work was for wages or gratis, whose word is accepted? This passage from the Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa sticks to the principle that the denier's word is accepted, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, introduce exceptions based on custom (urf) and apparent state (zahir al-hal). The discussion also includes inter-madhhab comparisons and later fatwa preferences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and claim
Determine who is the mudda'i (claimant) and who is the munkir (denier) in each scenario. The owner denies the contract or the obligation to pay; the craftsman claims wages.
In Hanafi procedure, the munkir's word is accepted with an oath.
2
State the base ruling (qiyas)
Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that the owner's word is always accepted, based on the principle that the denier's statement prevails. This is the qiyas (analogy) to other denial cases.
This is the default rule.
3
Understand the istihsan of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf considers prior dealing between the parties; Muhammad considers whether the craftsman runs a public shop. Both use istihsan because the apparent state (zahir al-hal) suggests a wage contract.
Istihsan here is a departure from qiyas due to custom or necessity.
4
Analyze the rebuttal: daf‘ vs. istihqaq
The commentary explains that the apparent state only suffices for daf‘ (preventing liability) but not for istihqaq (establishing a right). For entitlement, proper evidence (shahada) is required.
This distinction is key to understanding why the Sahibayn's view is not the default qiyas.
5
Note the later fatwa variation
Some sources (e.g., al-Durr al-Mukhtar) give fatwa on Abu Hanifa's view, while others (al-Tabyin, Shaykh al-Islam) follow Muhammad's view. The mufti may choose based on circumstances.
This reflects the flexibility within the Hanafi school.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
كتاب الاجارات
کپڑے کے مالک کا قول معتبر ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کے کام کے قیمتی ہو جانے کا منکر ہے اس لئے کہ قیمتی ہونا عقد سے ہوتا ہے۔ نیز وہ عمان کا بھی منکر ہے اور کاریگر دونوں کا مدعی ہے اور قول منکر ہی کا مقبول ہوتا ہے امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر وہ شخص کا ریگر کا حریف و خلیط ہو تو اس کے لئے اجرت ہوگی ورنہ نہیں کیونکہ ان کا سابقہ باہمی تعامل اجرت کے ساتھ طلب کی جہت کو معین کرتا ہے ان کے معمول کے مطابق ۔ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کاریگر اس پیشہ میں اجرت پر کام کرنے کے ساتھ مشہور ہو تو اس کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جب اس نے دکان اس لئے کھولی ہے تو یہ اجرت پر تصریح کے قائم مقام ہو گیا ظاہر کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور قیاس وہ ہے جو امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کیونکہ وہ منکر ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے استحسان کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ظاہر دفع کے لئے ہوتا ہے اور یہاں ضرورت استحقاق کی ہے۔
تشریح قوله باب ... الخ - اتفاق متعاقدین جو اصل ہے اس کے احکام سے فراغت کے بعد اختلاف متعاقدین کے احکام بیان کر رہے ہیں جو فرع ہے۔ اذا الاختلاف انما یکون بعارض۔
قوله واذا اختلف ... الخ - مالک نے درزی سے کہا کہ میں نے قباء سینے کے لئے کہا تھا تو نے قمیص سی دی۔ یا رنگریز سے کہا کہ میں نے کپڑا سرخ رنگنے کے لئے کہا تو نے زرد رنگ دیا ۔ اجیر کہتا ہے کہ جیسا تو نے کہا تھا میں نے ویسا ہی کیا ہے تو مالک کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ امام مالک وشافعی اور ابو ثور بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں اس لئے کہ اجیر کو مل کی اجازت کا ثبوت مالک کی جانب سے ہوتا ہے حتی کہ اگر وہ اصل اجازت ہی کا انکار کر دے تو اسی کا قول قبول ہوتا ہے تو صفت اجازت میں بھی اسی کا قول قبول ہوگا ۔ امام احمد ابن ابی لیٹی اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی کے نزدیک اجیر کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ اور بعض شوافع نے ایک تیسرا قول یہ بھی ذکر کیا ہے کہ متبایمان کی طرح وہ دونوں بھی قسم کھائیں گے اور تحالف کے بعد اجیر سے ضمان اور مالک سے اجرت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
قوله عملته لی الخ - مالک نے کہا کہ تو نے مجھے یہ کام مفت کر دیا ہے۔ اجیر کہتا ہے نہیں اجرت پر کیا ہے تو امام ابو حنیفہ اور بعض شوافع کے نزدیک مالک کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کے کام کے قیمتی ہو جانے سے منکر ہے اس لئے کہ تقویم بذریعہ عقد ہوگا اور یہاں عقد ہی نہیں ہے جب کہ وہ بلا اجرت عمل کا مدعی ہے اور عمل بلا اجرت اعانت ہوتی ہے نیز مالک ضمان یعنی وجوب اجر کا بھی منکر ہے۔ اور کاریگر ان دونوں باتوں کا مدعی ہے اور قول منکر ہی کا مقبول ہوتا ہے۔ پس کاریگر کو چاہیے۔ کہ وہ اپنے دعوئی پر بعینہ قائم کرے۔ امام شافعی کے یہاں کا ریگر ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ قوله وقال ابو يوسف الخ - امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ مالک اگر کاریگر کا حریف وخلیط ہو یعنی ان میں لین دین اور اجرت کے ساتھ معاملہ ہوتا رہا ہو تو اجرت ملے گی ورنہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ سابق میں جو ان کے درمیان معاملہ تھا وہ اس امر کا مؤید ہے کہ یہ معاملہ بھی ان کے معمول کے مطابق اجرت ہی پر واقع ہوا ہے۔ امام محمد، امام مالک اور امام احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کاریگر اس پیشہ کی دکان کھولے ہوئے ہو اور اجرت پر کام کرنے میں مشہور ہو تو اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا ورنہ مالک کا اس لئے کہ جب اس نے دکان اس کام کے لئے کھولی ہے تو بنظر ظاہر یہ اجرت پر تصریح کے قائم مقام ہے لیکن قیاس وہی ہے جو امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا ۔ کیونکہ مالک منکر ہے اور صاحبین کے استحسان کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ظاہر حال صرف دفعیہ کے لئے کافی ہوتا ہے اس سے استحقاق ثابت نہیں ہوتا ۔ اور یہاں کا ریگر کو اپنا استحقاق ثابت کرنے کی ضرورت ہے تو ایسی دلیل لانا چاہئیے جس سے استحقاق ثابت ہوتا ہے اور وہ شرعی گواہی ہے ۔
فائده . در مختار میں ہے کہ فتویٰ امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول پر ہے اور تبیین و تنویر، محیط، وشرح شاہان وغیرہ میں ہے کہ فتویٰ امام محمد کے قول پر ہے نہایہ، کفایہ ، غایہ میں شیخ الاسلام کا فتویٰ بھی امام محمد کے قول پر منقول ہے۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah volume 12. Book of Ijarat. The word of the owner of the cloth will be accepted. Because he denies that his work has become valuable, since valuation occurs through the contract. Also he denies the wage, and the craftsman claims both, and the word of the denier is accepted. Imam Abu Yusuf says: If the person is a regular dealing partner of the craftsman, then he will get wages, otherwise not, because their prior mutual dealing determines the direction of demand according to their custom. Imam Muhammad says: If the craftsman is famous in this profession for working for wages, then his word will be accepted. Because when he opened a shop for that purpose, this takes the place of explicit statement of wages, considering the apparent state. And the analogy (qiyas) is what Imam Abu Hanifa said, because he (the owner) is the denier. The answer to the istihsan of the two companions is that the apparent state is for prevention (daf'), and here the need is for entitlement (istihqaq).
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute and also an inter-madhhab discussion regarding a dispute between an owner and a craftsman (like a tailor or dyer) about the terms of work. The text begins by stating the general rule: the owner's word is accepted because he denies the existence of a contract that would make the work valuable, and the craftsman claims both the contract and the wage. Since the owner is the denier of the claim, his statement is taken on oath. Abu Yusuf then adds a condition: if the owner and craftsman have a prior dealing relationship (khaleet or hareef), then the craftsman's statement is accepted due to the custom of their transactions. Muhammad al-Shaybani further refines: if the craftsman runs a public shop in that trade and is known to work for wages, his word is accepted because the shop in itself implies a contract for hire. However, the commentary notes that the actual qiyas (analogy) is with Abu Hanifa's position, and the istihsan of the two companions is answered by the principle that the apparent state (zahir al-hal) is only sufficient for avoiding liability (daf'), not for establishing a right (istihqaq). For the latter, proper evidence (shari' shahada) is needed. The passage then discusses a similar scenario where the owner claims the work was done for free (tabarru'), while the craftsman claims it was for wages. The same rule applies: the owner's word is accepted. Other schools like Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Abu Thawr agree with the Hanafi position. However, Imam Ahmad and some Hanbalis prefer the craftsman's word. A third view among Shafi'is suggests mutual oaths (tahlif) similar to the case of two parties in a contract dispute. The benefit (fa'ida) at the end records a difference in later fatwa practice: al-Mukhtar leans toward Abu Hanifa, but other sources like al-Tabyin, al-Muhit, and the Shaykh al-Islam's fatwa (in al-Nihaya, al-Kifaya, al-Ghaya) are reported to follow Imam Muhammad's position.

Key Terms
منکر (munkir): The party who denies the claim of the other
مدعی (mudda'i): The party who makes a claim that contradicts the apparent state
استحسان (istihsan): Preference for a ruling due to custom or necessity over strict qiyas
دفع (daf'): Prevention of liability; a lower threshold than establishing a right
استحقاق (istihqaq): Entitlement to a right; requires stronger evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute between a cloth owner and a tailor about wages, under Imam Abu Hanifa's view, whose word is accepted?
A) The tailor's word
B) The owner's word
C) Both swear oaths and the contract is void
D) The court decides

Key Takeaway
The default rule favors the denier (owner), but Hanafi law allows istihsan-based exceptions when custom or public practice indicates a wage contract, and fatwa practice may follow either view.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Khiyar al-Ayb in Ijarah Contracts
Ruling with proof on khiyar al-ayb in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ayb in ijarah and apply the conditions that affect the option.

Core Idea
A lessee may rescind a rental if a defect harms dwelling, but using the property forfeits the option.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the Hidayah on the lessee's right to rescind a rental contract due to a defect. The text draws an analogy to sale and clarifies when the option is lost. Understanding this helps distinguish khiyar in ijarah from khiyar in sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The text states: if a lessee rents a house and finds a defect harmful for dwelling, he has the option to rescind. Note that the subject matter (manafi') is realized gradually.
The defect must be significant – one that normally affects dwelling.
2
Understand the analogy to sale
The ruling is derived by qiyas: as a buyer has khiyar al-ayb before delivery, so does a lessee. The illa is that the defect existed at contract time but is discovered after partial delivery of usufruct.
The hadith 'al-mushtari bil-khiyar idha wajada al-ayb' is the basis for the asl.
3
Trace loss of option by taking benefit
If the lessee uses the property after discovering the defect, he is deemed to have consented. Full rent becomes due, analogous to a buyer who uses a defective item.
Using property includes any usufruct, not just residence.
4
Trace loss of option by repair
If the lessor removes the defect before the lessee exercises the option, the cause (sabab) is eliminated, so no option remains.
The repair must actually eliminate the defect; if the defect persists, the option continues.
5
Note cross-madhhab agreement
The commentary notes that this ruling is agreed upon by Hanafis, Malik, Ahmad, and the preponderant Shafi'i view, indicating its strength.
This is a rare case of near-consensus on khiyar in ijarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب فسخ الاجارة
ترجمہ یہ باب فسخ اجارہ کے بیان میں ہے
کرایہ پر گھر لیا ایسا عیب پایا جور ہائش کے لئے نقصان دہ ہے مستاجر کو فسخ کا اختیار ہے
قال ومن استاجر دارا فوجد بها عيبا يضر بالسكنى فله الفسخ لان المعقود عليه المنافع وانها توجد شيئا فشيئا فكان هذا عيبا حادثا قبل القبض فيوجب الخيار كما فى البيع ثم المستاجر اذا استوفى المنفعة فقد رضى بالعيب فيلزمه جميع المبدل كما فى البيع وان فعل المواجر ما ازال به العيب فلا خيار للمستاجر
لزوال سببه
ترجمہ جس نے مکان اجارہ پر لیا پھر اس میں ایسا عیب پایا جو سکونت کو مضر ہے تو اس کو فسخ کا اختیار ہے۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ منافع ہیں جو تھوڑا تھوڑا کر کے پائے جاتے ہیں تو یہ قبضہ سے پہلے پیدا ہونے والا عیب ہوا۔ پس موجب خیار ہوگا۔ پھر جب مستاجر نے منفعت حاصل کر لی تو وہ عیب پر راضی ہو گیا۔ لہذا اس کو پورا عوض لازم ہوگا جیسے بیچ میں ہوتا ہے اور اگر موجر نے ایسی اصلاح کر دی جس سے عیب جاتا رہا تو مستاجر کو اختیار نہ ہوگا زوال سبب کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح .. قوله باب ... الخ - اس باب کو ابواب سابقہ سے مؤخر کرنے کی وجہ مناسبت بالکل ظاہر ہے اس لئے کہ فسخ عقد ثبوت عقد کے بعد ہی ہوتا ہے۔ فبا الضرورۃ ھو متاخر ۔
قوله ومن استاجر داراً .. الخ کسی نے ایک مکان اجارہ پر لیا۔ پھر اس میں ایسا عیب پایا جو ر ہائش کے لئے مضر ہے تو مستاجر کو فسخ اجارہ کا اختیار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ منافع ہیں اور وہ تھوڑا تھوڑا کر کے پائے جاتے ہیں۔ تو یہ عیب قبضہ سے قبل پیدا ہوا لہذا اس کو اختیار حاصل ہوگا ۔ جیسے بیع میں ہوتا ہے۔ پھر اگر مستاجر نے منفعت حاصل کر لی تو وہ عیب سے راضی ہو گیا۔ اس لئے احناف، امام مالک، امام احمد ، امام شافعی کے اظہر قول میں اس کے ذمہ پورا عوض لازم ہوگا جیسے بیج میں اگر مشتری عیب سے راضی ہو جائے تو پورا شمن واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر قبل از فسخ موجر نے ایسی اصلاح کر دی جس سے عیب جاتا رہا تو مستاجر کو فسخ کا اختیار نہیں رہے گا۔ کیونکہ اس کا سبب زائل ہو گیا۔
Chapter of Rescission of Ijarah. Translation: This chapter is about the rescission of ijarah. He rented a house, found a defect harmful for dwelling, the lessee has the option to rescind. He said: Whoever rents a house and finds in it a defect harmful for dwelling, he has the option to rescind, because the subject matter of the contract is the usufructs, and they are obtained little by little, so this is a defect occurring before delivery, thus it necessitates an option as in sale. Then if the lessee has taken the benefit, he has consented to the defect, so all the consideration becomes obligatory upon him as in sale. And if the lessor removes the defect, then there is no option for the lessee due to the removal of the cause. Translation: He who rented a house then found in it a defect harmful for dwelling, he has the option to rescind. Because the subject matter is usufructs, which are obtained little by little, so this is a defect occurring before taking possession, thus it gives an option as in sale. Then if the lessee has taken benefit, he has consented to the defect, so the full price becomes obligatory as in sale, and if the lessor makes a repair that removes the defect, the lessee has no option due to the removal of the cause. Commentary: The reason for placing this chapter after previous ones is obvious because rescission occurs only after the contract is concluded, so it is necessarily later. Then the commentary explains that the lessee has the option because the defect is considered to have occurred before delivery of the usufructs, analogous to sale. After taking benefit, consent is presumed, so full rent is due. The Hanafis, Malik, Ahmad, and the stronger view of Shafi'i agree that full consideration is due. If the lessor repairs before rescission, the option ceases.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning the option to rescind an ijarah contract due to a defect in the rented property. The key legal point is that the subject matter of ijarah is usufruct (manafi'), not the physical property itself. Usufructs are realized over time, so a defect existing at the time of contract but discovered later is analogized to a defect discovered before delivery in a sale contract. Therefore, the lessee has khiyar al-ayb (option for defect). However, if the lessee uses the property (takes benefit) after discovering the defect, he is deemed to have accepted it, and full rent is due. If the lessor rectifies the defect before the lessee exercises the option, the option is nullified. The commentary notes that this ruling is agreed upon by the Hanafis, Malik, Ahmad, and the preponderant view of Shafi'i. The text also provides a reason for placing this chapter after the previous ones: rescission logically comes after contract formation.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract
خیار (khiyar): Option or right to continue or rescind a contract
عیب (ayb): A defect that diminishes the value or benefit of the subject matter

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following does NOT cause the lessee to lose the option to rescind due to a defect?
A) The lessee uses the property for a month after discovering the defect
B) The lessor repairs the defect before the option is exercised
C) The lessee inspects the property but does not use it
D) The lessee notifies the lessor and demands a rent reduction

Key Takeaway
A lessee's right to rescind due to a defect is lost if he takes benefit after discovery or if the lessor repairs the defect before rescission.

Defect in Leased House and Right to Terminate
Ruling on termination of lease due to defect before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a tenant's option to terminate a lease due to a defect and apply the qiyas from sale to explain the reasoning.

Core Idea
A defect in a leased house before full possession gives the tenant an option to cancel, just as in sale.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school on defects in lease contracts. The text from al-Hidayah states that if a tenant finds a harmful defect in a rented house before fully taking possession, he has the right to cancel the lease. The reasoning is by qiyas (analogy) to a defect in a purchased item before delivery. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between situations where the tenant may or may not terminate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize the scenario: a tenant finds a defect harmful to habitation. The ruling is that the tenant has an option (khiyar) to cancel the lease.
The option is a right, not an obligation.
2
Locate the dalil and its type
The author uses qiyas (analogy) to sale. Identify the asl (sale of goods), the far (lease of property), and the illa (defect before complete possession).
The illa is the defect in the subject matter before full possession.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The benefits (manfa'ah) in ijara are realized gradually, so a defect before complete receipt is analogous to a defect in sale before delivery of the goods.
4
Note the conditions that affect the option
The option exists only if the tenant has not yet used the property. If he uses it, he is deemed to have accepted the defect and must pay full rent. Also, if the lessor removes the defect before cancellation, the option lapses.
Uses of the property count as acceptance.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
There is a minor intra-Hanafi difference regarding the basis of fatwa, but both Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agree on the existence of the option. The practical ruling remains the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن استاجر دارا فوجد بها عيبا يضر بالسكنى فله الفسخ لان المعقود عليه المنافع وانها توجد شيئا فشيئا فكان هذا عيبا حادثا قبل القبض فيوجب الخيار كما فى البيع ثم المستاجر اذا استوفى المنفعة فقد رضى بالعيب فيلزمه جميع المبدل كما فى البيع وان فعل المواجر ما ازال به العيب فلا خيار للمستاجر لزوال سببه
He said: Whoever rents a house and finds in it a defect that harms habitation, he has the right to cancel because the subject of the contract is benefits, and they are received little by little, so this is a defect arising before taking possession, so it necessitates an option as in sale. Then if the tenant takes the benefit, he has consented to the defect, so the entire rent is binding on him as in sale. And if the lessor does something that removes the defect, then the tenant has no option due to the removal of the cause.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on termination of a lease contract due to a defect. The author (al-Quduri or the matn) rules that if a tenant finds a defect in the house that harms habitation, he has the option to terminate the lease. The proof is that the subject matter is benefits which are realized gradually. Since the defect occurred before the tenant had fully taken possession (enjoyment of all benefits), it is like a defect found in purchased goods before delivery, which gives the buyer an option to rescind. The analogy (qiyas) to sale is clear. After the tenant uses the property, he is considered to have accepted the defect, so he must pay the full rent. If the lessor repairs the defect before the tenant cancels, the option is removed because the cause (the defect) is eliminated. A fatwa note mentions that there is an intra-Hanafi difference: Ibn 'Abidin in Durr al-Mukhtar states the fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view, while other works like al-Tabyin, al-Muhit, and Sharh Shah 'An indicate the fatwa is on Muhammad's view. The text's ruling aligns with the majority.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijārah): Lease or hire contract for services or usufruct of property.
فسخ (faskh): Termination or rescission of a contract, here by the option of the tenant.
عیب (ʿayb): A defect that diminishes the value or benefit of the leased property.
خیار (khiyār): The option to affirm or rescind a contract, here due to defect.
موجر (mūjir): The lessor, the owner who leases out the property.
مستاجر (mustaʾjir): The lessee, the tenant who rents the property.
منفعت (manfaʿah): Benefit or usufruct, the subject matter of a lease contract.
معقود علیہ (maʿqūd ʿalayh): The subject matter of the contract, here the benefits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a tenant finds a defect in the house that harms habitation before taking possession, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The tenant must pay full rent without option.
B) The tenant has the option to terminate the lease.
C) The lease is automatically void.
D) The lessor must reduce the rent.

Key Takeaway
A tenant has the right to cancel a lease if a harmful defect is discovered before full possession, but using the property or the landlord's repair removes that right.

Termination of Lease upon Destruction of Subject Matter: Automatic Dissolution vs. Right to Terminate
Ruling on dissolution of lease upon complete loss of benefits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on dissolution of a lease when the subject matter perishes, explain the analogical proofs for each, and apply the mufta bihi position to determine the tenant's obligation.

Core Idea
A lease is not automatically void when benefits are lost; the tenant gains a right to terminate but must pay proportionally for remaining benefits.

When a leased house collapses or a mill's water supply is cut off, does the lease automatically end? Imam Muhammad's matn says yes, but later Hanafi masters disagree. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute, the qiyas arguments behind each view, and the preferred ruling for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
State the two principal positions
Recognize that the matn declares the lease dissolved automatically. Then note that some later Hanafi scholars (e.g., Fakhr al-Islam, al-Sarakhsi) argue the contract does not dissolve but the tenant has a right to terminate (qābil li-l-faskh).
The basis of the first view is the plain text of the matn; the second view relies on a narration from Muhammad himself.
2
Identify the proofs for automatic dissolution
The matn analogizes to (a) loss of sold goods before delivery (fawt al-mabīʿ qabl al-qabḍ) and (b) death of a hired slave. In both cases, the contract is voided because the subject matter is irretrievably lost before the transferee takes possession.
The key common element: the benefit (sold goods, slave's service, leased benefits) is completely and permanently lost before the counterparty could exercise any right.
3
Identify the proofs for terminability (second view)
Opponents analogize to the running away of a slave (ibāq) before delivery in sale. The sale is not automatically dissolved; the buyer has an option (khiyār) to rescind. They also cite Muhammad's explicit statement (tanṣīṣ) that if the lessor rebuilds, the tenant cannot refuse and must resume the lease.
The distinction: loss of benefits may be reversible (e.g., water returns, house rebuilt) – like the slave who may be recaptured – so it does not trigger automatic dissolution.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under automatic dissolution, the tenant owes no rent from the moment of destruction. Under the terminability view, the tenant owes rent until he exercises his option to terminate, and if the lessor restores the benefits, the tenant must continue the lease.
Additionally, if only part of the benefit is lost (e.g., mill water cut but building usable for storage), rent is reduced proportionally in both views, but the automatic dissolution view would sever the whole lease.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
According to al-Kaafi and later authorities, the preferred view (asahh) is that the lease does not dissolve automatically but is terminable. Thus the tenant must pay full rent until he terminates, or pay proportionally for remaining benefits if he continues.
This ruling is operative for fatwa today, even though the matn (Zahir al-Riwayah) states the opposite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و اذا خربت الدار وانقطع شرب الضيعة او انقطع الماء عن الرحى انفسخت الاجارة لان المعقود عليه قد فات وهى المنافع المخصوصة قبل القبض فشابه فوت المبيع قبل القبض وموت العبد المستاجر ومن اصحابنا من قال ان العقد لا ينفسخ لان المنافع قد فاتت على وجه يتصور عودها فاشبه الاباق في البيع قبل القبض وعن محمد ان الآجر لو بناها ليس للمستاجر ان يمتنع ولا للآجر وهذا تنصيص منه على انه لم ينفسخ لكنه يُفسخ ولو انقطع ماء الرحى والبيت مما ينتفع به لغير الطحن فعليه من الاجر بحصته لانه جزء من المعقود عليه
He said: And if the house is destroyed, or the water supply for the land is cut off, or water is cut from the mill, the lease is dissolved because the subject matter has perished – and it is the specific benefits – before possession, so it resembles the loss of the goods before delivery in sale and the death of a hired slave. And among our companions are those who said: The contract does not dissolve because the benefits have perished in a manner that their return is conceivable, so it resembles the running away of a slave in sale before delivery. And from Muhammad: If the lessor rebuilds it, the tenant is not entitled to refuse, nor the lessor (to refuse to give), and this is an explicit statement from him that it did not dissolve, but it is terminable. And if the water of the mill is cut off and the house is such that it is beneficial for other than grinding, then he (the tenant) owes rent proportionally, because it is part of the subject matter.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage discusses when a lease ends due to complete loss of benefits. The initial ruling (of Imam Muhammad in the matn) is that if the house collapses, the water for land is cut off, or the mill's water stops, the lease is dissolved automatically. The reason is that the specific benefits – which are the subject matter – have been lost before the tenant had full possession. This is analogized to the loss of sold goods before delivery or the death of a hired slave. However, some Hanafi scholars (like Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi) held that the contract does not dissolve automatically but becomes terminable (qābil li-l-faskh). They argue that the loss of benefits could be temporary (water could return, house could be rebuilt), so it is like a slave running away before delivery – the buyer does not get automatic cancellation but has the option. Imam Muhammad's narration from Hisham supports this: if the lessor rebuilds, neither party can refuse; this indicates the contract did not dissolve but could be faskh. Also a ruling: if only part of the benefit is lost, e.g., water for mill but the building can be used for storage, then rent is reduced proportionally.

Key Terms
انہدام (inhidām): Collapse or destruction of the building structure.
انقطاع (inqiṭāʿ): Cessation or interruption, e.g., water supply.
شرب (shurb): Water supply for irrigation or drinking.
ضیعة (ḍayʿah): Agricultural land or estate.
رحی (raḥā): Water mill for grinding grain.
اباق (ibāq): The running away of a slave, used as a legal analogy.
تنصیص (tanṣīṣ): An explicit textual statement indicating a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if the water supply to a leased mill is cut off, but the mill building can be used for other purposes?
A) The tenant must continue paying full rent.
B) The lease is automatically dissolved.
C) The tenant has the option to terminate, and if he continues, rent is reduced proportionally.
D) The lease is void from the start.

Key Takeaway
When the subject matter of a lease perishes before full possession, the Hanafi mufta bihi is that the lease does not dissolve automatically but becomes terminable, with proportional rent reduction for partial loss.
