Dissolution of Ijarah Due to Loss of Usufruct Before Delivery
Ruling with evidence and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the dissolution of ijarah when the leased property is destroyed or usufruct is lost before delivery, and distinguish between automatic dissolution (infsakh) and the right to cancel (khiyar al-faskh).

Core Idea
Loss of usufruct before delivery makes ijarah dissolvable, not void.

In ijarah contracts, the subject matter is the usufruct (manfa'ah). If the usufruct is destroyed before the lessee takes possession, what happens to the contract? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer: it does not automatically dissolve but becomes subject to cancellation. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the intra-madhhab dispute as presented in Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and initial ruling
The text begins with three scenarios: house ruined, irrigation cut, mill water stopped. The initial ruling states that the contract dissolves (infsakhat).
This is the position of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
2
Analyze the analogy (qiyas) used
The dissolution is analogized to the loss of a sold item before delivery or the death of a hired slave. The illa (effective cause) is that the object of the contract—the specific usufruct—has ceased to exist before the lessee has taken possession.
This is a typical Hanafi qiyas linking ijarah to sale in terms of subject matter perishability.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi objection
Some later scholars (Fakhr al-Islam, Sarakhsi) argue that the contract does not dissolve automatically. They offer a counter-analogy: a slave who absconds before delivery in a sale—the sale is not automatically void, but the buyer has the option to cancel.
Their basis: the loss may be temporary; water can return or the house can be rebuilt.
4
Learn the relied-upon position (mufta bihi)
Al-Kafi states that the view that the contract becomes dissolvable (qabil li al-faskh) is asahh (more correct). This is the position adopted for fatwa.
Imam Muhammad's narration supports this: if the lessor rebuilds, neither party can refuse to proceed.
5
Apply to partial loss
If only part of the usufruct is lost (e.g., mill water stops but the building can be used for other purposes), the lessee must pay rent proportionally for the remaining benefit.
This is because the remaining part is still part of the contracted object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
١٠٣
جب گھر ویران ہو جائے یا زراعت یا پن چکی کا پانی بند ہو جائے تو اجارہ فسخ ہو جائے گا
كتاب الاجارات
قال و اذا خربت الدار وانقطع شرب الضيعة او انقطع الماء عن الرحى انفسخت الاجارة لان المعقود عليه قد فات وهى المنافع المخصوصة قبل القبض فشابه فوت المبيع قبل القبض وموت العبد المستاجر ومن اصحابنا من قال ان العقد لا ينفسخ لان المنافع قد فاتت على وجه يتصور عودها فاشبه الاباق في البيع قبل القبض وعن محمد ان الآجر لو بناها ليس للمستاجر ان يمتنع ولا للآجر وهذا تنصيص منه على انه لم ينفسخ لكنه يُفسخ ولو انقطع ماء الرحى والبيت مما ينتفع به لغير الطحن فعليه من الاجر بحصته لانه جزء من المعقود عليه
ترجمہ ... جب گھر ویران ہو جائے یا آب پاشی کی زمین یا پن چکی کا پانی ٹوٹ جائے تو اجارہ فسخ ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ فوت ہو چکا اور وہ مخصوص منافع ہیں کہ قبضہ سے پہلے جاتے رہے۔ تو قبل از مبیع کے فوت ہونے یا کرایہ پر لئے ہوئے غلام کے مرجانے کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور ہمارے بعض اصحاب نے کہا ہے کہ عقد فسخ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ منافع ایسے طور پر فوت ہوئے ہیں کہ ان کا عود کر نا متصور ہے۔ پس بیچ میں قبضہ سے پہلے غلام کے بھاگ جانے کے مشابہ ہوا۔ اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ اگر موجر نے اس کو بنا دیا تو نہ مستاجر کو باز رہنے کا اختیار ہے نہ موجز کو یہ ان کی طرف سے تصریح ہے کہ عقد فسخ نہیں ہوا۔ لیکن قابل فسخ ہو گیا۔ اگر پن چکی کا پانی بند ہو گیا اور پن چکی کا گھر ایسا ہے کہ پینے کے علاوہ دیگر نفع اٹھایا جاسکتا ہے تو مستاجر پر اس کے حساب سے اجرت واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ وہ گھر بھی معقود
علیہ کا ایک جزء ہے۔ تشريح ... قوله واذا خربت الدار... الخ- عقد اجارہ چند امور سے فسخ ہو جاتا ہے۔ ا کوئی ایسا عیب پیدا ہو جائے جس سے منفعت فوت ہو جائے جس کی تصریح پچھلے صفحہ پر گزر چکی ۔ جیسے گھر کا ویران ہو جانا۔ پن چکی یا زمین زراعت کے پانی کا بند ہوجانا وغیرہ کیونکہ یہ ایسا ہے جیسے قبضہ سے پہلے مبیع فوت ہو جائے کہ بیع فسخ ہو جاتی ہے یا جیسے اجارہ پر لیا ہوا غلام مرجائے ائمہ ثلاثہ اسی کے قائل ہیں۔
قوله ومن اصحابنا ... الخ - ہمارے مشائخ میں سے شیخ فخر الاسلام او شمس الائمہ سرسی وغیرہ نے کہا ہے کہ اجارہ خود تو فسخ نہیں ہوگا البتہ قابل فسخ ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ منافع کا زوال ایسے طور پر ہوا ہے کہ ان کا عود ممکن ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے بیچ میں قبضہ سے پہلے غلام بیع بھاگ جائے کہ عقد بیع فسخ نہیں ہو جا تا بلکہ مشتری کو فسخ کا اختیار حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ بدلیل آنکہ ہشام نے امام محمد سے روایت کیا ہے کہ اگر انہدام بیت کے بعد موجر نے اس کو بنا دیا تو مستاجر کو لینے سے اور موجر کو دینے سے انکار کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ یہ قول صریح ہے کہ عقد اجارہ فسخ نہیں ہوا تھا۔ البتہ قابل فسخ ہو گیا تھا۔ کافی میں ہے کہ یہی اصح ہے۔ جن مشائخ نے یہ کہا ہے کہ اجارہ مسخ ہو جائے گا ان کا استدلال اس سے ہے جو امام محمد نے کتاب البیوع میں ذکر کیا ہے۔
لوسقطت الدار فله ان يخرج سواء كان صاحب الدار حاضرًا او غائباً
When the house becomes ruined, or the irrigation of the land is cut off, or the water for the mill is cut off, the lease is dissolved because the object of the contract has ceased to exist—it being the specific usufructs before delivery—so it resembles the loss of the sold item before delivery and the death of the hired slave. Among our companions, some said that the contract is not dissolved because the usufructs have ceased in a manner that their return is conceivable, resembling the absconding of a slave in sale before delivery. From Muhammad: If the lessor rebuilds it, neither the lessee has the right to refuse nor the lessor [to demand refusal]—this is an explicit statement that it was not dissolved, but it becomes dissolvable. If the water of the mill is cut off and the house can be used for other purposes besides grinding, then the lessee owes rent proportionate to that part because it is part of the object of the contract.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with evidence and an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the dissolution of an ijarah (lease) contract when the property is destroyed or the usufruct is lost before delivery. The main ruling states that if the house is ruined, or the irrigation of the agricultural land stops, or the water for the mill stops, the ijarah is dissolved (munfasikhah). The reason is that the object of the contract—the specific usufructs—has perished before the lessee has taken possession, similar to a sale where the item is lost before delivery, or the hired slave dies. This is the position of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). However, some of our scholars (such as Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi) hold that the contract is not automatically dissolved but becomes subject to dissolution (qabil li al-faskh). They argue that the loss of usufruct is not necessarily permanent; the water might return or the house could be rebuilt. They analogize this to a slave who absconds before delivery in a sale—the sale is not automatically voided, but the buyer has the option to cancel. Imam Muhammad's narration supports this: if the lessor rebuilds the house after the destruction, neither party can refuse to proceed, indicating the contract remained valid but dissolvable. Al-Kafi states that this is the more correct (asahh) position. The text also addresses a scenario where only part of the usufruct is lost: if the mill's water stops but the house can be used for other purposes, the lessee must pay rent proportionally for the remaining benefit.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A contract for the hire of a specific property or services in exchange for rent.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment or dissolution of a contract, either by operation of law or by option.
منافع (manafi'): Usufructs or benefits that are the subject of an ijarah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (as per Al-Kafi), what happens to the ijarah contract if the rented house collapses before the lessee takes possession?
A) The contract is automatically dissolved (munfasikh).
B) The contract remains valid but both parties have the option to cancel it.
C) The contract is void (batil) from the start.
D) The lessee is entitled to a full refund but the contract continues.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on ijarah dissolution is that loss of usufruct before delivery does not automatically void the contract; it becomes subject to cancellation, and if part of the usufruct remains, proportionate rent is due.

Effect of Death of a Party on Ijarah
Ruling on ijarah dissolution upon death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether an ijarah contract dissolves upon the death of a contracting party and distinguish cases where the contract is made for oneself versus for another.

Core Idea
Death dissolves ijarah only if the contract was for oneself; it continues if made for another (agent, guardian, trustee).

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: what happens to a lease when the lessor or lessee dies? The answer depends on whether the deceased contracted for themselves or on behalf of someone else. We will examine the ruling, its rationale, and the exception for agents, guardians, and trustees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The ruling distinguishes between two situations: the contract is for oneself (li nafsihi) or for another (li ghayrihi). Determine which case is being discussed.
2
State the general rule
If a contracting party dies and the contract was for themselves, the ijarah dissolves. Understand the reason: the benefit or rent would otherwise pass to heirs, which is impermissible as the contract was personal.
3
Apply the exception
If the contract was made for another (e.g., agent for principal, guardian for orphan, trustee for waqf), the ijarah does not dissolve because the actual contracting party (the represented) remains alive.
4
Connect to the rationale
The rationale is that the contract's subject matter (usufruct or rent) is owned by the deceased personally; upon death, it transfers to heirs, making continuation impossible. In the exception, ownership remains with the represented party.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
جب متعاقدین میں سے کوئی ایک فوت ہو گیا اور اجارہ اپنے لئے ہی کیا تھا اجارہ منتخ ہوگا
قال و اذا مات احد المتعاقدين وقد عقد الاجارة لنفسه انفسخت الاجارة لانه لو بقى العقد تصير المنفعة المملوكة له او الاجرة المملوكة له لغير العاقد مستحقة بالعقد لانه ينتقل بالموت الى الوارث وذالك لا يجوز وان عقدها لغيره لم تنفسخ مثل الوكيل والوصى والمتولى فى الوقف لانعدام ما اشرنا اليه من المعنى قال ويصح شرط الخيار فى الاجارة وقال الشافعى لا يصح لان المستاجر لا يمكنه رد المعقود عليه بكماله. لو كان الخيار له لفوات بعضه ولو كان للمواجر فلا يمكنه التسليم ايضًا على الكمال وكل ذالك يمنع الخيار ولنا انه عقد معاملة لا يستحق القبض فيه فى المجلس فجاز اشتراط الخيار فيه كالبيع والجامع بينهما دفع الحاجة وفوات بعض المعقود عليه فى الاجارة لا يمنع الرد بخيار العيب فكذا بخيار الشرط بخلاف البيع وهذا لان رد الكل ممكن فى البيع دون الاجارة فيشترط فيه دونها ولهذا يجبر المستاجر على القبض اذا سلّم المواجر بعد مضى بعض المدة
ترجمہ جب متعاقدین میں سے کوئی مرگیا اور حال یہ کہ اجارہ اس نے اپنے ہی لئے باندھا تھا تو اجارہ فسخ ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ اگر یہ عقد باقی رہے تو اس کی منفعت مملوکہ یا اجرت مملوکہ اس عقد کی وجہ سے ایسے شخص کی مستحق ہوگی جو عاقد نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ استحقاق بوجہ موت وراث کی طرف منتقل ہو گا۔ اور یہ جائز نہیں اور اگر کسی اور کے لئے باندھا ہو تو فسخ نہ ہوگا جیسے وکیل وصی اور متولی وقف وہ معنی معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے جس کی طرف ہم نے اشارہ کیا۔ اور صحیح ہے اجارہ میں شرط خیار، امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ صحیح نہیں ۔ کیونکہ مستاجر کو پورا معقود علیہ واپس کرنا ممکن نہیں جب کہ خیار اس کے لئے ہو ۔ بعض معقود علیہ فوت ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اور اگر خیار موجر کے لئے تو وہ بھی معقود علیہ سپر دنہیں کر سکتا اور یہ سب مانع خیار ہے ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ ایک عقد معاملہ ہے جس میں مجلس کے اندر قبضہ واجب نہیں ہوتا تو اس میں خیار کی شرط لگانا جائز ہے جیسے بیع میں جائز ہے اور دونوں میں وجہ جامع دفع ضرورت ہے۔ اور اجارہ میں کچھ معقود علیہ کا فوت ہو جانا بوجہ خیار عیب واپسی کر نہیں روکتا ایسے ہی خیار شرط کی وجہ سے بھی واپسی کو نہیں روکے گا۔ بخلاف بیچ کے اور یہ اس لئے کہ بیچ میں کل واپس کرناممکن ہے نہ کہ اجارہ میں لہذا بیچ میں کل واپس کر نا ممکن ہے۔ نہ کہ اجارہ میں لہذا بیچ میں کل واپسی شرط کی گئی نہ کہ اجارہ میں ۔ اسی لئے مستاجر کو مجبور کیا جائے گا قبضہ پر جب کہ سپر د کرے موجد کچھ
مدت گزر جانے کے بعد ۔ تشریح قوله واذا مات الخ
(۲) اگر موجر ومستاجر میں سے کوئی مرجائے جب کہ اس نے عقد اجارہ اپنے ہی لئے کیا تھا ( کسی کی جانب سے وکیل نہیں تھا ) تو احناف، شعمی ثوری، ابوسلیمان اور لیٹ بن سعد کے نزدیک اجارہ مسخ ہو جائے گا اگر موجر مر جائے تو اجارہ اس لیئے فتح ہو گا کہ مرنے کے بعد شئی اس کے ورثہ کی ہوگئی ۔ اب اگر مستاجر اس سے نفع حاصل کرتا ہے تو ملک غیر سے منتفع ہونا لازم آیا اور یہ جائز نہیں ۔ اور اگر مستاجر مر جائے تو اس لئے فسخ ہو گا کہ اس صورت میں ملک غیر سے اجرت کی ادائیگی لازم آتی ہے اور یہ بھی جائز نہیں ۔ ہاں اگر اجارہ غیر کے لئے :۔ مثلاً وکیل نے موکل کے لئے کیا تھا یا وصی نے یتیم کے لئے کیا تھا یا عاقد متولی وقف تھا تواحد المتعاقدین کی
If one of the two contracting parties dies, and he had contracted the lease for himself, the lease is dissolved because if the contract remained, the benefit owned by him or the rent owned by him would become due by the contract to someone who is not the contracting party, since it transfers to the heir upon death, and that is not permissible. If he contracted it for someone else, it is not dissolved, such as the agent, the executor, and the trustee of a waqf due to the absence of the meaning we indicated. He said: The stipulation of an option (khiyar) is valid in lease. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not valid because the lessee cannot return the entire object of the contract if the option is for him due to the loss of part of it, and if the option is for the lessor, he also cannot deliver it completely, and all of that prevents the option. Our proof is that it is a transaction contract that does not require delivery in the sitting, so stipulating an option in it is permissible, like in sale, and the common ground between them is the fulfillment of need. Loss of part of the object of contract in lease does not prevent return due to option of defect, so likewise due to stipulation of option, unlike sale. This is because returning the whole is possible in sale but not in lease; hence it is required in sale but not in lease. For this reason, the lessee can be compelled to take possession if the lessor delivers after some time has passed.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings: first, the effect of death of a contracting party on an ijarah contract; second, the validity of stipulating an option (khiyar al-shart) in ijarah along with an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Shafi'i. On the first issue: If either the lessor or lessee dies and the contract was made for themselves (i.e., they are not representing others), the ijarah dissolves. The reason is that if it continued, the benefit or rent would be owned by the heirs, not the original party, which is impermissible because the contract was based on the specific personal capacity. However, if the contract was made on behalf of another (e.g., an agent for a principal, a guardian for an orphan, or a trustee of a waqf), it does not dissolve upon the death of the representative, as the contracting party (the represented) is still alive. On the second issue: The Hanafi school holds that it is valid to stipulate a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) in an ijarah contract. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that in ijarah the object of the contract (usufruct) is delivered in parts over time, making complete return impossible; if the option is for the lessee, he cannot return the entire usufruct since some may have elapsed, and if for the lessor, he cannot deliver the entire usufruct if some time has passed. The Hanafi response: Ijarah is a transaction contract where delivery is not required immediately in the sitting (like sale), so option is permissible. The underlying rationale (jami') is the need (daf' al-hajah) of people. Moreover, partial loss does not prevent return due to a defect option (khiyar al-'ayb) in ijarah, so similarly it does not prevent return due to stipulated option. This is unlike sale, where the entire object can be returned. In ijarah, the lessee can be compelled to accept delivery even after some period has passed, indicating that return of the whole is not required.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakil): An agent who contracts on behalf of another (al-muwakkil).
الوصي (al-wasi): An executor or guardian appointed to manage the affairs of an orphan or estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A trustee (mutawalli) of a waqf leases a waqf property. The trustee dies. According to the Hanafi school, what happens to the lease?
A) The lease dissolves because the trustee died.
B) The lease continues because the trustee contracted for the waqf.
C) The lease becomes voidable at the option of the new trustee.
D) The lease dissolves only if the lessee also dies.

Key Takeaway
Death dissolves ijarah only when the deceased contracted for themselves; otherwise, it continues.

Validity of Khiyar al-Shart in Ijarah
Inter-madhhab dispute on khiyar al-shart in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits stipulating a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) in ijarah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is valid in ijarah because partial consumption of usufruct does not prevent return, analogously to khiyar al-'ayb.

This lesson delves into an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether a lease can include an option to cancel within a set period. The Hanafi school allows it, while Imam al-Shafi'i rejects it based on the impossibility of returning the subject matter intact. We will examine both proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that it is valid (sahih) to stipulate khiyar al-shart in an ijarah contract. The text states 'yashhu shart al-khiyar fi al-ijarah'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that it is invalid because neither party can return the entire subject matter: the lessee cannot return all the usufruct (some consumed), and the lessor cannot deliver all the usufruct (some time passed). Return of the whole is a prerequisite for option.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (dalil)
Hanafis argue that ijarah is a transaction contract (mu'awada) where immediate delivery in the session is not required, thus option is permissible like in sale. The common ground (jami') is the need of people (daf' al-hajah).
4
Examine the rebuttal using khiyar al-'ayb
Partial consumption does not prevent return due to a defect option (khiyar al-'ayb) in ijarah; similarly, it does not prevent return due to stipulation (khiyar al-shart). This overturns the Shafi'i objection.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi jurisdictions, parties can agree on an option period (e.g., 3 days) in a lease. In Shafi'i, such a condition would invalidate the lease or be void.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
جب متعاقدین میں سے کوئی ایک فوت ہو گیا اور اجارہ اپنے لئے ہی کیا تھا اجارہ منتخ ہوگا
قال و اذا مات احد المتعاقدين وقد عقد الاجارة لنفسه انفسخت الاجارة لانه لو بقى العقد تصير المنفعة المملوكة له او الاجرة المملوكة له لغير العاقد مستحقة بالعقد لانه ينتقل بالموت الى الوارث وذالك لا يجوز وان عقدها لغيره لم تنفسخ مثل الوكيل والوصى والمتولى فى الوقف لانعدام ما اشرنا اليه من المعنى قال ويصح شرط الخيار فى الاجارة وقال الشافعى لا يصح لان المستاجر لا يمكنه رد المعقود عليه بكماله. لو كان الخيار له لفوات بعضه ولو كان للمواجر فلا يمكنه التسليم ايضًا على الكمال وكل ذالك يمنع الخيار ولنا انه عقد معاملة لا يستحق القبض فيه فى المجلس فجاز اشتراط الخيار فيه كالبيع والجامع بينهما دفع الحاجة وفوات بعض المعقود عليه فى الاجارة لا يمنع الرد بخيار العيب فكذا بخيار الشرط بخلاف البيع وهذا لان رد الكل ممكن فى البيع دون الاجارة فيشترط فيه دونها ولهذا يجبر المستاجر على القبض اذا سلّم المواجر بعد مضى بعض المدة
ترجمہ جب متعاقدین میں سے کوئی مرگیا اور حال یہ کہ اجارہ اس نے اپنے ہی لئے باندھا تھا تو اجارہ فسخ ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ اگر یہ عقد باقی رہے تو اس کی منفعت مملوکہ یا اجرت مملوکہ اس عقد کی وجہ سے ایسے شخص کی مستحق ہوگی جو عاقد نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ استحقاق بوجہ موت وراث کی طرف منتقل ہو گا۔ اور یہ جائز نہیں اور اگر کسی اور کے لئے باندھا ہو تو فسخ نہ ہوگا جیسے وکیل وصی اور متولی وقف وہ معنی معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے جس کی طرف ہم نے اشارہ کیا۔ اور صحیح ہے اجارہ میں شرط خیار، امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ صحیح نہیں ۔ کیونکہ مستاجر کو پورا معقود علیہ واپس کرنا ممکن نہیں جب کہ خیار اس کے لئے ہو ۔ بعض معقود علیہ فوت ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اور اگر خیار موجر کے لئے تو وہ بھی معقود علیہ سپر دنہیں کر سکتا اور یہ سب مانع خیار ہے ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ ایک عقد معاملہ ہے جس میں مجلس کے اندر قبضہ واجب نہیں ہوتا تو اس میں خیار کی شرط لگانا جائز ہے جیسے بیع میں جائز ہے اور دونوں میں وجہ جامع دفع ضرورت ہے۔ اور اجارہ میں کچھ معقود علیہ کا فوت ہو جانا بوجہ خیار عیب واپسی کر نہیں روکتا ایسے ہی خیار شرط کی وجہ سے بھی واپسی کو نہیں روکے گا۔ بخلاف بیچ کے اور یہ اس لئے کہ بیچ میں کل واپس کرناممکن ہے نہ کہ اجارہ میں لہذا بیچ میں کل واپس کر نا ممکن ہے۔ نہ کہ اجارہ میں لہذا بیچ میں کل واپسی شرط کی گئی نہ کہ اجارہ میں ۔ اسی لئے مستاجر کو مجبور کیا جائے گا قبضہ پر جب کہ سپر د کرے موجد کچھ
مدت گزر جانے کے بعد ۔ تشریح قوله واذا مات الخ
(۲) اگر موجر ومستاجر میں سے کوئی مرجائے جب کہ اس نے عقد اجارہ اپنے ہی لئے کیا تھا ( کسی کی جانب سے وکیل نہیں تھا ) تو احناف، شعمی ثوری، ابوسلیمان اور لیٹ بن سعد کے نزدیک اجارہ مسخ ہو جائے گا اگر موجر مر جائے تو اجارہ اس لیئے فتح ہو گا کہ مرنے کے بعد شئی اس کے ورثہ کی ہوگئی ۔ اب اگر مستاجر اس سے نفع حاصل کرتا ہے تو ملک غیر سے منتفع ہونا لازم آیا اور یہ جائز نہیں ۔ اور اگر مستاجر مر جائے تو اس لئے فسخ ہو گا کہ اس صورت میں ملک غیر سے اجرت کی ادائیگی لازم آتی ہے اور یہ بھی جائز نہیں ۔ ہاں اگر اجارہ غیر کے لئے :۔ مثلاً وکیل نے موکل کے لئے کیا تھا یا وصی نے یتیم کے لئے کیا تھا یا عاقد متولی وقف تھا تواحد المتعاقدین کی
If one of the two contracting parties dies, and he had contracted the lease for himself, the lease is dissolved because if the contract remained, the benefit owned by him or the rent owned by him would become due by the contract to someone who is not the contracting party, since it transfers to the heir upon death, and that is not permissible. If he contracted it for someone else, it is not dissolved, such as the agent, the executor, and the trustee of a waqf due to the absence of the meaning we indicated. He said: The stipulation of an option (khiyar) is valid in lease. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not valid because the lessee cannot return the entire object of the contract if the option is for him due to the loss of part of it, and if the option is for the lessor, he also cannot deliver it completely, and all of that prevents the option. Our proof is that it is a transaction contract that does not require delivery in the sitting, so stipulating an option in it is permissible, like in sale, and the common ground between them is the fulfillment of need. Loss of part of the object of contract in lease does not prevent return due to option of defect, so likewise due to stipulation of option, unlike sale. This is because returning the whole is possible in sale but not in lease; hence it is required in sale but not in lease. For this reason, the lessee can be compelled to take possession if the lessor delivers after some time has passed.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings: first, the effect of death of a contracting party on an ijarah contract; second, the validity of stipulating an option (khiyar al-shart) in ijarah along with an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Shafi'i. On the first issue: If either the lessor or lessee dies and the contract was made for themselves (i.e., they are not representing others), the ijarah dissolves. The reason is that if it continued, the benefit or rent would be owned by the heirs, not the original party, which is impermissible because the contract was based on the specific personal capacity. However, if the contract was made on behalf of another (e.g., an agent for a principal, a guardian for an orphan, or a trustee of a waqf), it does not dissolve upon the death of the representative, as the contracting party (the represented) is still alive. On the second issue: The Hanafi school holds that it is valid to stipulate a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) in an ijarah contract. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that in ijarah the object of the contract (usufruct) is delivered in parts over time, making complete return impossible; if the option is for the lessee, he cannot return the entire usufruct since some may have elapsed, and if for the lessor, he cannot deliver the entire usufruct if some time has passed. The Hanafi response: Ijarah is a transaction contract where delivery is not required immediately in the sitting (like sale), so option is permissible. The underlying rationale (jami') is the need (daf' al-hajah) of people. Moreover, partial loss does not prevent return due to a defect option (khiyar al-'ayb) in ijarah, so similarly it does not prevent return due to stipulated option. This is unlike sale, where the entire object can be returned. In ijarah, the lessee can be compelled to accept delivery even after some period has passed, indicating that return of the whole is not required.

Key Terms
شرط الخيار (shart al-khiyar): A condition in a contract allowing one or both parties to cancel within a specified period.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): The option to cancel a contract due to a defect in the subject matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for the validity of khiyar al-shart in ijarah?
A) Ijarah is a contract of necessity, so options are always allowed.
B) The lessee can return the entire usufruct at the end of the term.
C) Ijarah is a transaction contract like sale, and partial consumption does not prevent return, as evidenced by khiyar al-'ayb.
D) The Quran explicitly permits it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates khiyar al-shart in ijarah by analogizing to sale and to khiyar al-'ayb, overruling the Shafi'i objection based on incomplete return.

Death of a Party Dissolves Ijara Contract
Ruling on dissolution of ijara at death of a party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the death of a contracting party in ijara and explain the legal reasoning (talil) behind it.

Core Idea
If a party dies in an ijara contract made for himself, the contract dissolves because benefit cannot transfer to an heir.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the effect of death on an ijara contract. Unlike the majority of schools, the Hanafis hold that the contract is automatically dissolved when either the lessor or lessee dies, provided the contract was made for the deceased party themselves. The reason is rooted in the nature of ownership: the benefit or hire owed would transfer to the heir, which would unjustly bind the other party to a contract with a new owner. This ruling is a distinctive feature of Hanafi fiqh and illustrates the school's approach to contracts based on manfa'ah (benefits).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm (legal status) is. The act is the death of one party (mu'jir or musta'jir) during the term of an ijara contract. The ruling stated is that the contract 'infasakhat' (is dissolved).
The ruling applies only when the deceased party contracted for himself, not as a representative.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text provides a rational proof (talil) introduced by 'li-annahu law baqiya al-'aqd...' (because if the contract remained...). Identify the specific phrase that constitutes the proof.
The proof is not a Quranic verse or hadith but a legal rational argument based on ownership transfer.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
Analyze how the proof leads to the ruling. If the contract remained after death, the benefit (manfa'ah) or hire (ujrah) that was owed to the deceased would become owned by the heir. This would make the other party's right enforceable against someone they did not contract with, which is impermissible because it amounts to benefiting from the heir's property without consent.
The key concept is that ijara is a contract for benefits, and benefits are not considered heritable property in the same way as tangible assets.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (alternative views)
Identify the opposing positions. The Hanafi school's ruling is unique. The three other major Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Hanbal) hold that the contract remains binding and the heir steps into the place of the deceased. Also note the minority positions (Sufyan al-Thawri, Abu Sulayman) that agree with the Hanafis.
Understanding the ikhtilaf deepens comprehension of the Hanafi dalil and its underlying conception of ownership.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
Determine why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon). The text from Al-Hidayah presents this as the madhhab position. The reasoning is based on the principle that benefits are not owned like assets and thus cannot be transmitted to heirs by contract. This is a consistent application of the Hanafi view of ijara.
The tarjih authority is Al-Marghinani, who presents the ruling as established in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و اذا مات احد المتعاقدين وقد عقد الاجارة لنفسه انفسخت الاجارة لانه لو بقى العقد تصير المنفعة المملوكة له او الاجرة المملوكة له لغير العاقد مستحقة بالعقد لانه ينتقل بالموت الى الوارث وذالك لا يجوز وان عقدها لغيره لم تنفسخ مثل الوكيل والوصى والمتولى فى الوقف لانعدام ما اشرنا اليه من المعنى
He said: When one of the two contracting parties dies, and he had made the contract of hire for himself, the hire contract is dissolved because if the contract remained, the owned benefit or the owned hire would become due by the contract to someone other than the contracting party, because it transfers by death to the heir, and that is not permissible. And if he made it for someone else, it is not dissolved, like the agent, executor, and trustee of a waqf, due to the absence of the meaning we indicated.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on the death of a contracting party in ijara. The Arabic matn explicitly says that if either the lessor or lessee dies while the contract was made for themselves (not as a representative), the ijara is dissolved. The reason is that the benefit or hire owed would become owned by the heir, which is impermissible because it involves benefiting from another's property without right. However, if the contract was made for someone else (e.g., a wakil for the principal, a guardian for an orphan, or a mutawalli for a waqf), death of the representative does not dissolve the contract because the ownership does not transfer to the heir of the representative. The Urdu commentary adds that this is the position of the Hanafi school, Sufyan al-Thawri, Abu Sulayman, and others, while the three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Hanbal) hold that the contract continues and the heir steps in, as they consider benefits like assets.

Key Terms
الاجارة (al-ijārah): A contract of hire or lease where one party (mu'jir) provides a benefit (manfa'ah) in exchange for payment (ujrah).
انفسخت (infasakhat): The contract becomes dissolved or void automatically upon occurrence of the event (death).
المتعاقدين (al-muta'āqidayn): The two contracting parties, i.e., the mu'jir (lessor) and musta'jir (lessee).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the lessor (mu'jir) dies after contracting ijara for himself, what happens to the contract?
A) The contract remains binding on the heirs.
B) The contract is automatically dissolved.
C) The heirs may choose to continue the contract.
D) The contract becomes invalid only if the lessee objects.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the death of a party who contracted for himself automatically dissolves an ijara contract, due to the impermissibility of transferring the ownership of future benefits to an heir without the other party's consent.

Validity of Khiyar al-Shart in Ijara: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Proving validity of khiyar al-shart in ijara against Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on stipulating khiyar al-shart in ijara and explain the qiyas used to defend it against the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
An option of rescission is valid in hire because the need for deliberation overcomes partial consumption.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over whether a party to a hire contract (ijara) can stipulate an option to rescind (khiyar al-shart). The Hanafi school holds it is valid, analogizing to sale and to the option for defect, while Shafi'i argues that the consumed nature of benefits prevents full return. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply qiyas and appreciate how different premises lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the text: stipulating khiyar al-shart in ijara is valid (sahih).
The text begins with 'Wa yasihhu shart al-khiyar fi al-ijara'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is invalid because the subject matter (benefits) cannot be fully returned after partial consumption.
The text quotes: 'Qala al-Shafi'i la yasihh...'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i's dalil: if the lessee has an option, he cannot return the benefit already consumed; if the lessor has an option, he cannot deliver all benefits completely. This impossibility prevents the option.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi uses two analogies: (1) qiyas to sale – both are commutative contracts where immediate possession is not required, and the need (haja) justifies the option. (2) qiyas to khiyar al-ayb – partial loss does not prevent return for a defect, so similarly for a stipulation.
The text says: 'Wa lana innahu aqd muawada... fajaza ishtirat al-khiyar fihi ka al-bay'... fawat al-ba'd la yamna' al-radd bi khiyar al-ayb fakadha bi khiyar al-shart.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafis allow the condition; Shafi'is do not. In fatwa, the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
The text implies this is the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويصح شرط الخيار فى الاجارة وقال الشافعى لا يصح لان المستاجر لا يمكنه رد المعقود عليه بكماله. لو كان الخيار له لفوات بعضه ولو كان للمواجر فلا يمكنه التسليم ايضًا على الكمال وكل ذالك يمنع الخيار ولنا انه عقد معاملة لا يستحق القبض فيه فى المجلس فجاز اشتراط الخيار فيه كالبيع والجامع بينهما دفع الحاجة وفوات بعض المعقود عليه فى الاجارة لا يمنع الرد بخيار العيب فكذا بخيار الشرط بخلاف البيع وهذا لان رد الكل ممكن فى البيع دون الاجارة فيشترط فيه دونها ولهذا يجبر المستاجر على القبض اذا سلّم المواجر بعد مضى بعض المدة
He said: And the stipulation of option in hire is valid. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not valid because the lessee cannot return the entire contracted subject matter. If the option were for him, due to the loss of some of it; and if the option were for the lessor, he also cannot deliver it completely, and all of that prevents the option. And for us: It is a commutative contract in which taking possession is not required in the session, so stipulating option in it is valid, like sale, and the common ground between them is fulfillment of need, and the loss of some of the contracted subject matter in hire does not prevent return due to the option of defect, likewise due to the option of stipulation, contrary to sale. This is because returning the whole is possible in sale but not in hire, so it is stipulated there, not here. For this reason, the lessee is compelled to take possession when the lessor delivers after some of the period has passed.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage addresses the inter-madhhab dispute over stipulating khiyar al-shart (option of rescission) in an ijara contract. The Hanafi position is that it is valid, while Imam al-Shafi'i rejects it. Shafi'i's argument is that the subject matter of ijara is benefits that are consumed over time; thus, if the lessee has an option, he cannot return the benefit already consumed, and if the lessor has an option, he cannot deliver the full benefit. The Hanafi response uses two proofs: First, ijara is a commutative contract (mu'awada) where immediate possession is not required, analogous to sale. Second, the partial loss of the subject matter does not prevent return under khiyar al-ayb (option for defect), so similarly it does not prevent return under khiyar al-shart. The difference from sale is that in sale, complete return is possible; in ijara, it is not, but this does not invalidate the option. The Urdu commentary explains that the common cause is the need for deliberation to avoid loss, and that the lessee can be forced to accept delivery after the option period.

Key Terms
شرط الخيار (sharṭ al-khiyār): A condition in a contract that gives one or both parties the right to rescind the contract within a specified period.
الاجارة (al-ijārah): A contract of hire or lease for benefits.
البيع (al-bay‘): Sale contract; used as the analogical basis for ijara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam al-Shafi'i reject stipulating khiyar al-shart in ijara?
A) Because ijara is a non-commutative contract.
B) Because the subject matter (benefits) cannot be fully returned.
C) Because there is no need for options in ijara.
D) Because the contract must be executed immediately.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, stipulating khiyar al-shart in ijara is valid by qiyas to sale and khiyar al-ayb despite partial consumption of benefits.

Dissolution of Ijara Due to Valid Excuses: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on dissolution of ijara for excuses against Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dissolving ijara for excuses, explain the qiyas to defect in sale, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
An excuse that causes extra harm dissolves ijara, like a defect before delivery in sale.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether ijara (hire contract) can be dissolved for reasons other than defects. The Hanafi school holds that valid excuses ('udhr) such as cessation of need or impossibility of benefit allow dissolution, while Shafi'i restricts it to defects only. The debate hinges on the legal nature of benefits (manafi') and the analogy to sale.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: ijara dissolves (tanfasikh) upon occurrence of a valid excuse ('udhr). The text says 'wa tufsakh al-ijarah bi al-a'dhar'.
This is the opposite of the Shafi'i view.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that ijara does not dissolve except for a defect, because benefits are like tangible assets (a'yan), making the contract binding like sale.
The key difference lies in how benefits are conceptualized.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues that since benefits are akin to tangible assets, the contract is binding and cannot be dissolved arbitrarily. Only a defect in the subject matter justifies dissolution.
This is a strong analogy if benefits are indeed like goods.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis counter that benefits are not actually possessed; they are consumed over time. The inability to proceed without extra harm is the same meaning as a defect before delivery in sale. The text says: 'fasar al-'udhr fi al-ijarah ka al-'ayb qabl al-qabd fi al-bay'.
The common cause ('illa) is the burden of extra harm not owed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafis allow dissolution for excuses like cessation of need, illness, etc., while Shafi'is do not and require payment of full hire even if the purpose is lost.
Practical difference: a person who hires a cook for a wedding then cancels the wedding can rescind under Hanafi, but must pay under Shafi'i.

قال و تفسخ الاجارة بالاعذار عندنا وقال الشافعى لا تفسخ الا بالعيب لان المنافع عنده بمنزلة الاعيان حتى يجوز العقد عليها فاشبه البيع ولنا ان المنافع غير مقبوضة وهى المعقود عليها فصار العذر في الاجارة كالعيب قبل القبض في البيع فتفسخ به اذ المعنى يجمعهما وهو عجز العاقد عن المضى في موجبه الا بتحمل ضرر زائد لم يستحق به وهذا هو معنى العذر عندنا وهو كمن استاجر حدادا ليقلع ضرسه لوجع به فسكن الوجع أو استاجر طباخا ليطبخ له طعام الوليمة فاختلعت منه تفسخ الاجارة لان في المضى عليه الزام ضرر زائد لم يستحق بالعقد
He said: And the hire contract is dissolved due to excuses according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not dissolved except for a defect, because according to him benefits are like tangible assets, so the contract on them is valid and it resembles sale. And for us: Benefits are not possessed and they are the contracted subject matter. So an excuse in hire is like a defect before delivery in sale, so it dissolves it, as the meaning combines them, which is the inability of the contracting party to proceed with the contract except by bearing extra harm that was not owed. This is the meaning of excuse according to us. And it is like a person who hires a surgeon to extract his tooth due to pain, then the pain subsides; or hires a cook to cook his wedding feast, then his wife divorces him (by khul'), the hire dissolves because proceeding would impose extra harm not owed by the contract.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that ijara can be dissolved upon the occurrence of a valid excuse ('udhr), whereas Imam al-Shafi'i restricts dissolution to defects only. Shafi'i's view is based on considering benefits as tangible assets, making the contract binding like a sale. The Hanafi argument, however, states that benefits are not in the possession of the lessee at the start; they are the subject matter of the contract. Therefore, an excuse that makes performance harmful is analogous to a defect in the goods before delivery in a sale contract, which allows the buyer to rescind. The common cause ('illa) is the inability to proceed without incurring extra harm not owed. The text gives two examples: hiring a dentist to extract a painful tooth, then the pain stops; and hiring a cook for a wedding feast, then the wife divorces the host by khul' so the feast is cancelled. In both cases, proceeding with the contract would cause unnecessary harm, so the contract is dissolved. The Urdu commentary elaborates that excuses recognized by Hanafis include loss of purpose, illness, etc., and this is a key difference from Shafi'i school.

Key Terms
الاعذار (al-a‘dhār): Excuses or valid reasons that make it harmful or impossible to continue the contract.
العذر (al-‘udhr): An excuse that prevents the contracting party from proceeding without extra harm, as exemplified in the text.
المنافع (al-manāfi‘): Benefits or usufructs that are the subject matter of ijara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which example does the text give for a valid excuse that dissolves ijara?
A) A rented house collapses.
B) The hired cook's fee increases.
C) Hiring a dentist to pull a tooth but the pain stops.
D) The lessor decides to sell the property.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an ijara contract dissolves when a valid excuse makes continued performance harmful, unlike Shafi'i which restricts dissolution to defects.

Death Does Not Rescind Ijarah
Ruling on effect of death on ijarah contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that death does not rescind an ijarah contract and explain the rational proof.

Core Idea
Death does not nullify ijarah; the contract continues with the heirs.

In Hanafi fiqh, the ijarah (rental) contract is binding and remains unaffected by the death of either party. This lesson explains the ruling and the rational proof behind it, contrasting with a minority view that considers benefits akin to physical assets.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the Hanafi position: death does not rescind the ijarah contract.
The contract remains valid and binding.
2
Understand the rational proof
Analyze why death does not rescind: the benefit (manfa'ah) is not owned until consumed, and no necessity arises from death to cancel.
The lessee's estate or heirs continue the contract.
3
Compare with opposing view
Note that three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) and others hold ijarah is never rescinded because benefits are like physical properties.
Both sides agree on continuity, but reasoning differs.
4
Apply to case
Consider scenarios: lessor dies or lessee dies. What happens to the contract?
Heirs step into the deceased's role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارات
موت سے اجارہ فسخ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں ملک غیر سے مشتقع ہونا یا اجرت ادا کرنا لازم نہیں آتا ۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ، ابن سیرین، ایاس بن معاویہ ، عثمان بنی اور ابو ثور کے نزدیک اجارہ کسی حال میں فتح نہ ہوگا بلکہ وارث قائم مقام ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں منافع اعیان کے مانند ہیں اور اجارہ عقد لازم ہے۔ فلا تنسفح بالموت
Book of Rentals. The rental contract will not be rescinded by death. Because in this case, ownership of the benefit from another or payment of hire does not become necessary. According to the three Imams, Ibn Sirin, Iyas ibn Mu'awiya, 'Uthmani, and Abu Thawr, the rental is never rescinded in any case; rather the heir stands in place. Because according to them, benefits are like physical properties, and the rental is a binding contract. So it is not rescinded by death.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the effect of death. The Hanafi position: death does not rescind ijarah because the benefit (manfa'ah) is not owned until it is consumed, and the contract is binding (lazim). The lessee's estate or heirs continue the contract. The opposing view (three Imams, etc.) holds that ijarah is never rescinded even by death because benefits are like physical assets (a'yan), so the contract remains fully binding. The Hanafi reasoning is that the benefit is not in the possession of either party at the time of death, so the contract is not automatically void.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract for hiring the benefit (manfa'ah) of a person or property in exchange for a known wage (ujrah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The contract is immediately rescinded.
B) The contract continues, and the lessor's heirs take his place.
C) The lessee may choose to rescind.
D) The contract becomes void retroactively.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, death of a party does not rescind an ijarah contract; the heirs succeed to the rights and obligations.

Khiyar al-Shart in Ijarah: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on khiyar al-shart in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on khiyar al-shart in ijarah, contrast it with the Shafi'i view, and evaluate the key arguments including analogy to sale and the defect option.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is valid in ijarah because it is a commutative contract like sale, and partial consumption does not prevent return.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: can a lessor or lessee stipulate an option to cancel a rental contract within a specified period? The Hanafi school answers yes, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. The disagreement hinges on the nature of ijarah as a commutative contract and the possibility of restitution after the subject matter (benefit) has been partially consumed. Let us walk through the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Determine what the dispute is about: the validity of stipulating an option (khiyar al-shart) in an ijarah contract. Hanafis say it is valid; Shafi'is say it is invalid.
The option allows either party to rescind within a fixed period.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the subject matter (manfa'ah) is consumed over time; if the option is exercised after some use, the benefits already used cannot be returned, making full restitution impossible. This prevents the establishment of the option.
The key is restitution (i'ada) of the entire subject matter.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis counter that ijarah is a commutative contract ('aqd mu'awadah) similar to sale (bay') and not like marriage. They use analogy (qiyas) to sale, where option is allowed, citing the common cause ('illah) of need to deliberate and avoid loss. They further analogize to the defect option (khiyar al-'ayb), which is universally allowed in ijarah despite partial consumption.
Partial consumption does not preclude return; compensation can be adjusted.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Practically, Hanafis allow inclusion of an option clause in rental contracts; Shafi'is do not. This affects how contracts are drafted in different madhhabs.
Know your madhhab when writing contracts.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school. The argument from analogy to sale and defect option is considered strong.
No need to accept it if you follow another school, but understand the reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و يصح شرط الخيار
(۳۰) ہمارے یہاں اجارہ میں خیار شرط کرنا صحیح ہے۔ پس اگر موجد یا مستاجر کے لئے خیار شرط ہو تو وہ اس کی وجہ سے اجارہ کو فسخ کر سکتے ہیں امام شافعی کے یہاں عقد اجارہ میں خیار کا ہونا درست ہی نہیں اس لئے کہ مستاجر کو پورا معقود علیہ واپس کرنا ناممکن ہے۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ فوت ہو چکا۔ یعنی اگر خیار ثابت ہو تو مدت خیار کے اندر جو منافع فوت ہو گئے ان کا واپس کرنا ممکن نہیں حالانکہ خیار کی وجہ سے کل واپس کرنا چاہیے اور اگر خیار موجر کے لئے ہوتو وہ بھی پورا معقود علیہ سپر نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ مدت خیار میں کچھ منافع گذر چکے تو گویا قبل از تسلیم بائع کے پاس کچھ مبیع تلف ہو گئی۔ اور ان میں سے ہر ایک ثبوت خیار سے مانع ہے۔
قوله ولنا انه عقد ..... الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجارہ ایک عقد معاوضہ ہے ( نکاح کے مانند نہیں ہے ) جس کے لئے مجلس قبضہ کا ہونا ضروری نہیں (پس یہ صرف وسلم کی طرح بھی نہیں ہے ) توسیع کی طرح اس میں بھی خیار شرط صحیح ہوگا اور بیع و اجارہ میں وجہ جامع دفع ضرورت ہے کہ دو تین روز غور کر لے تا کہ خسارہ نہ ہو۔ اور اجارہ میں اگر کچھ معقود علیہ فوت ہو جائے تو بالا تفاق خیار عیب کی وجہ سے واپس کر سکتا ہے تو ایسے ہی خیار شرط کی وجہ سے بھی واپس کر سکے گا بخلاف بیع کے کہ بیچ اور اجارہ میں فرق ہے اور وہ یہ کہ بیچ میں کل واپس کرنا ممکن ہے اجارہ میں ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بیع میں کل کی واپسی شرط کی گئی نہ کہ اجارہ ہیں ۔
He said: And the stipulation of option is valid. (30) According to us, stipulating an option in ijarah is valid. So if the lessor or lessee stipulates an option, they can rescind the ijarah due to it. According to Imam Shafi'i, having an option in an ijarah contract is not valid at all, because it is impossible for the lessee to return the entire subject matter. Since the subject matter has been consumed. That is, if the option is established, it is not possible to return the benefits that have passed during the option period, whereas the entire subject matter must be returned due to the option. And if the option is for the lessor, he also cannot deliver the entire subject matter because some benefits have passed during the option period, as if some of the sold property was destroyed before delivery. Each of these prevents the establishment of the option. He said: And for us, it is a contract of exchange... Our evidence is that ijarah is a contract of exchange (not like marriage) for which a session of possession is not necessary (so it is also not like a forward sale). By analogy to sale, the stipulation of an option is valid, and the common cause in sale and ijarah is the need to avoid harm, so that one may deliberate for a few days to avoid loss. And in ijarah, if some of the subject matter is lost, it can be returned due to a defect option by consensus; similarly, it can be returned due to a stipulation option. Unlike sale, where there is a difference: in sale, total return is possible; in ijarah, it is not possible. Therefore, total return is stipulated in sale, not in ijarah.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school allows khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) in ijarah contracts, meaning either party can stipulate a period within which they can cancel the contract. Imam Shafi'i rejects this because the subject matter (manfa'ah – benefit) is consumed over time, so if the option is exercised, the benefits already enjoyed cannot be returned. The Hanafi response: ijarah is a commutative contract (like sale but unlike marriage) and does not require a session of delivery; therefore, it is analogous to sale where option is allowed. Furthermore, the parties may need a few days to consider to avoid loss. Also, the defect option (khiyar al-'ayb) is universally allowed in ijarah despite partial consumption, so similarly, stipulation option should be allowed. The difference from sale is that in sale, the entire object (mabi') can be returned; in ijarah, partial consumption does not prevent return because the compensation (ujrah) can be adjusted.

Key Terms
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by either party to rescind or confirm the contract within a specified period.
عقد معاوضہ ('aqd mu'awadah): A commutative contract where each party gives and receives something of value.
خیار عیب (khiyar al-'ayb): An option to return defective goods or benefits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi justification for allowing khiyar al-shart in ijarah?
A) Ijarah is like marriage, which allows options.
B) Ijarah is a commutative contract analogous to sale, and the need to avoid harm justifies the option.
C) The Quran explicitly permits options in ijarah.
D) Ijarah is a non-binding contract, so any condition is acceptable.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is valid in Hanafi ijarah because the contract is commutative and partial consumption does not prevent return; the defect option provides a precedent.

Rescission of Ijarah Due to Excuses: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi vs Shafi'i on rescinding ijarah due to excuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on rescinding ijarah due to excuses, explain the Hanafi proof based on qiyas, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
An excuse causing extra harm in ijarah equals a defect before sale possession—rescission valid.

The Hanafi school permits rescission of an ijarah contract when an unforeseen excuse makes continuation harmful beyond the contract's intent. The Shafi'i school disagrees, allowing rescission only for defects. This lesson unpacks the debate and the Hanafi qiyas (analogy) that grounds their position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The text begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: ijarah is rescinded due to excuses ('udhr).
The term 'udhr here means a circumstance that makes continuation unreasonably harmful.
2
Identify the opposing view
Al-Shafi'i and others (three Imams, Abu Thawr) restrict rescission to defects only, likening ijarah to sale.
3
Examine the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that benefits are like physical properties (a'yan), so ijarah is analogous to sale; only defects permit rescission.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis counter that benefits are not possessed at contract formation (ghayr maqbuda); they are the subject matter. Thus an excuse is like a defect before possession in sale—both involve inability to proceed without extra harm.
The common illa (cause) is 'ajz al-'aqid 'an al-madi illa bi tahammul darar za'id'.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis allow rescission for excuses (e.g., pain subsides, wedding cancelled), while Shafi'is do not.
The commentator also mentions Ibn al-'Izz's objection that qiyas is used without direct text, but affirms qiyas as valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و تفسخ الاجارة بالاعذار عندنا وقال الشافعى لا تفسخ الا بالعيب لان المنافع عنده بمنزلة الاعيان حتى يجوز العقد عليها فاشبه البيع ولنا ان المنافع غير مقبوضة وهى المعقودة عليها فصار العذر في الاجارة كالعيب قبل القبض في البيع فتفسخ به اذ المعنى يجمعهما وهو عجز العاقد عن المضى في موجبه الا بتحمل ضرر زائد لم يستحق به وهذا هو معنى العذر عندنا وهو كمن استاجر حدادا ليقلع ضرسه لوجع به فسكن الوجع أو استاجر طباخا ليطبخ له طعام الوليمة فاختلعت منه تفسخ الاجارة لان في المضى عليه الزام ضرر زائد لم يستحق بالعقد
ترجمہ اور فتح کر دیا جائے گا اجارہ عذروں کی وجہ سے ہمارے نزدیک۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ فسخ نہیں کیا جائے گا مگر عیب کی وجہ سے کیونکہ منافع ان کے نزدیک بمنزلہ اعیان ہیں یہاں تک کہ ان پر عقد جائز ہے تو وہ بیع کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع مقبوض نہیں ہیں اور وہی معقود علیہ ہیں ۔ پس اجارہ میں عذر ایسا ہو گیا جیسے بیچ میں قبضہ سے پہلے عیب ہوتو بوجہ عذر رفح کرسکتا ہے کیونکہ سبب دونوں کو جامع ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک عذر کے یہی معنی ہیں اور اس کی مثال یہ ہے کہ کسی نے جراح کو مزدوری پر لیا کہ اس کی دور دوالی ڈاڑھ اکھاڑ دے پھر درد تھم گیا یا باورچی کو ولیمہ کا کھانا پکانے کے لئے اجارہ پر لیا پھر عورت نے خلع لے لیا تو اجارہ صبح ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ

ہمارے نزدیک اجارہ عذر کی وجہ سے بھی مسخ کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ اور ابو ثور کے نزدیک صرف عیب کی وجہ سے فسخ کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ ان کے یہاں منافع بمنزلہ اعیان ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ ان کے نزدیک منافع پر عقد واقع ہوسکتا ہے تو وہ بیع کے مشابہ ہو گیا کہ جیسے مبیع کو عیب کے بغیر واپس نہیں کر سکتا اس طرح منفعت کو بھی بلا عیب واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ قاضی شریح اور ابن ابی لیلی کے نزدیک تو ۔ بلا عذر بھی فتح کر سکتے ہیں کیونکہ ان کے یہاں اجارہ لازمی عقد نہیں ہے۔
قوله ولنا ان المنافع .. الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع بھی مقبوض نہیں حالانکہ یہی معقود علیہ ہیں تو اجارہ میں عذر ایسا ہو گیا جیسے بیچ میں قبضہ سے پہلے عیب ہو تو عذر کی وجہ سے فسخ کر سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ جو از نسخ کا جو سبب ہے وہ بیچ اور اجارہ دونوں میں موجود ہے اور وہ سب یہ ہے کہ عاقد موجب عقد کے موافق برتاؤ نہیں کر سکتا مگر ایسا مزید ضر راٹھا کر جس کا استحقاق بذریعہ عقد نہیں ہوا۔ اور ہمارے یہاں عذر کے یہی معنی ہیں کہ عاقد اگر اجارہ کو باقی رکھے تو اس کا ایسا نقصان لازم آئے جو اس پر عقدا جارہ سے لازم نہیں ہوتا۔
تنبیہ شیخ ابن العز نے اس مقام پر یہ اعتراض کیا ہے کہ اعذار اور موت متعاقدین سے اجارہ کا مسخ ہونا ایک ایسی بات ہے جس پر نہ کوئی نص موجود ہے نہ قول صحابی نہ اجماع بلکہ صرف عیب کی وجہ سے فتح بیچ پر قیاس ہے مگر موصوف کا یہ اعتراض نہایت ہی بودا ہے اس لئے کہ شرعی ادلہ اربعہ میں سے قیاس ایک مستقل دلیل ہے جس کا تحقق حکم شرعی کے اثبات کے لئے کافی ہے جو مانحن فیہ میں موجود ہے۔
قوله وهو كمن استاجر .... الخ - یہاں سے موجب فسخ اعذار کی چند صورتیں ذکر کر رہے ہیں ۔ 1 ایک شخص نے دردناک ڈاڑھا کھیڑنے کے لئے کسی اجارہ کو اجرت پر لیا پھر ڈاڑھ اکھیڑنے سے پہلے درد جاتارہا تو اجارہ فتح ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اجارہ باقی رکھنے میں صحیح سالم ڈاڑھ کو اکھاڑنا پڑتا ہے جو مستاجر پر عقد اجارہ کی وجہ سے لازم نہیں تھا۔ (۲) کسی نے ایک باورچی کو ولیمہ کا کھانا پکانے کے لئے اجارہ پر لیا پھر عورت نے خلع لے لیا وہ مرگئی تو اجارہ مسخ ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اگر جارہ فسخ نہ ہو بلکہ پورا کرنا لازم ہو تو مستاجر کے ذمہ مزید ضر ر لازم آئے گا جس کا استحقاق بذریعہ عقد اجارہ نہیں ہوا تھا۔
He said: And the rental contract is rescinded due to excuses in our view. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not rescinded except due to a defect, because according to him benefits are like physical properties such that the contract on them is valid, so it resembles sale. And for us, benefits are not possessed, and they are the subject matter. So an excuse in ijarah is like a defect before possession in sale, so it is rescinded due to it, because the meaning combines both: the inability of the contracting party to proceed with the obligation without bearing extra harm not deserved. And this is the meaning of excuse according to us. For example, if someone hires a blacksmith to extract a tooth due to pain, then the pain subsides, or hires a cook to cook food for a wedding feast, then the wife divorces (khul'), the rental is rescinded because proceeding would impose extra harm not deserved by the contract.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute on rescinding ijarah due to excuses (a'dhar). Hanafis allow it when continuing the contract would cause extra harm not anticipated at the time of contract. The common illah is the party's inability to proceed without bearing unnecessary hardship. Examples: hiring a dentist to pull a painful tooth but the pain stops; hiring a cook for a wedding but the marriage ends. In both, the purpose is frustrated, and continuing would impose extra burden. Shafi'is and others (the three Imams, Abu Thawr) restrict rescission to defects only, analogizing ijarah to sale. Qadi Shuraih and Ibn Abi Layla even allow rescission without excuse, considering ijarah non-binding. The commentator dismisses Ibn al-'Izz's objection that this ruling lacks direct textual evidence, affirming qiyas as a valid proof. The Hanafi view is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
عذر ('udhr): An excuse or circumstance that makes continuation of the ijarah unreasonably harmful to one party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a valid excuse ('udhr) to rescind an ijarah?
A) The lessee finds a cheaper alternative.
B) The purpose of the hire ceases to exist (e.g., pain subsides before tooth extraction).
C) The lessor wants to use the property himself.
D) The market price of the service drops.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ijarah can be rescinded for excuses that cause extra harm beyond the contract's intent, based on qiyas with defect before possession in sale.

Rescission of Ijarah Due to Lessor's Insolvency
Ruling on rescission of ijarah by qadi due to lessor's insolvency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a qadi rescinds an ijarah contract and sells the leased property for debt repayment.

Core Idea
When a lessor's debts cannot be paid except by selling the leased asset, the qadi rescinds the ijarah to satisfy creditors.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical juncture between contract law and debt enforcement. It clarifies that the qadi has authority to dissolve an ijarah contract when the lessor becomes insolvent and the leased property is the only means to repay debts. This ruling balances the rights of the lessee with the claims of creditors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the contractual context
Understand that the scenario involves a lessor (who rented out property) who later becomes insolvent. The lessee is already in possession under a valid ijarah contract.
2
Identify the triggering condition
The lessor's debts must be such that they cannot be paid except by selling the specific property that is subject to the ijarah contract.
The lessor must have no other assets to cover the debts.
3
Identify the qadi's action
Upon the lessor's insolvency, the qadi rescinds the ijarah contract and sells the property to satisfy the debts. The rescission is a judicial act, not automatic.
The qadi acts as a protector of creditors' rights.
4
Understand the rationale
The ruling prevents harm to creditors by enabling debt recovery, while the lessee's rights are overridden due to the lessor's inability to perform. The rescission is necessary to unlock the property's value.
This is based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Source Text

دکان بازار میں کرایہ پر لی تا کہ تجارت کرے گا مال ضائع ہو گیا یا اسی طرح دکان یا مکان کرایہ پر لیا پھر مفلس ہو گیا اور اس کو دین لازم ہو گئے ان دیون کو اسی کرایہ کے مکان : کے شمن سے ادا کیا جا سکتا ہے قاضی عقد اجارہ کو فسخ کرے اور اسکو دین کے بدلے بیچ دے
وكذا من استاجر دكانا في السوق ليتجر فيه فذهب ماله وكذا اذا آجر دكانا او دارا ثم افلس ولزمته ديون لا يقدر على قضائها الا بثمن ما آجر فسخ القاضى العقد وباعها في الدين لان فى الجرى على موجب العقد
He hired a shop in the market to trade in it, then his wealth was lost; similarly, if he rented out a shop or house, then became insolvent and debts became binding upon him, and he cannot pay them except with the price of what he rented, then the qadi rescinds the contract and sells it for the debt, because proceeding with the contract...
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This is a ruling on a specific scenario: if a person rents a shop for business but then loses his capital, or if a lessor becomes insolvent and has debts that can only be paid by selling the rented property, the qadi (judge) may rescind the ijarah contract and sell the property to satisfy the debts. The reason is that continuing the contract would prevent the creditor from recovering the debt, and the qadi has authority to dissolve contracts to fulfill debt obligations. This is based on the principle of preventing harm and ensuring justice. The passage is incomplete but indicates the legal mechanism.

Key Terms
افلاس (iflas): Insolvency; inability to pay debts due to lack of assets.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission; annulment of a contract by judicial decree.

A) When the lessee fails to pay rent.
B) When the lessor becomes insolvent and can only pay debts by selling the leased property.
C) When the property is damaged.
D) When the lessee wishes to exit the contract.

Key Takeaway
The qadi may rescind an ijarah contract and sell the leased property to satisfy the lessor's debts when no other assets are available.

Rescission of Ijarah for Excuse: Hanafi View vs. Other Schools
Inter-madhhab dispute on rescission of ijarah for an excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits rescission of an ijarah contract for an excuse and evaluate the opposing schools' position.

Core Idea
Ijarah can be rescinded for an excuse because benefits are not possessed, analogizing to a defect before possession in sale.

This passage addresses a key difference between the Hanafi school and the majority of other schools regarding when an ijarah (hire/lease) contract can be rescinded. While the three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) and Abu Thawr restrict rescission to defects in the subject matter, the Hanafis allow rescission for any genuine excuse that imposes an extra burden not contracted for. Understanding this dispute requires grasping the Hanafi view that benefits (manafi') are not physically possessed, which is the basis for their istihsan-based analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the schools and their positions
List all positions mentioned: Hanafi (excuse), three Imams+Abu Thawr (defect only), Qadi Shurayh and Ibn Abi Layla (no excuse needed).
Note that Qadi Shurayh's view is an extreme, deeming ijarah non-binding.
2
Trace the opposing proof
The three Imams argue that benefits are like corporeal things (manafi' bimanzilat al-a'yan). Therefore, ijarah is analogous to sale, allowing rescission only for defects.
This analogy treats benefits as goods that can be physically returned.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafis use istihsan: benefits are not possessed at the time of contract, so an excuse is like a defect before possession in a sale (which allows rescission). The common cause (illah) is the inability to proceed without suffering an additional harm not contracted for.
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) because it focuses on the lack of possession.
4
Identify the cause (illah)
Both sale and ijarah share the illah: the contracting party cannot act according to the contract without enduring extra harm not owed by the contract.
This illah is derived from the Hanafi definition of udhr.
5
Apply the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis allow rescission for excuses like inability to use the benefit, while the three Imams require a defect like damage to the asset.
Always ask: what concrete difference does this dispute make in a real case?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارات
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
اجارہ پورا کرنے میں ایک زائد ضرر لازم کرنا ہے جس کا استحقاق بذریعہ عقد نہیں ہوا تھا۔ تشريح .. قوله وتفسخ الاجارة.
۱) ہمارے نزدیک اجارہ عذر کی وجہ سے بھی مسخ کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ اور ابو ثور کے نزدیک صرف عیب کی وجہ سے فسخ کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ ان کے یہاں منافع بمنزلہ اعیان ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ ان کے نزدیک منافع پر عقد واقع ہوسکتا ہے تو وہ بیع کے مشابہ ہو گیا کہ جیسے مبیع کو عیب کے بغیر واپس نہیں کر سکتا اس طرح منفعت کو بھی بلا عیب واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ قاضی شریح اور ابن ابی لیلی کے نزدیک تو ۔ بلا عذر بھی فتح کر سکتے ہیں کیونکہ ان کے یہاں اجارہ لازمی عقد نہیں ہے۔

تنبیہ شیخ ابن العز نے اس مقام پر یہ اعتراض کیا ہے کہ اعذار اور موت متعاقدین سے اجارہ کا مسخ ہونا ایک ایسی بات ہے جس پر نہ کوئی نص موجود ہے نہ قول صحابی نہ اجماع بلکہ صرف عیب کی وجہ سے فتح بیچ پر قیاس ہے مگر موصوف کا یہ اعتراض نہایت ہی بودا ہے اس لئے کہ شرعی ادلہ اربعہ میں سے قیاس ایک مستقل دلیل ہے جس کا تحقق حکم شرعی کے اثبات کے لئے کافی ہے جو مانحن فیہ میں موجود ہے۔
Book of Ijarah. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 12. Compelling an additional harm in completing the ijarah which was not entitled by the contract. Explanation: His saying: 'And the ijarah is rescinded.' 1) According to us, the ijarah can be rescinded due to an excuse as well. According to the three Imams and Abu Thawr, rescission is only permissible due to a defect because according to them, benefits are like corporeal things. Thus, a contract on benefits can be concluded, so it resembles a sale: just as sold goods cannot be returned without a defect, likewise benefits cannot be returned without a defect. According to Qadi Shurayh and Ibn Abi Layla, they can rescind even without an excuse because according to them, ijarah is not a binding contract. His saying: 'And for us, the benefits...' - Our proof is that benefits are not possessed, even though they are the subject matter. So an excuse in ijarah is like a defect before possession in a sale, allowing rescission due to excuse. The cause of rescission exists in both sale and ijarah: the contracting party cannot act in accordance with the contract without suffering an additional harm that was not entitled by the contract. And our definition of an excuse is that if the contracting party maintains the ijarah, a loss would be necessitated for him that does not arise from the contract itself. Note: Shaykh Ibn al-'Izz objected at this point that the rescission of ijarah due to excuses and death of the contracting parties is not supported by any text, nor by the saying of a companion, nor by consensus, but only by analogy to rescinding a sale due to a defect. But this objection is very weak because analogy is an independent proof among the four sources of Islamic law, sufficient to establish a legal ruling, which is present in our case.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on the grounds for rescinding an ijarah (hire) contract. The Hanafi school holds that ijarah can be rescinded due to any genuine excuse (udhr) that imposes an additional harm on the contracting party beyond what was agreed upon. The three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) and Abu Thawr restrict rescission only to defects in the subject matter, analogizing benefits to physical goods. Qadi Shurayh and Ibn Abi Layla go even further, allowing rescission without any excuse because they consider ijarah non-binding. The Hanafi proof is based on istihsan: since benefits (manafi') are not physically possessed at the time of contract, an excuse creates a situation analogous to a defect discovered before possession in a sale – both allow rescission to prevent uncompensated harm. The passage defends the use of qiyas (analogy) against an objection that no explicit text exists, affirming that qiyas is a valid independent source of law.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of hiring or leasing for a specified benefit in exchange for known wages/rent.
عذر (udhr): An excuse or circumstance that makes continuation of the contract harmful to one party beyond what was agreed.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract, returning both parties to pre-contract status.
منافع (manafi'): Benefits or usufructs, the subject matter of ijarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi proof for allowing rescission of ijarah due to an excuse?
A) Benefits are like physical goods.
B) Hadith of the Prophet.
C) Benefits are not possessed, analogous to defect before possession in sale.
D) Consensus of all schools.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows rescission of ijarah for any excuse causing extra burden, based on the non-possessed nature of benefits analogized to a pre-possession defect in sale.

Ijarah Rescission for Excuses: The Qadi's Role (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on qadi's role in ijarah rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on rescission of ijarah for excuses and apply the reconciled rule distinguishing apparent from non-apparent excuses.

Core Idea
For ijarah rescission, an apparent excuse needs no qadi; a non-apparent excuse requires qadi verification.

When an unforeseen excuse makes fulfilling an ijarah contract harmful, may the affected party rescind unilaterally or must a qadi intervene? This passage presents four concrete examples—from dental extraction to insolvency—and then reveals an intra-Hanafi disagreement rooted in different texts within the school. Understanding how the later scholars reconciled these sources is essential for applying the ruling today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four examples of excuses
List the four scenarios: (1) toothache gone before extraction, (2) wife divorces/dies before walima, (3) hirer loses capital for trade, (4) lessor becomes insolvent. Note the common element: continuing would impose extra harm not contracted for.
Each example illustrates a different type of excuse—some objective, some subjective.
2
State the two Hanafi opinions on rescission
Opinion A (al-Ziyadat, al-Quduri): rescission requires a qadi's ruling because the matter is ijtihadi. Opinion B (al-Jami' al-Saghir): no qadi needed; the party rescinds alone, analogized to a defect before possession in a sale.
Both opinions are based on Zahir al-Riwayah texts; the ikhtilaf is internal to the school.
3
Understand the reconciliation
Some later scholars reconciled: if the excuse is apparent (e.g., loss of capital, toothache gone), no qadi needed; if non-apparent (e.g., hidden debt), qadi must verify and rescind.
The key is the evidentiary difficulty: non-apparent excuses require verification to prevent fraud.
4
Apply the reconciled view to the examples
Classify each example as apparent or non-apparent. Loss of capital and toothache are apparent; hidden debt is non-apparent. The walima case depends on whether the khul'/death is publicly known.
This classification is case-specific and may require qadi's judgment if borderline.
5
Contrast with the position of the Three Imams
The Three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) do not allow rescission of ijarah for excuses at all. This underscores why the Hanafi ikhtilaf required a qadi – to settle a contestable claim.
This external disagreement reinforces the justification for qadi intervention in disputed cases.

Source Text
